Prohibition of Tawaf for Menstruating Woman: Hanafi Ruling on Validity and Penalty
Presents prohibition of tawaf during haid/nifas with hadith proof and penalty for violation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tawaf during menstruation/postpartum, identify the proof from the hadith of 'A'ishah, and explain the penalty required when tawaf al-ifadah is performed in a state of major impurity.

Core Idea
Tawaf during haid is haram but valid; purity is a condition of perfection, not validity.

Menstruation and postpartum bleeding (nifas) impose restrictions on many acts of worship, including tawaf. The Hanafi school distinguishes between conditions for validity and conditions for perfection, leading to a unique ruling: the tawaf is valid even without purity, but the sin of performing it in that state must be expiated by a sacrifice. This lesson examines the textual proof and the penalty.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its prohibition
The passage clearly states that tawaf during menstruation or postpartum is prohibited (haram). Note that prohibition does not mean invalidity.
2
Locate the dalil
Two hadiths are cited: the command to 'A'ishah (ra) to do all Hajj acts except tawaf until pure, and the hadith equating tawaf to prayer. The first provides an explicit prohibition; the second is contextualized to show that purity is not a condition of validity.
3
Analyze the Hanafi inference
The prohibition is due to the honor of the Ka'bah, not because tawaf inherently requires purity. If purity were a condition for validity, the tawaf would be invalid; but Allah knows that women may be excused, so the act is valid albeit sinful.
Contrast with Shafi'i view: purity is a condition for validity.
4
Determine the consequence
Despite the prohibition, the tawaf is valid (sahih) and releases the pilgrim from ihram. However, a penalty (dam) is required to compensate for the sin.
5
Distinguish the penalty amount
For tawaf al-ifadah (the obligatory tawaf of Hajj) performed in major impurity, the penalty is a badana (camel). For minor impurity (hadath), the penalty is a sheep, unless the tawaf is repeated in purity before slaughtering the sacrificial animal.
The text also implies that for optional tawaf, the penalty may differ, but that is not covered here.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و) يحرم بالحيض والنفاس (الطَّواف بالكعبة، لقول النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم لعائشة حاضت: «فَافْعَلِي مَا يَفْعَلُ الْحَاجُ غَيْرَ أنْ لا تَطُوفِي بِالْبَيْتِ حَتَّى تَطْهُرِي ) متفق عليه. ولقوله : ( الطَّوَافُ حَوْلَ الْبَيْتِ مِثْلُ الصَّلاةِ، إلا أنَّكُمْ تَتَكَلَّمُونَ فِيهِ، فَمَنْ تَكَلَّمَ فَلا يَتَكَلَّمَنَّ إِلا بِخَيْرِ » . والمنع لشرف البيت لا لعارضية المسجد، والطهارة شرط كمال للطواف لا لصحته، فيصح مع الجنابة والحيض والنفاس، وتحل به من الإحرام وعليها بدنة في الفرض، وهو طواف الإفاضة. وعلى المحدث شاة ما لم يعده طاهراً قبل ذبح الهدي كغيره.
(And) it is prohibited during menstruation and postpartum (to perform tawaf around the Ka'bah), due to the saying of the Prophet ﷺ to 'A'ishah when she menstruated: 'Do what the pilgrim does except do not perform tawaf of the House until you become pure' (agreed upon). And due to his saying: 'Tawaf around the House is like prayer, except that you speak in it; so whoever speaks, let him only speak good.' And the prohibition is due to the honor of the House, not because of the incidental ruling of the mosque. And purity is a condition of perfection for tawaf, not for its validity, so it is valid with janabah, menstruation, and postpartum. And she is released from ihram by it, and upon her is a camel (badana) in the obligatory (tawaf), which is tawaf al-ifadah. And upon the one with hadath (minor impurity) is a sheep if he does not repeat it while pure before slaughtering the sacrificial animal, like others.
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage covers the ruling on tawaf during menstruation and postpartum. The first proof is the hadith of 'A'ishah: she was told to do all acts of Hajj except tawaf until she is pure. The second proof is the hadith equating tawaf to prayer, which implies the need for purity but the text then clarifies that purity is a condition of perfection (shart kamal), not validity. Therefore, if a menstruating woman performs tawaf, it is valid but she must offer a penalty: a camel (badana) for the obligatory tawaf (tawaf al-ifadah) during Hajj, and a sheep for the one with minor hadath if he does not repeat it in a state of purity before slaughtering the sacrificial animal. This shows that the prohibition is serious (haram) but the act is not void.

Key Terms
طواف (tawaf): Circumambulation of the Ka'bah seven times, a ritual of Hajj and Umrah.
بدنة (badana): A camel or large animal sacrificed as penalty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a woman in menstruation performs tawaf al-ifadah during Hajj, what is required according to the text?
A) She must repeat the tawaf after purification
B) The tawaf is invalid and she must repeat Hajj
C) She must offer a camel (badana) as penalty
D) She must offer a sheep

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, tawaf performed during menstruation is valid but carries a penalty, distinguishing between conditions of perfection and validity.

Definition and Obligation of Hajj
Definition and obligation statement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of Hajj and explain why it is fard immediately upon capacity.

Core Idea
Hajj is fard immediately upon ability; delaying it is sinful in the Hanafi school.

The Book of Hajj opens with a precise legal definition and then establishes its obligation. This lesson unpacks the definition and the key legal ruling that Hajj is fard once in a lifetime, to be performed without delay according to the most sound view. Understanding this foundation is critical for the conditions and pillars that follow.

Guided Path
1
Understand the definition
Identify the specific places (Makkah, ‘Arafat, etc.) and specific actions (ihram, standing, tawaf, etc.) that constitute Hajj, as well as its fixed months (Shawwal, Dhu al-Qa‘dah, first ten of Dhu al-Hijjah).
The definition excludes ‘Umrah, which has different times.
2
Recognize the legal ruling
Note that Hajj is fard ‘ayn once in a lifetime. The text uses the term 'فَرْضٌ' indicating obligation.
3
Note the temporal aspect
The phrase 'عَلَى الفور في الأصح' means it must be performed immediately upon acquiring ability, not delayed. This is the muftā bihi position.
There is an ikhtilāf on whether one may delay, but the relied-upon view is immediate.
4
Identify the ikhtilāf on the year of obligation
The footnote mentions disagreements on which year Hajj was made obligatory (5, 6, 9, 10 AH). The famous view is 6 AH.
This ikhtilāf does not affect the ruling today.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحج: هو زيارة بِقَاعِ مَخصُوصَةٍ بِفِعْلٍ مَخْصُوص فِي أشهره – وهي: شوال، وذو القعدة، وعشر ذي الحجة - . فَرْضٌ مَرَّةً عَلَى الفور في الأصح. وشروط فرضيته ثمانية على الأصح: الإسلام والعقل والبلوغ والحرية والوقت والقدرة على الزاد ولو بمكة بنفقة وسط، والقدرة على راحلة مختصة به، أو على شق مَحْمِلِ بالمِلْكِ أو الإجارة، لا الإباحة والإعارة لغير أهل مكة ومن حولهم إذا أمكنهم المشي بالقدم والقوة بلا مشقة، وإلا فلا بد من الراحلة مطلقاً، وتلك القدرة فاضلة عن نفقته، ونفقة عياله إلى حين عوده ، وعمَّا لا بدَّ منه كالمنزل وأثاثه، وآلات المحترفين، وقضاء الدين. ويشترط العلم بفرضية الحج لمن أسلم بدار الحرب، أو الكون بدار الإسلام. وشرط وجوب الأداء خمسة على الأصح: صحة البدن، وزوال المانع الحسي ) عن الذهاب للحج، وأمن الطريق، وعدم قيام العدة، وخروج محرم ولو من رضاع أو مصاهرة مسلم مأمون عاقل بالغ أو زوج لامرأة في سفر. والعبرة بغلبة السلامة براً وبحراً على المفتى به. ويصح أداء فرض الحج بأربعة أشياء للحر: الإحرام والإسلام وهما شرطان، ثم الإتيان بركنيه وهما: الوقوف محرماً بعرفات لحظة: من زوال يوم التاسع إلى فجر يوم النحر بشرط عدم الجماع قبله محرماً). والركن الثاني: هو أكـثـر طـواف الإفاضة في وقته، وهو (): ما بعد طلوع فجر النحر وواجبات الحج إنشاء الإحرام من الميقات،
(۱) اختلف العلماء في السنة التي فرض فيها الحج، والمشهور أنها سنة ست وهو الصحيح، وقيل سنة خمس ، وقيل : سـ تسع. وصححه القاضي عياض ، وقيل : فرض قبل الهجرة وهو بعيد وأبعد منه قول بعضهم إنـه فــرض سنة عشر. أخرج البخاري عن زيد بن أرقم : ( أن النبي لحج بعد ما هاجر حجة واحدة وأخرج الدارقطني عـن جـابـر بـن الله قال حج رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ثلاث حجج حجتين قبل أن يهاجر وحجة قرن بها عمرة، وكانت حجتـه بعـد مـا هاجر سنة عشر. وحج أبو بكر الصديق في السنة التي قبلها سنة تسع وأما سنة ثمان وهي عام الفتح فحج بالناس قبلها عتاب بن أسيد اهـ وهو الذي لولاه النبي يا أميراً بمكة بعد الفتح. وذكر منلا علي أنه حج قبل أن يهاجر حججاً لا يعلم عددها. وقال ابن الأثير : كان يحج كل سنة قبل أن يهاجر، يعني إلا أن يمنع منه مانع. ط.
(۲) كالحبس والخوف.
(۳) من طلاق بائن أو رجعي أو وفاة؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿ لا تُخْرِجُوهُنَّ مِنْ بُيُوتِهِنَّ ﴾ [الطلاق:١] والحــــج يمكن أداؤه في وقت آخر. ط.
(٤) فإن فعل ذلك فسد حجه وعليه أن يمضي فيه كالصحيح وأن يقضي من قابل. ط.
(٥) أي: طواف الإفاضة.
The Book of Hajj: It is the visitation of specific places with specific actions in its months – which are Shawwal, Dhu al-Qa‘dah, and the first ten days of Dhu al-Hijjah. It is an obligation once in a lifetime, to be performed immediately according to the most sound view. The conditions for its obligation are eight according to the most sound view: Islam, sanity, puberty, freedom, time, ability to provide provisions even if in Mecca at moderate expense, and ability to provide a mount specifically for him or a share in a howdah, by ownership or lease, but not by permission or loan for those other than the people of Mecca and those around them if they can walk on foot with strength without hardship; otherwise, a mount is absolutely necessary. That ability must be in excess of his own expenses and the expenses of his dependents until his return, and for necessities like housing, furniture, professional tools, and debt repayment. Knowledge of the obligation of Hajj is required for one who becomes Muslim in dar al-harb, or for one residing in dar al-Islam. The conditions for obligatory performance are five according to the most sound view: soundness of body, removal of physical obstruction to travel for Hajj, safety of the route, absence of an ‘iddah period, and the presence of a mahram (even through fosterage or marriage) who is Muslim, trustworthy, sane, adult, or a husband for a woman in travel. Consideration is given to the predominance of safety by land and sea according to the fatwa. The performance of the obligatory Hajj is valid with four things for a free person: ihram and Islam (both are conditions), then performing its two pillars: standing at ‘Arafat in ihram for a moment from noon of the 9th to dawn of the Day of Sacrifice, provided there is no intercourse before that while in ihram. The second pillar is the majority of Tawaf al-Ifadah in its time, which is after the dawn of the Day of Sacrifice. The obligatory acts of Hajj include committing to ihram from the miqat.
(1) The scholars differed over the year in which Hajj was made obligatory; the famous view is it was the sixth year, and that is correct; some say the fifth year, some say the ninth. Qadi ‘Iyad preferred this. Some say it was made obligatory before hijra, which is far-fetched; even more far-fetched is the saying of some that it was made obligatory in the tenth year. Bukhari narrated from Zayd ibn Arqam that the Prophet (صلى الله عليه وسلم) performed only one Hajj after hijra. Darqutni narrated from Jabir ibn ‘Abd Allah that the Prophet performed three Hajj: two before hijra and one with ‘umrah, which was after hijra in the tenth year. Abu Bakr performed Hajj in the year before that, the ninth year. As for the eighth year, the year of conquest, ‘Attab ibn Asid led the people in Hajj. Mulla ‘Ali mentioned that he performed many Hajj before hijra, the number unknown. Ibn al-Athir said he performed Hajj every year before hijra unless prevented.
(2) Like imprisonment and fear.
(3) From irrevocable or revocable divorce or death; because of Allah’s saying: “Do not expel them from their houses” [65:1]. Hajj can be performed at another time.
(4) If he does so, his Hajj is invalid, and he must continue it as if valid and make it up the next year.
(5) That is, Tawaf al-Ifadah.
Source pages p. 688

Commentary
This passage opens the Book of Hajj with a definition: Hajj is the visitation of specific places (Makkah, ‘Arafat, etc.) with specific actions in its months (Shawwal, Dhu al-Qa‘dah, and first ten days of Dhu al-Hijjah). It is fard once in a lifetime, to be performed immediately (ala al-fawr) according to the most sound view. The conditions for it being fard are eight: Islam, sanity, puberty, freedom, the arrival of the Hajj season, ability to afford provisions and a mount (by ownership or lease, not loan), and the ability must be in excess of one’s own and dependents’ needs. Knowledge of its obligation is also a condition for new Muslims in dar al-harb. For performance, five conditions are required: physical health, absence of physical or security hindrances, safe route, no ‘iddah for women, and a mahram for women travel. Reliance on safety by predominant opinion is the basis for fatwa. The valid performance of Hajj requires ihram and Islam as conditions, then two pillars: standing at ‘Arafat (from noon of 9th to dawn of 10th) without having intercourse before ihram, and the majority of Tawaf al-Ifadah after dawn of the 10th. The obligatory acts include ihram from the miqat. Footnotes discuss the disagreement on the year Hajj was made obligatory, clarify ‘physical obstruction’ (imprisonment, fear), the prohibition of a woman in ‘iddah from traveling, the invalidation of Hajj by intercourse, and that Tawaf al-Ifadah is the second pillar.

Key Terms
الحج (al-ḥajj): Visitation of specific places (Makkah, ‘Arafat, etc.) with specific actions in its months.
الفرض (al-farḍ): An obligatory act that is established by definitive evidence.
على الفور (ʿalā al-fawr): Immediately, without delay.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on the timing of Hajj for one who has the ability?
A) It can be delayed without sin
B) It must be performed immediately (ala al-fawr)
C) It is recommended but not obligatory
D) It is only obligatory once every five years

Key Takeaway
Hajj is a one-time immediate fard upon a Muslim who meets the conditions of ability; delaying it without excuse is sinful in the Hanafi school.

Hajj — Pilgrimage

Hajj: Definition, Conditions, Pillars, Wajibat, and Sunan
Introduces the Book of Hajj with its definition, conditions, pillars, wajibat, and sunan.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of Hajj, identify its conditions of obligation and performance, and distinguish between its pillars, wajibat, and sunan.

Core Idea
Hajj is an immediate individual obligation once conditions are met, with two pillars and many wajibat; omission of a wajib requires sacrifice, while omission of a pillar invalidates it.

This lesson introduces the Book of Hajj in the Hanafi school. You will learn the definition of Hajj, when it becomes obligatory, what conditions must be met, and the structure of its performance through pillars, wajibat, and sunan. Understanding this framework is essential for any student of fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Define Hajj and its obligation level
Read the definition of Hajj and note that it is fard 'ayn once in a lifetime, immediately upon fulfillment of conditions (ala al-fawr).
The phrase 'ala al-asahh indicates the relied-upon opinion.
2
Distinguish conditions of obligation from conditions of performance
The passage lists eight shurut al-fardiyyah (conditions for the obligation itself) and five shurut wujub al-ada' (conditions for the act of performing it). Identify each set.
E.g., mahram is a condition of performance, not obligation.
3
Identify the two pillars (arkan)
Find which acts are designated as rukn. The passage states two: standing at Arafat and the majority of Tawaf al-Ifadah. Omitting either invalidates Hajj.
Note that ihram and Islam are conditions, not pillars.
4
List the wajibat and their function
The passage enumerates many wajibat (e.g., ihram from miqat, stoning, sacrifice for qarin/mutamatti). If a wajib is omitted, Hajj is still valid but requires a dam (sacrificial animal).
Distinguish wajib from rukn and sunnah.
5
Identify the sunan and prohibitions
The passage lists sunan (e.g., ghusl, two white garments) and prohibitions (e.g., wearing sewn garments, covering head for men). Sunnah omission is valid with no compensation; prohibitions may incur penalty.
Footnotes provide additional evidence for some rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحج
كتاب الحج: هو زيارة بِقَاعِ مَخصُوصَةٍ بِفِعْلٍ مَخْصُوص فِي أشهره – وهي: شوال، وذو القعدة، وعشر ذي الحجة - . فَرْضٌ مَرَّةً عَلَى الفور في الأصح. وشروط فرضيته ثمانية على الأصح: الإسلام والعقل والبلوغ والحرية والوقت والقدرة على الزاد ولو بمكة بنفقة وسط، والقدرة على راحلة مختصة به، أو على شق مَحْمِلِ بالمِلْكِ أو الإجارة، لا الإباحة والإعارة لغير أهل مكة ومن حولهـم إذا أمكنهم المشي بالقدم والقوة بلا مشقة، وإلا فلا بد من الراحلة مطلقاً، وتلك القدرة فاضلة عن نفقته، ونفقة عياله إلى حين عوده ، وعمَّا لا بدَّ منه كالمنزل وأثاثه، وآلات المحترفين، وقضاء الدين. ويشترط العلم بفرضية الحج لمن أسلم بدار الحرب، أو الكون بدار الإسلام. وشرط وجوب الأداء خمسة على الأصح: صحة البدن، وزوال المانع الحسي عن الذهاب للحج، وأمن الطريق، وعدم قيام العدة، وخروج محرم ولو من رضاع أو مصاهرة مسلم مأمون عاقل بالغ أو زوج لامرأة في سفر. والعبرة بغلبة السلامة براً وبحراً على المفتى به. ويصح أداء فرض الحج بأربعة أشياء للحر: الإحرام والإسلام وهما شرطان، ثم الإتيان بركنيه وهما: الوقوف محرماً بعرفات لحظة: من زوال يوم التاسع إلى فجر يوم النحر بشرط عدم الجماع قبله محرماً). والركن الثاني: هو أكثر طواف الإفاضة في وقته، وهو ما بعد طلوع فجر النحر. وواجبات الحج إنشاء الإحرام من الميقات، ومد الوقوف بعرفات إلى الغروب، والوقوف بالمزدلفة فيما بعد فجر يوم النحر وقبل طلوع الشمس، ورمي الجمار، وذبح القارن، والمُتَمَتِّعِ، والحلق، وتخصيصه بالحرم وأيام النحر، وتقديم الرمي على الحلق، ونحر القارن والمُتَمَتِّعِ بينهما، وإيقاع طواف الزيارة في أيام النحر، والسعي بين الصفا والمروة في أشهر الحج، وحصوله بعد طواف معتد به والمشي فيه لمن لا عذر له، وبداءة السعي من الصفا، وطواف الوداع، وبُدَاءة كل طواف بالبيت من الحجر الأسود، والتيامن فيه، والمشي فيه لمن لا عذر له، والطهارة من الحدثين، وستر العورة، وأقل الأشواط بعد فعل الأكثر من طواف الزيارة، وترك المحظورات كلبس الرجل المخيط، وستر رأسه ووجهه، وستر المرأة وجهها، والرفث والفسوق، والجدال، وقتل الصيد والإشارة إليه والدلالة عليه. وسنن الحج: منها الاغتسال ولو لحائض، ونفساء، أو الوضوء إذا أراد الإحرام، ولبس إزار ورداء جديدين أبيضين، والتطيب، وصلاة ركعتين والإكثار من التلبية بعد الإحرام، رافعاً بها صوته متى صلى.
(1) اختلف العلماء في السنة التي فرض فيها الحج، والمشهور أنها سنة ست وهو الصحيح، وقيل سنة خمس، وقيل سنة تسع. وصححه القاضي عياض، وقيل: فرض قبل الهجرة وهو بعيد وأبعد منه قول بعضهم إنه فرض سنة عشر. أخرج البخاري عن زيد بن أرقم: أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم حج بعد ما هاجر حجة واحدة وأخرج الدارقطني عن جابر بن عبد الله قال حج رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ثلاث حجج حجتين قبل أن يهاجر وحجة قرن بها عمرة، وكانت حجته بعد ما هاجر سنة عشر. وحج أبو بكر الصديق في السنة التي قبلها سنة تسع وأما سنة ثمان وهي عام الفتح فحج بالناس قبلها عتاب بن أسيد اهـ وهو الذي ولاه النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أميراً بمكة بعد الفتح. وذكر منلا علي أنه حج قبل أن يهاجر حججاً لا يعلم عددها. وقال ابن الأثير: كان يحج كل سنة قبل أن يهاجر، يعني إلا أن يمنع منه مانع. ط.
(2) كالحبس والخوف.
(3) من طلاق بائن أو رجعي أو وفاة؛ لقوله تعالى: {لا تُخْرِجُوهُنَّ مِنْ بُيُوتِهِنَّ} [الطلاق:1] والحج يمكن أداؤه في وقت آخر. ط.
(4) فإن فعل ذلك فسد حجه وعليه أن يمضي فيه كالصحيح وأن يقضي من قابل. ط.
(5) أي: طواف الإفاضة.
(6) أو التقصير.
(7) أي: بين الرمي والحلق فهو على ترتيب حروف (رذح) ط.
(8) لأنه للنظافة وإزالة الرائحة لا قصد الطهارة، ولقوله: (أن النفساء والحائض تغتسل وتحرم، وتقضي المناسك كلها غير أن لا تطوف بالبيت حتى تطهر)، أخرجه الترمذي في الحج، باب: (100)، (945).
(9) ينوي فيهما سنة الإحرام ليحرز فضيلة السنة، يقرأ فيهما بالكافرون والإخلاص لحديث ورد بذلك، ولما فيهما من البراءة عن الشرك وتحقيق التوحيد. ويقول بعد الصلاة: اللهم إني أريد الحج أو العمرة أو الحج والعمرة فيسرهما لي وتقبلهما مني، وفي الإفراد يفرد. ط.
Book of Hajj: Hajj is the visitation of specific places with specific actions in its months – which are Shawwal, Dhu al-Qa'dah, and the first ten days of Dhu al-Hijjah. It is obligatory once, immediately, according to the most correct opinion. Its conditions of obligation are eight according to the most correct: Islam, sanity, puberty, freedom, time, ability to provide provisions even if in Makkah with moderate expenses, ability to provide a mount specific to him or to share a litter by ownership or hire – not by permission or loan for other than the people of Makkah and those around them if they can walk on foot with strength without hardship; otherwise, a mount is absolutely necessary. And that ability must be surplus to his expenses and the expenses of his dependents until his return, and surplus to necessities like home, furniture, tools of professionals, and debt repayment. Knowledge of the obligation of Hajj is required for one who accepts Islam in dar al-harb or is in dar al-Islam. Conditions for the obligation of performance are five according to the most correct: sound body, removal of physical obstacles to going for Hajj, safety of the road, absence of waiting period (iddah), and the accompaniment of a mahram – even by fosterage or marriage – a trustworthy, sane, adult Muslim, or a husband for a woman on a journey. Consideration is given to the prevailing safety by land and sea according to the mufta bihi. The performance of the obligatory Hajj is valid with four things for a free person: ihram and Islam – both are conditions – then performing its two pillars: standing at Arafat in ihram for a moment from noon of the ninth day to dawn of the Day of Sacrifice, provided there is no intercourse before it while in ihram. The second pillar is the majority of Tawaf al-Ifadah in its time, which is after dawn of the Day of Sacrifice. The wajibat of Hajj are: initiating ihram from the miqat, prolonging standing at Arafat until sunset, standing at Muzdalifah after dawn of the Day of Sacrifice and before sunrise, stoning the jamarat, sacrificing for the qarin and mutamatti', shaving or trimming, specifying it to the Haram and days of sacrifice, presenting stoning over shaving, sacrificing the qarin and mutamatti' between them, performing Tawaf al-Ziyarah during the days of sacrifice, Sa'i between Safa and Marwah in the months of Hajj, its occurrence after a valid tawaf, walking in it for one without excuse, beginning Sa'i from Safa, Tawaf al-Wada', beginning every tawaf at the Black Stone, keeping the left shoulder towards the Kaaba, walking in it for one without excuse, purification from both hadaths, covering the awrah, performing at least the majority of the circuits of Tawaf al-Ziyarah, and avoiding prohibitions like wearing sewn garments for men, covering the head and face for men, covering the face for women, obscenity, sinfulness, argumentation, killing game, pointing to game, and guiding to game. The sunan of Hajj include: performing ghusl even for a menstruating woman or woman in post-natal bleeding, or wudu if one intends ihram, wearing two new white garments, applying perfume, praying two rak'ahs, and increasing talbiyah after ihram, raising the voice when he has prayed. Footnotes: (1) Scholars differed on which year Hajj was made obligatory; the well-known view is year six and that is correct, and it was also said year five, and said year nine. Al-Qadi Iyad authenticated it, and it was said it was made obligatory before the Hijrah which is far-fetched, and even more far-fetched is the statement of some that it was made obligatory in year ten. Al-Bukhari narrated from Zayd ibn Arqam that the Prophet (peace be upon him) performed only one Hajj after migrating, and Al-Daraqutni narrated from Jabir ibn Abdullah that he said: 'The Messenger of Allah performed three Hajjs: two before migrating and one with Umrah, and his Hajj after migration was in year ten.' Abu Bakr performed Hajj in year nine, and in year eight, which was the Conquest, `Attab ibn Asid led the people in Hajj. Mulla Ali mentioned that he performed several Hajjs before migration, the number unknown. Ibn al-Athir said: He used to perform Hajj every year before migrating, unless prevented. (2) Like imprisonment and fear. (3) From irrevocable divorce, revocable divorce, or death; because of Allah's saying: 'Do not expel them from their houses' [65:1], and Hajj can be performed at another time. (4) If he does that, his Hajj is spoiled, and he must continue in it like a valid Hajj and make it up the following year. (5) i.e., Tawaf al-Ifadah. (6) Or trimming. (7) i.e., between stoning and shaving, and it is in the order of the letters (r-dh-h). (8) Because it is for cleanliness and removing odor, not for purification, and because of his saying: 'The woman in post-natal bleeding and the menstruating woman should perform ghusl and enter ihram, and perform all rites except that they do not circumambulate the House until they become pure,' narrated by al-Tirmidhi. (9) He intends in them the sunnah of ihram to attain the virtue of sunnah, recites in them Surah al-Kafirun and al-Ikhlas due to a hadith, and for what they contain of disavowal of shirk and realization of tawhid. He says after the prayer: 'O Allah, I intend Hajj or Umrah or Hajj and Umrah, so make them easy for me and accept them from me.' In ifrad, he intends singly.
Source pages p. 688

Commentary
This passage introduces the Book of Hajj in the Hanafi school, providing a comprehensive overview of its definition, obligation, conditions, pillars, wajibat, and sunan. The author begins by defining Hajj as the visitation of specific places (Makkah, Mina, Arafat, Muzdalifah) with specific actions during the months of Shawwal, Dhu al-Qa'dah, and the first ten days of Dhu al-Hijjah. Hajj is obligatory once in a lifetime, immediately upon fulfilling conditions (not deferrable without excuse) according to the most correct opinion (al-asahh). Eight conditions of obligation (shurut al-fardiyyah) are listed: Islam, sanity, puberty, freedom, the occurrence of the Hajj season, ability to provide provisions and a mount (or share in a litter) from surplus wealth beyond essential needs and dependents' expenses, and knowledge of the obligation for those in dar al-harb or dar al-Islam. Then five conditions for the obligation of performance (shurut wujub al-ada') are given: sound health, absence of physical obstacles, safety of the route, not being in iddah, and availability of a mahram for women. The validity of Hajj requires four things: ihram and Islam (conditions) and the two pillars: standing at Arafat (wuquf) from zuhr on the 9th to dawn of the 10th, and the majority of Tawaf al-Ifadah after dawn of the 10th. Seventeen wajibat follow, including ihram from the miqat, extending wuquf to sunset, staying at Muzdalifah, stoning, sacrifice for qarin and mutamatti', shaving/trimming, and others. Finally, nine sunan are listed, such as ghusl before ihram, wearing white garments, perfume, two rak'ahs, and raising the voice in talbiyah. The footnotes provide additional details on the historical timing of the obligation, explanations of penalties, and hadith evidence for specific rulings. Throughout, the author uses phrases like 'ala al-asahh' (according to the most correct opinion) to indicate preferred Hanafi positions.

Key Terms
الحج (al-Hajj): Visitation of specific sacred places (Arafat, Muzdalifah, Mina, Kaaba) with specific actions during specific months.
الفور (al-fawr): Immediate performance upon fulfillment of conditions; not deferrable.
القدرة (al-qudrah): Ability to provide provisions and a mount or share in a litter, surplus to essential needs and debts.
الإحرام (al-ihram): The state of consecration for Hajj or Umrah, marked by intention and talbiyah, entering restrictions.
الركن (al-rukn): An integral part of Hajj without which the act is invalid; here: wuquf at Arafat and tawaf al-ifadah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT a condition for the obligation of Hajj (shurut al-fardiyyah)?
A) Islam
B) Sanity
C) Having a mahram for women
D) Ability to provide provisions

Key Takeaway
Hajj is an individual obligation once in a lifetime, immediate upon ability; its validity rests on the two pillars of standing at Arafat and Tawaf al-Ifadah, with wajibat compensated by dam if missed.

Wajibat and Muharramat of Hajj in the Hanafi School
List of wajibat and muharramat of Hajj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify each act mentioned in the passage as wajib, sunnah, or haram, and state the consequence of omission or commission.

Core Idea
Not every act prescribed for Hajj carries equal weight: wajib requires compensation, sunnah is optional, and haram incurs penalty.

This passage from Nur al-Idah concisely enumerates the obligatory rites, recommended practices, and prohibitions during Hajj. It serves as a memorization anchor for distinguishing the different categories of acts according to the Hanafi school. Understanding these categories is essential for knowing the legal consequences of one's actions during Hajj.

Guided Path
1
Identify all acts listed
Read the passage and extract every distinct act: standing at Arafat, staying at Muzdalifah, throwing pebbles, slaughtering, shaving, tawaf al-ziyarah, sa'i, tawaf al-wada', etc.
Some items are conditions (like purification) which are not independent wajibat.
2
Classify each act as wajib, sunnah, or haram
Using your knowledge of Hanafi fiqh, assign each act to its category. Wajib acts must be performed; omission requires dam. Sunnah acts are recommended but not required. Haram acts must be avoided; commission requires jaza'.
The passage mixes categories; e.g., 'extending stay until sunset' is wajib, 'beginning from the Black Stone' is sunnah.
3
Determine consequences for wajib omission and haram commission
For each wajib, note that if omitted intentionally or unintentionally, a dam (sacrifice) is due. For each haram, note the penalty (e.g., a sheep for hunting). Sunnah omission has no consequence.
The passage does not specify penalties; those are known from other sources.
4
Memorize the sequence and categories
Practice reciting the list in order, grouping them by category. Use mnemonic devices: 'Arafat to sunset, Muzdalifah at dawn, ramy, slaughter, shave, tawaf, sa'i, farewell tawaf, then conditions, then prohibitions.'
This passage is a memorization anchor; frequent recitation is beneficial.

الصفا ومد الوقوف بعرفات إلى الغروب، والوقوف بالمزدلفة فيما بعد فجر يوم النحر وقبل طلوع الشمس، ورمي الجمار، وذبح القارن، والمُتَمَتِّعِ، والحلق، وتخصيصه بالحرم وأيام النحر، وتقديــم الرمي على الحلق، ونَحرُ القارِنِ والمُتَمَتِّعِ بينهما ) ، وإيقاع طواف الزيارة في أيام النحر، وا ر، والسعي والمروة في أشهر الحج، وحصوله بعد طواف معتد به والمشي فيه لمن لا عذر له، وبداءة بین السعي من الصفا (۳)، وطواف الوداع )، وبُدَاءةُ كل طواف بالبيت من الحجر الأسود، والتيامن فيه، والمشي فيه لمن لا عذر له، والطهارة من الحدثين، وستر العورة، وأقل الأشواط بعد فعل الأكثر مـــن طواف الزيارة، وترك المحظورات كلبس الرجل المخيط، وستر رأسه ووجهه، وستر المرأة وجهها (ه)، والرفث ) والفسوق ، والجدال، وقتل الصيد والإشارة إليه والدلالة عليه.
Safa and extending the stay at Arafat until sunset, and staying at Muzdalifah after dawn of the day of Nahr and before sunrise, and throwing the pebbles, and slaughtering the qarin and mutamatti', and shaving, and specifying it to the Haram and the days of Nahr, and giving precedence to throwing over shaving, and slaughter of the qarin and mutamatti' between them, and performing the visitation circumambulation on the days of Nahr, and (the sa'i between) Safa and Marwah in the months of Hajj, and its occurrence after a valid tawaf, and walking in it for one without excuse, and beginning the sa'i from Safa, and the farewell circumambulation, and beginning every circumambulation of the House from the Black Stone, and making it to the right (counterclockwise), and walking in it for one without excuse, and purification from both minor and major hadath, and covering the private parts, and the minimum circuits after performing the majority of tawaf al-ziyarah, and abandoning prohibited acts such as a man wearing sewn garments, covering his head and face, a woman covering her face, and obscenity, and sinning, and disputing, and hunting game and pointing to it and guiding to it.
Source pages p. 689

Commentary
This passage lists the obligatory acts (wajibat) and prohibitions (muharramat) of Hajj according to the Hanafi school. It begins with the requirement to extend the stay at Arafat until sunset, which is a distinct wajib. Other wajibat include staying at Muzdalifah after dawn, throwing pebbles, slaughter (for qarin and mutamatti'), shaving or trimming hair, performing tawaf al-ziyarah on the days of Nahr, and sa'i between Safa and Marwah. The prohibitions during ihram include wearing sewn garments for men, covering the head and face for men, covering the face for women, engaging in obscenity (rafath), sinning (fusuq), disputing (jidal), and hunting. The passage also notes the sunnah acts of beginning sa'i from Safa and tawaf from the Black Stone, walking for those without excuse, and purification. This is a concise summary to be memorized.

Key Terms
الرَّفَث (ar-rafath): Obscenity or explicit sexual talk; also refers to sexual intercourse in the context of Hajj prohibitions.
الفُسُوق (al-fusuq): Sinful behavior, transgression of religious limits; includes cursing, backbiting, etc.
الجِدَال (al-jidal): Disputation or quarrelling, especially regarding the rituals of Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes between wajib (compensation required), sunnah (recommended), and haram (penalty incurred) in Hajj acts.

Sunan (Recommended Acts) and Disliked Acts of Hajj
Enumeration of recommended acts (sunan) and a disliked act (makruh) of Hajj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and explain at least ten sunan of Hajj and the one makruh act, distinguishing between sunnah muakkadah and makruh tanzihi.

Core Idea
The sunan of Hajj are rewarded but not required; missing them does not invalidate the pilgrimage.

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah lists the recommended acts (sunan) that the Prophet ﷺ consistently performed during Hajj. These acts bring great reward but are not obligatory. The passage also mentions one disliked act (makruh) that should be avoided. Understanding these helps pilgrims maximize their spiritual benefit.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Legal Category
Scan the passage: all acts are called 'sunan' except the last part which mentions 'kariha' (disliked). This distinction is key: sunan are recommended, makruh is not prohibited but discouraged.
The Hanafi school uses 'sunnah' for acts the Prophet consistently performed; leaving them loses reward but does not incur sin.
2
Group the Sunan by Hajj Phase
The sunan follow the chronological order of Hajj: preparation (bathing, garments), entering ihram (talbiyah), entering Makkah (tawaf al-qudum, idtiba', raml), sa'i, then the days of Hajj (sermon, Arafah, Muzdalifah, Mina, Jamarat). Grouping helps memorization and application.
For example, the bath before ihram is sunnah even for a menstruating woman, but she must not enter the mosque.
3
Note the Conditional and Gender-Specific Acts
Some sunan are conditional: raml only if sa'i follows in Hajj months; harwalah only for men; idtiba' only in tawaf. Distinguish these to avoid incorrect application.
Women do not perform raml or harwalah; they walk normally.
4
Recognize the Disliked Act and Its Reason
The only makruh is sending heavy luggage to Makkah during the days of Mina. The reason is that it distracts the pilgrim from the rituals and may cause arrogance or inconvenience.
This is makruh tanzihi, not tahrimi; doing it does not incur sin but is contrary to the preferred practice.
5
Apply the Hanafi Position in Practice
The passage represents the mu'tamad (reliable) Hanafi view. A pilgrim should strive to perform these sunan, but if some are missed, the Hajj remains valid.
For example, if one forgets to say takbir upon seeing the Ka'bah, no compensation is needed.

Commentary
This passage lists the sunan (recommended acts) of Hajj according to the Hanafi school. These are acts that the Prophet ﷺ consistently performed and are meritorious but not obligatory. They include: bathing (even for a menstruating or post-partum woman) or wudu before ihram; wearing new white garments; applying perfume; praying two rak'ahs; reciting talbiyah loudly; increasing talbiyah at specific times; sending blessings on the Prophet; asking for Paradise; seeking refuge; washing before entering Makkah; entering from the upper gate during the day; takbir and tahlil upon seeing the Ka'bah; supplication; performing tawaf al-qudum (arrival circumambulation) even outside Hajj months; adorning idtiba' (uncovering right shoulder) and raml (quick walking) in the first three circuits if followed by sa'i during Hajj months; harwalah (walking briskly) between the green pillars; walking calmly otherwise; increasing tawaf (which is better than optional prayer for non-Makkan pilgrims); the sermon on the 7th of Dhul Hijjah; going to Mina on Tarwiyah; staying at Arafat after sunrise; the imam's combined sermons at Arafat; supplication and humility; departing from Arafat with dignity; staying at Muzdalifah near Mount Quzah; staying at Mina with belongings; and several acts of throwing stones. It also mentions a disliked act (makruh): sending heavy luggage to Makkah during the days of Mina, as it distracts the pilgrim. The passage concludes with details on the manner of throwing pebbles: being mounted for the Jamrat al-Aqabah, walking for the first and middle jamrah, and standing in the valley.

Key Terms
الاضْطِبَاع (al-iddiba'): To place the upper garment (rida') under the right armpit and drape it over the left shoulder, leaving the right shoulder uncovered during tawaf.
الرَّمَل (ar-raml): Walking briskly with short steps and slight swaying of the shoulders during the first three circuits of tawaf al-qudum when followed by sa'i during Hajj months.
الهَرْوَلَة (al-harwalah): A brisk walk similar to jogging, between the two green pillars in Sa'i, specific to men.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is a sunnah (recommended) for a non-Makkan pilgrim?
A) Sending heavy luggage to Makkah during the days of Mina
B) Performing tawaf al-qudum even outside the months of Hajj
C) Covering the face for a woman during ihram
D) Throwing the jamrah while mounted on all days

Key Takeaway
The sunan of Hajj are numerous and bring reward, but missing them does not invalidate the pilgrimage; the only makruh act is sending luggage early to Makkah.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
intermediate

The Sunan of Hajj: A Comprehensive Summary
Enumerates recommended acts of Hajj with times and conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the major sunan of Hajj according to the Hanafi school and identify the recommended times and conditions for each.

Core Idea
Performing the sunan of Hajj perfects the pilgrimage; omitting them does not invalidate it.

This passage from Nur al-Idah outlines the sunan (recommended acts) of Hajj as taught in the Hanafi school. These acts, while not obligatory, complete the perfection of the pilgrimage and carry great reward. The text provides a comprehensive list spanning from the approach to Mecca to the final visit to the Prophet's Mosque in Medina, with specific details on timing and conditions for each sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Categorize the sunan by stage
The text lists sunan in chronological order: before entering Mecca, at the Ka'bah, during Tawaf, Sa'y, at Arafah, Muzdalifah, Mina, and after departure. Group them to understand the flow of Hajj.
This helps in memorizing the sequence.
2
Identify conditions and timings
For each sunnah, note if it has a specific time (e.g., Tawaf al-Qudum even outside Hajj months, stoning between sunrise and zawal on the first day), place (e.g., between the two green milestones in Sa'y), or gender specification (e.g., raml for men).
Some sunan are continuous (e.g., repeating talbiyah), others are time-bound.
3
Distinguish between sunnah, makruh, and mubah
The text explicitly marks some acts as makruh (e.g., stoning before sunrise on the first day) but valid. Understand the gradation: sunnah (reward), makruh (disliked but valid), mubah (permissible without preference).
This is crucial for fatwa and practice.
4
Connect to the fiqh ruling
Each sunnah is a recommended act; omission does not invalidate Hajj. Recognize that these sunan are from Zahir al-Riwayah and the mufta bihi position of the Hanafi school.
This underpins the non-obligatory nature of these acts.

Or if he ascends high ground or descends a valley, or meets a rider, and in the pre-dawn hours, and repeating the talbiyah whenever he begins it, sending blessings upon the Prophet, asking for Paradise and the company of the righteous, seeking refuge from the Fire. Ghusl for entering Mecca, entering it from the Bab al-Ma'lah during the day, saying takbir and tahlil facing the noble House, supplicating with whatever he wishes upon seeing it, and it is answered. Tawaf al-Qudum even in other than the months of Hajj, idtiba' in it, walking quickly (raml) if he performs sa'y after it in the months of Hajj, hurrying (harwalah) between the two green milestones for men, and walking with calmness in the rest of the sa'y. Performing tawaf abundantly, which is better than supererogatory prayer for the non-Makkan. The khutbah after zuhr prayer on the seventh of Dhul-Hijjah in Mecca, a single khutbah without sitting, teaching the rituals. Leaving after sunrise on the day of Tarwiyah from Mecca to Mina, staying overnight there, then leaving after sunrise on the day of Arafah to Arafat. The imam delivers a khutbah after zawal before the combined zuhr and asr prayers (jam' taqdim) – two khutbahs with a sitting between them. Striving in humility, weeping, supplicating for oneself, parents, and believing brothers with whatever one wishes of worldly and otherworldly matters in the two gatherings. Departing with tranquility and dignity after sunset from Arafat, descending at Muzdalifah on high ground away from the valley floor near Mount Quzah, staying overnight there on the night of sacrifice. Staying at Mina during the days of Mina with all his belongings. It is disliked to send his heavy luggage to Mecca at that time. He should make Mina on his right and Mecca on his left while standing for the stoning of the jamarat. Being mounted while stoning Jamrat al-Aqabah on all days, and walking to the first jamarah (nearest the mosque) and the middle one. Standing in the valley floor while stoning. The stoning on the first day is between sunrise and zawal, and on the remaining days between zawal and sunset. Stoning on the first and fourth days between dawn and sunrise is disliked. Stoning during the three nights is disliked, but valid because all nights follow the subsequent days except the night after Arafah (the night of sacrifice and the three nights of stoning) which follow the preceding day. The permissible time for stoning is after zawal until sunset on the first day. From this you know all the times for stoning in terms of permissibility, dislike, and recommendation. It is from the sunnah to sacrifice (hady) for one performing ifrad Hajj, and to eat from it, and from the voluntary sacrifice, and for tamattu' and qiran only. It is from the sunnah to deliver a khutbah on the day of Nahr like the first, in which he teaches the remaining rituals – it is the third khutbah of Hajj. Hastening the departure (nafr) from Mina before sunset on the 12th if he wishes; if he remains until sunset on the 12th, nothing is due but he has done wrong; if he remains until dawn of the 14th, he must stone. It is from the sunnah to descend at al-Muhassab for an hour after leaving Mina, drinking Zamzam water until satiated, facing the House, looking at it standing, pouring it on his head and entire body, for it is for whatever purpose he drinks it of worldly or religious matters. It is from the sunnah to cling to al-Multazam – placing his chest and face against it – and holding onto the curtains for an hour supplicating as he wishes, kissing the threshold of the House, entering it with adab and reverence. Then nothing remains but the greatest acts of devotion: visiting the Prophet (peace be upon him) and his companions. He should intend this when leaving Mecca from Bab Shubayka from the lower pass. We will mention a separate section on visitation if Allah wills.
Source pages p. 690

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement enumerating the sunan (recommended acts) of Hajj as per the Hanafi school. The text lists a comprehensive series of recommended practices spanning from the approach to Mecca, entering it, performing Tawaf and Sa'y, the khutbahs, the stay at Mina, Arafah, Muzdalifah, the stoning of the jamarat, the sacrifice, the khutbah of Yaum al-Nahr, departure from Mina, and concluding with the visitation of the Prophet's Mosque in Medina. Each item is presented as a sunnah, and some rulings on dislike (karahah) and permissibility (ibahah) are included. For example, the time for stoning on the first day is recommended between sunrise and zawal, while stoning before sunrise is disliked but valid. The passage also clarifies that the nights of stoning follow the preceding days except the night of 'Arafah. Additionally, it notes that Tawaf al-Qudum is sunnah even outside the months of Hajj, and that idtiba' (exposing the right shoulder) is performed during it, with raml (quick walking) in the first three rounds of Sa'y if it follows Tawaf in the months of Hajj. The commentary in the footnotes provides definitions and clarifications: e.g., "al-ulu" means high ground; the recommended du'a upon seeing the Ka'bah includes 'Allahumma ij'al du'a'i mustajab'; idtiba' involves placing the wrap under the right arm; raml is defined as fast walking with shoulder movements in the first three rounds; harwalah is the pace between the green pillars; and the authority for Zamzam water comes from Ibn Majah. The overall structure is a straightforward enumeration, making this a memorization anchor for students. The Hanafi school emphasizes these sunan as completing the perfection of Hajj, without affecting its validity if omitted.

Key Terms
سنن الحج (sunan al-hajj): Recommended acts during pilgrimage; their performance earns reward but omission does not invalidate Hajj.
الاضطباع (al-idtiba'): To place the upper garment under the right armpit and throw its end over the left shoulder, exposing the right shoulder.
الرمل (ar-raml): Walking quickly with short steps and shoulder movements in the first three circuits of Sa'y.
الهرولة (al-harwalah): A fast pace between the two green milestones in Sa'y.
المحصب (al-muhassab): A place near Mecca, also called al-Abtah, where it is sunnah to halt after leaving Mina.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The sunan of Hajj are numerous and cover every stage; knowing them allows a pilgrim to earn maximum reward while understanding that omission does not invalidate the Hajj.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
beginner

Sunnan of Hajj: Times of Ramy, Hady, and Visit
Listing and explaining post-ramy sunan of Hajj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the sunan of Hajj that follow the stoning rituals and distinguish the rulings of permissibility, dislike, and recommendation for each act.

Core Idea
The sunan of Hajj complete the pilgrimage; know them to perfect your reward.

Having completed the essential stoning rituals, the pilgrim is encouraged to observe a series of sunan that round off the Hajj experience. This passage from the classical Hanafi text Nur al-Idah outlines these sunan, including the proper times for stoning, the sacrificial offering (hady), the khutbah on the Day of Nahr, the etiquette of leaving Mina, and the special acts near the Kaaba. Understanding these sunan helps the pilgrim maximize the spiritual benefits of Hajj.

Guided Path
1
Categorize the acts mentioned
List each act described in the passage and note whether it is labeled as 'from the sunnah' or given a ruling of dislike or permissibility.
The text repeatedly says 'Min al-sunnah' (among the sunnah) for acts like hady, khutbah, Muhassab, etc.
2
Identify the stoning time rulings
Note the three categories of stoning times: permissible (after zawal on the first day), disliked (certain days at dawn, and all three nights), and the validity of stoning at night despite the dislike.
The text explicitly says 'makruh' (disliked) but 'sahih' (valid).
3
Link sunan to their contexts
For each sunnah, recall the context in which it is performed: e.g., hady follows the stoning, khutbah on the 10th, departure on the 12th or 13th, halting at Muhassab after Mina, etc.
This helps in remembering the sequence of Hajj.
4
Note exceptions and special cases
Pay attention to the exception for the night after Arafah and the ruling on staying until dawn of the 13th (which requires additional stoning).
The text says nights are attached to following days except the night of Eid and the three stoning nights.
5
Summarize the greatest remaining act
The passage ends by indicating that visiting the Prophet's ﷺ mosque and grave is the greatest devotion after completing the Hajj rituals.
This sets up the next chapter on ziyarah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأول فيما بين طلوع الشمس وزوالها، وفيما بين الزوال وغروب الشمس في باقي الأيام، وكره الرمي في اليوم الأول والرابع فيما بين طلوع الفجر والشمس. وكره في الليالي الثلاث، وصح، لأن الليالي كلها تابعة لما بعدها من الأيام إلا الليلة التي تلي عرفة حتى صح فيها الوقوف بعرفات، وهي: ليلة العيد وليالي الرمي الثلاث فإنها تابعة لما قبلها، والمباح من أوقات الرمي ما بعد الزوال إلى غروب الشمس من اليوم الأول وبهذا عَلِمْتَ أوقات الرمي كلها جوازاً وكراهة واستحباباً، ومن السُّنَّةِ هَدْي المُفْرِدِ بالحج، والأكل منه، ومن هدي التطوع، والمتعة والقران فقط. ومن السنة الخطبة يوم النحر مثل الأولى يُعلِّمُ فيها بقية المناسك، وهي ثالثة خطب الحج، وتعجيل النفر إذا أراده مـن منـى قبـل غروب الشمس من اليوم الثاني عشر، وإن أقام بها حتى غربت الشمس من اليوم الثاني عشر فلا شيء عليه وقد أساء، وإن أقام بمنى إلى طلوع فجر اليوم الرابع لزمه رميه. ومن السُّنَّةِ النزول بالمُحَصَّبِ ساعة بعد ارتحاله من مِنَى ، وشرب ماء زمزم والتضلع منه واستقبال البيت، والنظر إليه قائماً، والصب منه على رأسه وسائر جسده، وهو لما شرب له من أمور الدنيا والآخرة. ومـن السُّنَّةِ التزام المُلْتَزَم، وهو أن يضع صدره ووجهه عليه، والتشبث بالأستار ساعة داعياً بمـا أحـب، وتقبيل عتبة البيتِ، ودُخُولُهُ بالأدب، والتعظيم ثم لم يبق عليه إلا أعظم القربات، وهي: زيارة النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وأصحابه، فينويه عند خروجه من مكة من باب شبيكة من الثنية السفلى، وسنذكر للزيارة فصلاً على حدته إن شاء الله تعالى.
First: between sunrise and its zenith, and between the zenith and sunset on the remaining days. And it is disliked to stone on the first and fourth days between dawn and sunrise. And it is disliked on the three nights, but valid, because all nights are attached to the days after them except the night that follows Arafah, as standing at Arafah is valid in it; it is the night of Eid and the three nights of stoning, for they are attached to what precedes them. And the permissible time for stoning is after zenith until sunset of the first day. By this you have known all the times of stoning: permissibility, dislike, and desirability. And among the sunnah is the hady of the one performing Hajj individually (ifrad), and eating from it, and from the hady of voluntary, tamattu' and qiran only. And among the sunnah is the khutbah on the Day of Nahr like the first, in which he teaches the remaining rituals; it is the third khutbah of Hajj. And hastening the departure (nafr) from Mina before sunset on the 12th day if one desires it. If he stays there until sunset on the 12th day, nothing is upon him but he has done wrong. And if he stays in Mina until dawn of the 4th day, stoning is incumbent upon him. And among the sunnah is halting at al-Muhassab for a while after departing from Mina. And drinking Zamzam water, drinking one's fill, facing the House, looking at it while standing, pouring it on one's head and entire body, and it is for whatever one drinks it for (of worldly or otherworldly matters). And among the sunnah is clinging to al-Multazam, i.e., placing his chest and face on it, and clinging to the curtains while supplicating as he pleases, and kissing the threshold of the House, and entering it with respect and reverence. Then nothing remains for him except the greatest of acts of devotion: visiting the Prophet ﷺ and his Companions, intending it when leaving Makkah from the Shubaikah gate from the lower pass. And we will mention a separate chapter on the visit, if Allah wills.
Source pages p. 691

Commentary
This passage lists various sunan of Hajj after the stoning rituals. It begins with detailing the times for stoning: permissible, disliked, and recommended. It covers the hady (sacrificial animal) for ifrad, tamattu', and qiran, and the khutbah of the Day of Nahr. It then discusses the ruling on early departure from Mina and staying until the 13th. Next, it mentions the sunnah of halting at al-Muhassab (the valley between Mina and Makkah), drinking Zamzam water in abundance facing the qiblah, and pouring it over oneself. It notes the virtue of Zamzam water being for whatever one intends. Then it describes the sunnah of clinging to al-Multazam, kissing the threshold, and entering the Kaaba with reverence. Finally, it states that the greatest remaining devotion is visiting the Prophet's ﷺ mosque and grave, and that a separate chapter will cover it.

Key Terms
المحصب (al-Muhassab): A place between Mina and Makkah (also called al-Abtah) where it is sunnah to halt after departing Mina.
المتلزم (al-Multazam): The area between the Black Stone and the door of the Kaaba where one places his chest and face, considered a place of supplication.
الهدي (al-hady): The sacrificial animal offered during Hajj, required for tamattu' and qiran, and recommended for ifrad and voluntary.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on stoning during the nights of the 11th, 12th, and 13th of Dhul-Hijjah?
A) It is permissible and recommended.
B) It is disliked but valid.
C) It is invalid and must be repeated.
D) It is obligatory for those who delayed.

Key Takeaway
The sunan of Hajj after ramy complete the pilgrimage; they are recommended acts that enhance reward but are not obligatory.

Entering Ihram: Preparations and the Talbiyah
Step-by-step instructions for beginning ihram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the recommended acts before ihram and state the essential components (intention and talbiyah) that establish the state of ihram.

Core Idea
Ihram is entered by intention and talbiyah; everything else is sunnah.

This passage guides the pilgrim step-by-step from the miqat, covering personal grooming, garments, prayer, and the essential declaration. Understanding these steps ensures that ihram is valid and complete.

Guided Path
1
Identify the miqat and first required action
The pilgrim enters ihram from the designated miqat (e.g., Rabigh). The first recommended act is performing ghusl or wudu, with ghusl being preferred.
Ghusl is considered sunnah muakkadah for men and women, even for menstruating women if not harmful.
2
List recommended acts of cleanliness and adornment
The passage recommends trimming nails, mustache, plucking armpit hair, shaving pubic hair, applying oil/perfume, and having intercourse with one's spouse before ihram.
These acts are sunnah, not wajib; omitting them does not affect validity of ihram.
3
Describe proper ihram garments for men
Men wear an izaar (lower garment) and rida' (upper wrap), preferably new and white. They should not button, knot, or sew the cloth; doing so is makruh but does not invalidate ihram.
Women wear their ordinary sewn clothing; the prohibition on sewn garments applies only to men.
4
Outline the prayer and talbiyah
After garments, the pilgrim prays two rak'ahs, makes intention for Hajj, and recites the talbiyah. The full text is given; additions are sunnah. Upon reciting the talbiyah with intention, ihram is established.
The talbiyah is wajib (obligatory) in the Hanafi school; omitting it invalidates ihram.

Rules of Ihram: Prohibitions, Permissible Acts, and Arrival in Makkah
Rules of ihram and arrival in Makkah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the prohibitions of ihram, distinguish permissible acts, and describe the recommended actions upon arriving in Makkah.

Core Idea
In ihram, avoid rafath, fisq, jidal, hunting, sewn garments, perfume, and hair removal; but ghusl, shade, and money-belt are allowed.

This passage continues the rules of ihram, listing forbidden and permissible acts, followed by the etiquettes of entering Makkah and beginning tawaf. Understanding these rules is essential to preserve the validity of one's Hajj.

Guided Path
1
List the prohibitions (muharramat) of ihram
The passage explicitly forbids: sexual intercourse (rafath), sin (fisq), arguing (jidal), hunting land game, wearing sewn garments (for men), covering head and face, applying perfume, shaving hair, and others. Identify each category.
Rafath includes intercourse and indecent talk; fisq includes all sins; jidal includes arguing.
2
Identify permissible acts during ihram
It is permissible to perform ghusl, take shade under a tent or litter, tie a money-belt, and recite talbiyah frequently.
These acts are mubah (permissible) and do not violate ihram.
3
Describe the etiquettes of reciting talbiyah
Talbiyah should be recited after prayers, on high places, descending valleys, meeting caravans, and at dawn. The voice should be raised without straining.
Frequent talbiyah is sunnah.
4
Outline the recommended acts upon reaching Makkah
It is recommended to perform ghusl, enter during the day from the Ma'la gate, continue talbiyah until the Salam gate, enter the mosque humbly, make supplication upon seeing the Kaaba, and approach the Black Stone for kissing or pointing.
The idtiba' (exposing right arm) is recommended during tawaf.

How to Enter Ihram
Describes the recommended and obligatory steps to enter the state of ihram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended actions before entering ihram and explain the correct method of pronouncing the talbiyah with intention.

Core Idea
Ihram is entered by intention and talbiyah at the miqat after performing recommended acts of cleanliness.

This lesson explains the proper procedure for entering the state of ihram for Hajj, starting from the miqat. It covers the recommended preparations, the proper attire, and the crucial role of intention and the talbiyah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the starting point
Recognize that ihram must be entered from the miqat. The text mentions 'from the miqat, like Rabigh'. The miqat is a fixed boundary that cannot be passed without ihram.
If you pass the miqat without ihram, a sacrifice is required.
2
Perform recommended cleanliness
List the recommended acts: ghusl (preferred) or wudu, trimming nails, moustache, plucking armpit hair, shaving pubic hair, and intercourse with one's wife. Even menstruating or postpartum women should perform ghusl if it does not harm them.
These are mustahabb (recommended) for physical and spiritual purification.
3
Dress in ihram garments
The man wears two unstitched garments: an izār (lower) and ridā’ (upper). They should be new or washed, white being best. He does not button, knot, or sew them. If he does, it is disliked but no expiation is required.
Women do not wear special garments; they must avoid face veil and gloves.
4
Apply perfume and pray
Apply perfume (even perfumed oil) is recommended, then pray two rak‘ahs. The intention is made: 'O Allah, I intend Hajj, so make it easy for me and accept it from me.'
Prayer is performed before the talbiyah.
5
Recite the talbiyah with intention
Immediately after the prayer, recite the talbiyah with the intention of entering ihram. The text gives the exact words and notes that additions are sunnah. The combination of intention and talbiyah constitutes the entry into ihram.
Do not shorten the talbiyah; the full wording is recommended.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في كيفية تركيب أفعال الحج إذا أراد الدخول في الحج أحرم من الميقات كرابغ فيغتسل أو يتوضأ، والغُسلُ أحَبُّ وهو للتنظيف؛ فتغتسل المرأة الحائض والنفساء إذا لم يضرها. ويستحب كمالُ النظافة وقص الظفر، والشارب، ونتف الإبط، وحلق العانة، وجماع الأهل، والدهنِ ولو مطيباً، ويلبس الرجل إزاراً، ورداء جديدين أو غسيلين، والجديد الأبيض أفضل، ولا يَزُره ولا يعقده؛ ولا يُخَلَّلهُ؛ فإن فعل كره ولا شيء عليه، وتطيب، وصلّ ركعتين وقل: اللهم إني أريد الحج، فيسره لي وتقبله مني، ولبِّ دُبُرَ صلاتك تنوي بها الحج، وهي ( لبيك اللهم لبيك لا شريك لك لبيك، إنَّ الحمد والنعمة والملك لك، لا شريك لك ولا تنقص من هذه الألفاظ شيئاً، وزد فيها «لبيك وسعديك، والخير کله يديك لبيك والرُّغبى إليك والزيادة سنة، فإذا لبيـت نـاويـاً فقد بین أحرمت، فاتق الرفث وهو : الجِماعُ، وقيل: ذكــره بحضرة النساء والكــلام الفاحش، والفسوق والمعاصي، والجدال مع الرفقاء والخدم، وقتل صيد البرّ، والإشارة إليه، والدلالـة عـلـيـه ولـبـس المخيط، والعمامة والخفَّين وتغطية الرأس والوجه، ومس الطيب، وحلق الرأس والشعر
A chapter on how to compose the actions of Hajj. When one intends to enter Hajj, he enters ihram from the miqat, like Rabigh, so he performs ghusl or wudu, and ghusl is more beloved, and it is for cleanliness; so the menstruating and postpartum woman performs ghusl if it does not harm her. Complete cleanliness, trimming the nails, moustache, plucking armpit hair, shaving pubic hair, intercourse with one's wife, and applying oil even if perfumed are recommended. The man wears two new or washed garments—a lower and an upper—and new white is best. He does not button or knot them, nor sew them; if he does, it is disliked but nothing is upon him. He applies perfume, prays two rak'ahs, and says: O Allah, I intend Hajj, so make it easy for me and accept it from me. Then he recites the talbiyah immediately after his prayer, intending thereby Hajj. It is: Labbayk Allahumma labbayk, la sharika laka labbayk, inna al-hamda wa al-ni'mata wa al-mulka laka, la sharika laka. Do not shorten any of these words, and add 'Labbayk wa sa'dayk, wa al-khayru kulluhu bi yadayk labbayk wa al-righba ilayk'—the addition is sunnah. When you recite the talbiyah with intention, you have entered ihram. Then avoid rafath which is intercourse, and it is said mentioning it in the presence of women and obscene speech, fisq (sins), jidal (quarreling) with companions and servants, hunting land game, pointing to it, indicating it, wearing stitched garments, the turban, leather socks, covering the head and face, touching perfume, shaving the head and hair.
Source pages p. 692

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling statement on the method of entering ihram for Hajj. It begins by stating that one should enter ihram from the miqat after performing ghusl or wudu, with ghusl being preferred. Even a menstruating or postpartum woman should do ghusl if it does not harm her. Then it lists recommended acts of cleanliness and grooming. The man wears two unstitched garments; stitching, knotting, or sewing them is disliked. He applies perfume, prays two rak'ahs, and then recites the talbiyah with the intention of Hajj. The talbiyah is the verbal declaration that constitutes ihram when accompanied by intention. The passage then lists the prohibitions of ihram: sexual intercourse (rafath), obscene speech, sins, quarreling, hunting land game, pointing to game, wearing stitched clothes, covering the head and face (for men), applying perfume, and shaving hair. These are all forbidden for the muhrim.

Key Terms
الميقات (al-miqat): The designated boundary from which one must enter ihram for Hajj or Umrah.
الرفث (al-rafath): Sexual intercourse and obscene talk in the presence of women.
الفسوق (al-fisq): All acts of disobedience to Allah (sins).
الجدال (al-jidal): Quarreling or arguing with companions or servants.
المخيط (al-makhit): Garments that are sewn or stitched, including shirts, trousers, etc.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on a menstruating woman performing ghusl before entering ihram?
A) It is obligatory.
B) It is prohibited because she is in a state of impurity.
C) It is recommended if it does not harm her.
D) It is disliked.

Key Takeaway
Ihram is entered by reciting the talbiyah with intention after performing recommended acts of purification.

Prohibitions of Ihram
Lists the prohibited actions for a person in the state of ihram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the prohibitions of ihram as mentioned in the text and explain the Hanafi classifications for each.

Core Idea
While in ihram, the pilgrim must avoid rafath, fisq, jidal, hunting, wearing stitched clothes, covering the head, applying perfume, and shaving hair.

This lesson details the actions that become forbidden (haram) once one enters the state of ihram. The text lists ten categories of prohibitions that range from moral offenses to specific dress restrictions. Understanding these prohibitions is essential to preserve the sanctity of ihram.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general command
The text says: 'Then avoid (ittaqi) rafath, fisq, jidal...' The word 'ittaqi' is an imperative indicating a prohibition. The pilgrim must abstain from these acts.
Some of these are also prohibited outside ihram but are emphasized here.
2
Define rafath
Rafath primarily means sexual intercourse. The text notes an opinion that it also includes mentioning intercourse in the presence of women and obscene speech. The Hanafi position includes both.
Intercourse invalidates the Hajj; obscene speech requires expiation.
3
Define fisq and jidal
Fisq encompasses all sins, both major and minor. Jidal is quarreling with companions or servants. These are general prohibitions that apply in all states but are especially important in ihram.
Fisq includes actions like lying and backbiting.
4
List the acts related to hunting
Hunting land game, pointing to it, and indicating its location are all prohibited. This includes any participation in hunting.
Sea game is permitted.
5
List the dress and grooming prohibitions
The text prohibits wearing stitched garments, the turban, leather socks, covering the head and face (for men), applying perfume, and shaving the head and hair. These are specific to the state of ihram.
Women cover their heads normally but may not cover their faces with a veil.

The Sunnahs of Entering Makkah and Performing Tawaf al-Qudum
Ruling statement on permissible acts and sunnahs upon arrival

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the sunnahs upon entering Makkah and describe the correct procedure for Tawaf al-Qudum, including idtiba', raml, and the ruling on the Hatim.

Core Idea
Tawaf al-Qudum is sunnah for the Afaqi; includes idtiba', raml, and must be performed behind the Hatim.

This passage from the Hanafi text Nur al-Idah outlines the recommended acts for a pilgrim arriving in Makkah. It details the etiquette of entering the city and the mosque, greeting the Black Stone, and performing the arrival tawaf (Tawaf al-Qudum) with its specific sunnah practices. Mastering these steps ensures one follows the Prophetic model in the early moments of Hajj or Umrah.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish permissible from sunnah acts
Identify which acts are merely permissible (e.g., bathing, shade) and which are sunnah specifically upon arrival (e.g., entering during the day from Bab al-Ma'la).
2
Trace the prescribed sequence
The text prescribes a sequence: enter Makkah → enter mosque → greet Black Stone → perform tawaf → pray two rak'ahs → touch Stone again. Note each step's specific instructions.
3
Identify key elements of Tawaf al-Qudum
The tawaf should be performed with idtiba' (right arm uncovered) and raml (quick pace) in the first three circuits, and must be conducted outside the Hatim. Recognize that this tawaf is for the afaqi only.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويجوز الاغتسال، والاستظلال بالخيمة، والمحمل، وغيرهما، وشدُّ الهِمْيان في الوسط، وأكثر التلبية متى صليت، أو علوت شرفاً، أو هبطت وادياً، أو لقيت ركباً وبالأسحار، رافعاً صوتك بلا جهد مضر. وإذا وصلت إلى مكة يستحب أن تغتسل، وتدخلها نهاراً من باب المَعْلَى لتكون مستقبلاً في دخولك بــاب البيت الشريف تعظيماً. ويستحب أن تكون ملبياً في دخولك حتى تأتي باب السلام، فتدخل المسجد الحرام منه، متواضعاً خاشعاً ملبياً، ملاحظاً جلالة المكان مكبراً مُهَلّلاً مصلياً على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ، متلطفـاً بالمَزَاحِمٍ، داعياً بما أحببت فإنه مستجاب عند رؤية البيت المكرم، ثم استقبل الحجر الأسود مكبراً مهللا رافعاً يديك كما في الصلاة وضعهما على الحجر وقبله بلا صوت، فمن عجز عن ذلك إلا بإيذاء، تركه ومس الحجر بشيء، وقبله أو أشار إليه من بعيد مكبراً مهللاً حامداً مصلياً على النبي ، ثم طف أخذاً عن يمينك مما يلي الباب مضطبعاً، وهو: أن تجعل الرداء تحت الإبط الأيمن، وتلقي طرفيه على الأيسر سبعة أشواط داعياً فيها بما شئت، وَطُف وراء الحَظِيمِ، وإن أردت أن تسعى بين الصفا والمروة عقب الطواف ، فَارْمل في الثلاثة الأشواط الأول، وهو المشي بسرعة مـع هـز الكتفين، كالمبارز يتبختر بين الصفين، فإن زَحَمَهُ الناس ،وقف، فإذا وجد فُرْجَةً رَمَلَ، لأنه لا بد له منه، فيقف حتى يقيمه على الوجه المسنون، بخلاف استلام الحجر الأسود لأن له بدلاً وهو استقباله، ويستلم الحجر كلما مر به، ويختم الطواف به وبركعتين في مقام إبراهيم عليه الصلاة والسلام، أو حيث تيسر من المسجد ، ثم عاد فاستلم الحجر وهذا طواف القدوم، وهو سنة للآفاقي
And it is permissible to bathe, to take shade under a tent, a litter, and other things, and to tie a money belt around the waist. And to recite the talbiyah frequently whenever you pray, or ascend a height, or descend a valley, or meet a caravan, and at dawn, raising your voice without harmful strain. When you arrive at Makkah, it is recommended to bathe, enter it during the day from the Bab al-Ma'la so that you face the door of the Noble House upon entering out of veneration. It is recommended to be reciting the talbiyah upon entering until you reach the Bab al-Salam, then enter the Sacred Mosque through it, humble, submissive, reciting talbiyah, observing the majesty of the place, saying takbir, tahlil, and sending blessings on the Prophet (ﷺ), being gentle with those crowding, making whatever supplication you wish, for it is answered upon seeing the honored House. Then face the Black Stone, saying takbir and tahlil, raising your hands as in prayer, place them on the Stone and kiss it without sound. Whoever cannot do so without causing harm, leaves it, touches the Stone with something, and kisses it, or points to it from afar, saying takbir, tahlil, praising and sending blessings on the Prophet. Then perform tawaf, taking to your right from the side of the door, with idtiba'—which is to place the upper garment under the right armpit and throw its ends over the left shoulder—seven circuits, supplicating therein as you wish. And perform tawaf behind the Hatim. If you intend to perform sa'y between Safa and Marwah after tawaf, then do raml in the first three circuits, which is walking quickly with shaking of the shoulders, like a valiant fighter strutting between two rows. If people crowd him, he stops, and when he finds a gap, he does raml, because it is necessary for him. So he stops until he does it in the prescribed manner, unlike touching the Black Stone because it has a substitute, which is facing it. He touches the Stone every time he passes by it, and concludes the tawaf with it and two rak'ahs at the Station of Ibrahim (ﷺ) or wherever in the mosque is convenient. Then he returns and touches the Stone. This is Tawaf al-Qudum, and it is sunnah for the one coming from afar (afaqi).
Source pages p. 692

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement on permissible acts while in ihram and the sunnahs of entering Makkah and performing Tawaf al-Qudum. It lists acts permissible in ihram: bathing, taking shade under a tent or litter, tying a money belt, and reciting the talbiyah frequently at specific times. Upon reaching Makkah, it is recommended to bathe, enter during the day from Bab al-Ma'la, and continue talbiyah until reaching Bab al-Salam. Entering the mosque with humility and making supplication upon seeing the Ka'bah is recommended. The method of greeting the Black Stone is described: kissing if possible without harm, otherwise touching or pointing. Tawaf is performed with idtiba' (uncovering the right arm) and raml (quick pace) in the first three circuits for men. The Hatim must be kept outside the tawaf path. After tawaf, two rak'ahs are prayed at Maqam Ibrahim, then the Stone is touched again. This tawaf is called Tawaf al-Qudum and is sunnah for those coming from outside Makkah (afaqi).

Key Terms
الإضطباع (al-idtiba'): Placing the upper garment under the right armpit and throwing the ends over the left shoulder, exposing the right arm during tawaf.
الرمَل (al-raml): Walking briskly with short steps and shaking the shoulders, like a fighter.
طواف القدوم (tawaf al-qudum): The tawaf performed upon arrival in Makkah by those coming from outside its boundaries.
الحطيم (al-hatim): The curved wall adjacent to the Ka'bah; originally part of it. Tawaf must be performed behind it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on Tawaf al-Qudum for a person from Makkah?
A) It is obligatory.
B) It is sunnah.
C) It is not sunnah; it is for afaqi only.
D) It is recommended equally for all.

Key Takeaway
Tawaf al-Qudum is a sunnah specific to non-Makkans; it includes idtiba', raml in the first three circuits, and must be performed behind the Hatim.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
