Performing Sa'y Between Safa and Marwah
Method of performing sa'y

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the step-by-step method of sa'y and identify its conditions and recommended acts according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Sa'y is seven circuits between Safa and Marwah, with running in the valley between the green markers.

After completing tawaf, the pilgrim proceeds to the hills of Safa and Marwah for sa'y. This lesson explains the detailed method: ascending Safa, facing the Ka'bah with supplications, descending, running briskly between the two green markers in the valley, and repeating the same at Marwah. We also clarify the Hanafi ruling that sa'y is wajib and the conditions for its validity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the starting point and direction
Begin at Safa, face the Ka'bah, and raise your hands in supplication. Then walk towards Marwah at a normal pace.
The order is important: start at Safa, end at Marwah.
2
Describe the actions at Safa and Marwah
Upon ascending, face the Ka'bah and recite takbir, tahlil, talbiyah, and salawat, and make du'a with raised hands. Do the same at Marwah.
These supplications are recommended (sunnah), not obligatory.
3
Explain the running (sa'y hasith) in the valley
When you reach the bottom of the valley between the two green markers, men should run briskly. After passing the valley, resume normal walking.
Women do not run; they walk normally.
4
State the number and sequence of circuits
Perform seven circuits: each circuit is from one hill to the other. Start at Safa and end at Marwah, so the odd circuits end at Marwah, even circuits at Safa.
The running is done in every circuit when crossing the valley.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم تخرج إلى الصفا، فتصعد وتقوم عليها حتى ترى البيت، فتستقبله مكبراً مهللاً ملبياً مصلياً داعياً، وترفع يديك مبسوطتين، ثم تهبط نحو المَروَةِ على هيئة، فإذا وصل بطن الوادي سعى بين الميلين الأخضـريــن سعياً حثيثاً، فإذا تجاوز بطن الوادي مشى على هِينَتِهِ، حتى يأتي المروة فيصعد عليها، ويفعل كما فعل على الصفا، ويستقبل البيت مكبراً مهللاً ملبياً مصلياً داعياً، باسطاً يديه نحو السماء، وهذا شوط ثم يعود قاصداً الصفا، فإذا وصل إلى الميلين الأخضرين سعى، ثم مشى على هِينَتِه حتى يأتي الصفا فيصعد عليها، ويفعل كما فعل أولاً، وهذا شوط ثان، فيطوف سبعة أشواط يبتدئ بالصفــا ويختم بالمروة، ويسعى في بطن الوادي في كل شوط منها
Then you go out to Safa, ascend and stand upon it until you see the House, then face it saying takbir, tahlil, talbiyah, sending blessings, and supplicating, and raise your hands outstretched. Then descend towards Marwah in a normal manner. When you reach the bottom of the valley, hasten between the two green markers with quick walking. When you pass the bottom of the valley, walk at your normal pace until you reach Marwah, ascend upon it, and do as you did on Safa: face the House saying takbir, tahlil, talbiyah, sending blessings, and supplicating, spreading your hands towards the sky. This is one circuit. Then you return heading to Safa. When you reach the two green markers, hasten, then walk at your normal pace until you reach Safa, ascend upon it, and do as you did the first time. This is a second circuit. So you perform seven circuits, starting with Safa and ending with Marwah, and you hasten in the bottom of the valley in each circuit of them.
Source pages p. 693

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement on the performance of sa'y between Safa and Marwah. After completing tawaf, the pilgrim proceeds to Safa, ascends it, faces the Ka'bah, and makes supplication with raised hands while reciting takbir, tahlil, talbiyah, and salawat. Then he descends and walks towards Marwah at a normal pace. Upon reaching the bottom of the valley (between the two green markers), he runs briskly (sa'y hasith) until he passes the valley, then resumes normal walking until he reaches Marwah. At Marwah, he does the same as at Safa: facing the Ka'bah and supplicating. This constitutes one circuit. The return from Marwah to Safa is the second circuit, again with running in the valley. He completes seven circuits, starting at Safa and ending at Marwah. The running in the valley is performed each time he traverses it.

Key Terms
السعي (al-sa'y): The ritual walking between Safa and Marwah seven times.
الميلان الأخضران (al-milan al-akhdaran): Two green markers indicating the bottom of the valley where running (sa'y hasith) is performed.
بطن الوادي (batn al-wadi): The bottom of the valley between Safa and Marwah, marked by the two green markers.
سعي حثيث (sa'y hasith): Quick walking or running, but not full sprint.
شوط (shaut): One circuit from Safa to Marwah or vice versa. Seven circuits complete the sa'y.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Where does the pilgrim run quickly during sa'y?
A) On the hills of Safa and Marwah.
B) Between the two green markers at the bottom of the valley.
C) Throughout the entire distance.
D) Only on the first circuit.

Key Takeaway
Sa'y consists of seven circuits between Safa and Marwah, with brisk walking in the valley between the green markers during each circuit.

The Pilgrim's Itinerary from Makkah to Arafat
Describes the sunnah sequence from Makkah to Arafat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended sequence of actions for a pilgrim (muhrim) from staying in Makkah to reaching Arafat on the 9th of Dhul Hijjah according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Voluntary tawaf is best until the 8th, then Mina overnight, then Arafat after sunrise on the 9th.

This lesson walks through the sunnah itinerary for a pilgrim after completing sa'y. The text describes staying in Makkah as a muhrim, performing voluntary tawaf, and the precise timings for departing to Mina and then to Arafat. Understanding this sequence helps the pilgrim follow the Prophetic practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the actions in Makkah
Find the ruling for staying in Makkah as a muhrim: the pilgrim remains in ihram and may perform voluntary tawaf whenever he wishes. This tawaf is better than supererogatory prayer for the afaqi (one from outside Makkah).
The virtue of tawaf over nafil prayer is specific to those not from Makkah.
2
Describe the departure to Mina
On the 8th of Dhul Hijjah (Yawm al-Tarwiyah), after Fajr prayer in Makkah, the pilgrim prepares to go to Mina. He leaves after sunrise, prays Zuhr at Mina, and stays there overnight. He does not abandon talbiyah except during tawaf.
Staying at Mina is sunnah; the pilgrim alights near Masjid al-Khayf.
3
Describe the move to Arafat
After praying Fajr at Mina at dawn on the 9th, the pilgrim waits until sunrise, then proceeds to Arafat. He stays at Arafat and when the sun passes its zenith (zawal), he goes to Masjid Namirah for the combined prayer.
The sequence emphasizes following the imam's schedule.

Combining Zuhr and Asr at Arafat: Conditions and Procedure
Conditions and procedure for combining Zuhr and Asr at Arafat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conditions for combining Zuhr and Asr at Arafat according to the Hanafi school and explain the procedure when praying behind the imam.

Core Idea
Combining Zuhr and Asr at Arafat requires ihram and following the imam; without both, pray separately.

This lesson explains the unique combination of Zuhr and Asr prayers on the 9th of Dhul Hijjah at Arafat. The text outlines the conditions: being in ihram and praying behind the greatest imam (or his deputy). The procedure includes sermons, one adhan, and two iqamas, with no supererogatory prayer between them. If one misses the congregation, each prayer is offered in its proper time.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two conditions for combination
Look for 'بشرطين الإحرام والإمام الأعظم'. The combination is only valid for a muhrim praying behind the head of state or his deputy. This is a Hanafi restriction.
The combination is not a general concession for travel; it is specific to Hajj.
2
Describe the prayer procedure
The imam delivers two sermons with a sitting between, then leads Zuhr and Asr with one adhan and two iqamas. No supererogatory prayer is offered between them. This is the sunnah procedure.
The two sermons are similar to Jumu'ah but without the call to prayer before the sermon.
3
Explain the ruling for missing the imam
If the pilgrim cannot catch the imam's congregation, he prays each prayer in its own usual time (Zuhr at zawal, Asr later). There is no permission to combine individually.
This underscores that combination is not a personal concession; it is tied to the imam's congregation.

Rulings and Sunan of Sa'i between Safa and Marwah
Describes the sunan and rulings of sa'i including raml and walking in the valley.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunan and rulings of sa'i between Safa and Marwah, including the manner of walking, the area of running, and the number of laps.

Core Idea
Sa'i is performed seven times from Safa to Marwah, with running between the green markers and walking elsewhere.

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah explains the detailed sunan of sa'i, building on the obligation of sa'i itself. You will learn the specific actions: ascending the hills, facing the Ka'ba, supplicating, and the precise location for running. Understanding these sunan ensures your sa'i is complete and in accordance with the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main rites and their order
The passage first describes tawaf (including behind al-Hatim, raml, touching the Black Stone, and tawaf al-qudum), then the sa'i procedure. Note that tawaf al-qudum is sunnah for those coming from outside the miqat.
2
Distinguish between sunnah and obligatory elements
Raml in tawaf is a sunnah muakkadah; running (s'a) between the green markers in sa'i is also a sunnah performed in every lap. The sa'i itself is wajib in the Hanafi school, but the passage focuses on the sunan.
The text states 'يسعى في بطن الوادي في كل شوط منها'.
3
Locate the specific rulings for special cases
If crowded, one stops and then resumes raml when possible, as it has no substitute. In contrast, touching the Black Stone can be substituted by facing it. Tawaf must be performed behind al-Hatim, not between it and the Ka'ba.
See the phrase 'بخلاف استلام الحجر الأسود'.
4
Apply the rules for sa'i procedure
Begin at Safa, ascend and face the Ka'ba, supplicate with raised hands. Descend to Marwah, run between the two green markers in the valley bottom, walk normally elsewhere. At Marwah, repeat the supplication. Complete seven laps, starting at Safa and ending at Marwah.
The text explicitly says 'يبتدئ بالصفا ويختم بالمروة'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(٢) الصفا على الأيسر سبعة أشواط داعياً فيها بما شئت، وَطُف وراء الحَظِيمِ، وإن أردت أن تسعى بين والمروة عقب الطواف ، فَارْمل في الثلاثة الأشواط الأول، وهو المشي بسرعة مـع هـز الكتفين، كالمبارز يتبختر بين الصفين، فإن زَحَمَهُ الناس ،وقف، فإذا وجد فُرْجَةً رَمَلَ، لأنه لا بد له منه، فيقف حتى يقيمه على الوجه المسنون، بخلاف استلام الحجر الأسود لأن له بدلاً وهو استقباله، ويستلم الحجر كلما مر به، ويختم الطواف به وبركعتين في مقام إبراهيم عليه الصلاة والسلام، أو حيث تيسر من المسجد ، ثم عاد فاستلم الحجر وهذا طواف القدوم، وهو سنة للآفاقي، ثم تخرج إلى الصفا، فتصعد وتقوم عليها حتى ترى البيت، فتستقبله مكبراً مهللاً ملبياً مصلياً داعياً، وترفع يديك مبسوطتين، ثم تهبط نحو المَروَةِ على هيئة (۳)، فإذا وصل بطن الوادي سعى بين الميلين الأخضـريــن سعياً حثيثاً، فإذا تجاوز بطن الوادي مشى على هِينَتِهِ، حتى يأتي المروة فيصعد عليها، ويفعل كما فعل على الصفا، ويستقبل البيت مكبراً مهللاً ملبياً مصلياً داعياً، باسطاً يديه نحو السماء، وهذا شوط ثم يعود قاصداً الصفا، فإذا وصل إلى الميلين الأخضرين سعى، ثم مشى على هِينَتِه حتى يأتي الصفا فيصعد عليها، ويفعل كما فعل أولاً، وهذا شوط ثان، فيطوف سبعة أشواط يبتدئ بالصفــا ويختم بالمروة، ويسعى في بطن الوادي في كل شوط منها.
(۱) الحطيم هو قطعة جدار في طرف الميزاب من الحطم بمعنى الكسر ، سمي به لأنه حطم من البيت، فإنه كان في الأول من البيت، وإذا كان كذلك يطاف من وراءه، فلو طاف من الفرجة التي بينه وبين البيت لا يجوز احتياطاً. اللباب (١٨٥/١) بتصرف.
(۲) هو حجر كان يقوم عليه عند نزوله عن الإبل وركوبه عند إتيانه هاجر وولده ظهر فيه أثر قدميه. ط.
(۳) انظر ص (٦٨٩) التعليق رقم (٥)..
Chapter 2: Sa'i on the left side seven laps, supplicating therein as you wish. And perform tawaf behind al-Hatim. And if you intend to perform sa'i between Safa and Marwah after tawaf, then do raml in the first three laps, which is walking quickly with shaking of the shoulders, like a wrestler strutting between two rows. If people crowd him, he stops, and when he finds a gap, he performs raml, because it is necessary for him. So he stops until he performs it in the sunnah manner, unlike touching the Black Stone because it has a substitute, which is facing it. And he touches the Black Stone whenever he passes by it, and concludes the tawaf with it and two rak'ahs at the Maqam of Ibrahim (peace be upon him), or wherever is convenient in the mosque. Then he returns and touches the Stone. This is tawaf al-qudum, and it is sunnah for the one coming from outside the miqat (afaqi). Then he goes out to Safa, ascends and stands upon it until he sees the House, then faces it saying takbir, tahlil, talbiyah, salawat, and supplications, raising his hands open. Then he descends towards Marwah in a certain manner (3). When he reaches the bottom of the valley, he runs between the two green markers with vigorous running. When he passes the bottom of the valley, he walks at his normal pace until he reaches Marwah, ascends upon it, and does as he did on Safa, facing the House with takbir, tahlil, talbiyah, salawat, and supplications, spreading his hands towards the sky. This is one lap. Then he returns heading for Safa. When he reaches the two green markers, he runs, then walks at his normal pace until he reaches Safa, ascends upon it, and does as he did first. This is a second lap. So he performs seven laps, starting at Safa and ending at Marwah, and runs in the bottom of the valley in each lap. Footnotes: (1) Al-Hatim is a piece of wall at the side of the waterspout, from 'hatm' meaning breaking; it is so called because it was broken from the House. It was originally part of the House. Therefore, one makes tawaf from behind it. If one makes tawaf from the gap between it and the House, it is not valid as a precaution. (2) It is a stone on which he used to stand when dismounting from his camel and mounting it when he came to Hajar and his son; the trace of his feet appeared on it. (3) See page 689, comment no. 5.
Source pages p. 693

Commentary
This passage from Imdad al-Fattah, a commentary on Nur al-Idah, details the sunan and rulings of sa'i between Safa and Marwah. The author begins by noting that the sa'i is performed on the left side of the valley, comprising seven laps during which one may make any supplications. He then discusses the ruling on tawaf behind al-Hatim, emphasizing that one must circumambulate outside this wall, not between it and the Ka'ba. The performance of raml is described: a brisk, proud manner of walking with shoulder movements, limited to the first three laps of tawaf. If crowded, one stops and resumes when possible, as raml is a non-negotiable sunnah. This is contrasted with touching the Black Stone, which has a substitute of merely facing it. The pilgrim touches the Stone each circuit and concludes tawaf with two rak'ahs at the Maqam of Ibrahim. Tawaf al-qudum is a sunnah specifically for those entering from outside the miqat (afaqi). For sa'i itself, one ascends Safa, faces the Ka'ba, and engages in dhikr and du'a with raised hands. Then one descends to Marwah, running between the two green markers in the valley's bottom, and walking at a normal pace elsewhere. This process is repeated for seven laps, starting and ending at the respective hills. The footnotes clarify: al-Hatim is a remnant of the Ka'ba, so tawaf must be outside it; the stone at Maqam is where Ibrahim stood; and a reference to a prior comment about the descent from Safa.

Key Terms
الصفا (al-Safa): The hill from which sa'i begins.
المروة (al-Marwah): The hill at which sa'i ends.
الرمل (al-raml): Walking briskly with shoulder movements in the first three laps of tawaf.
السعي (al-sa'y): The rite of walking and running between Safa and Marwah seven times.
بطن الوادي (batn al-wadi): The bottom of the valley between Safa and Marwah where running occurs.
الميلان الأخضران (al-milan al-akhdaran): Two green markers indicating the area where running is performed in sa'i.
الحطيم (al-Hatim): A curved wall on the north side of the Ka'ba; tawaf must be performed behind it.
مقام إبراهيم (Maqam Ibrahim): The stone upon which Ibrahim stood while building the Ka'ba; two rak'ahs are performed near it after tawaf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The entire distance between Safa and Marwah.
B) Only between the two green markers in the valley.
C) Only on the hills of Safa and Marwah.
D) None; walking is sufficient.

Key Takeaway
The sunan of sa'i include running between the green markers in every lap, ascending both hills, and supplicating while facing the Ka'ba.

Hajj Rituals from the 8th to the 10th of Dhul Hijjah
Describes the recommended and obligatory acts of Hajj from the 8th to the 10th of Dhul Hijjah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the sequence of Hajj rites from the 8th to the 10th of Dhul Hijjah, state the conditions for combining Zuhr and Asr at Arafat, and explain the Hanafi preference for shaving over shortening.

Core Idea
The Hajj rites culminate at Arafat, then Muzdalifah, then Mina; shaving is more virtuous than shortening.

This lesson details the prescribed actions from the 8th to the 10th of Dhul Hijjah, including the stay in Mina, the standing at Arafat, the overnight at Muzdalifah, and the stoning at Jamrat al-Aqaba. It also highlights the Hanafi ruling that shaving the head is better than shortening, supported by a hadith from Bukhari.

Guided Path
1
Trace the chronological order of rites
Identify the movement from Mecca to Mina on the 8th, then to Arafat on the 9th, then to Muzdalifah after sunset, and finally to Mina on the 10th for stoning and shaving.
2
Identify conditions for combining Zuhr and Asr at Arafat
Note the two conditions: being in the state of ihram and following the great Imam or his deputy. If the Imam is not present, pray each prayer at its usual time.
3
Understand the ruling on standing places
All of Arafat is valid for standing except Batn 'Uranah; all of Muzdalifah is valid except Batn Muhassir.
4
Analyze the evidence for shaving vs shortening
Examine the hadith where the Prophet supplicated three times for those who shave and only once for those who shorten, indicating the greater merit of shaving.

فيأتي إلى مِنَى وينزل بها، ثم يأتي جمرة العقبة فيرميها من بطن الوادي بسبع حصيات مثل حصى الخزف ويستحب أخذ الجمار من المزدلفة أو من الطريق. ويكره من الذي عند الجمرة. ويكره الرمي من أعلى العقبة لإيذائه الناس، ويلتقطها التقاطاً، ولا یکسر حجراً حِمَارَاً، ويغسلها ليتيقن طهارتها فإنها يقام بها قربة، ولـو رمـى بنجسة أجزأه وكره، ويقطع التلبية مع أول حصاة يرميها. وكيفية الرمي أن يأخذ الحصاة بطرف إبهامه وسبابته في الأصح، لأنه أيسر وأكثر إهانة للشيطان. والمسنون الرمي باليد اليمنى، ويضع الحصاة على ظهر إبهامه، ويستعين بالمُسَبَّحَةِ، ويكون بين الرامي وموضع السقوط خمسة أذرع. ولو وقعت على ظهر رجل أو محل (٢) أي: كالذي يطلب الطعام وهيئته كالدعي. ط.
(۳) سمي به لأن الفيل [ أصحاب الفيل ] حسر وأعيا فيه فلا يجوز الوقوف فيه. ط.
(٤) لما روي عن أبي هريرة رضي الله عنه قال: قال رسول الله : ( اللهم اغفر للمحلقين» قالوا: يا رسول الله والمقصرين؟ قال: اللهم اغفر للمحلقين ثلاثاً، قالوا: يا رسول الله والمقصرين قال: « والمقصرين». أخرجه البخاري في الحج، باب الحلق والتقصير (۱۷۲۸).
Then he stays in Mecca as a muhrim, and performs tawaf around the House whenever he wishes, and that is better than optional prayer for the afaqi. Then when he prays Fajr in Mecca on the 8th of Dhul Hijjah, he prepares to go out to Mina, and leaves after sunrise. It is mustahabb to pray Zuhr in Mina. He does not abandon talbiyah in all his states except during tawaf. He stays in Mina until he prays Fajr there in the early morning darkness, and descends near the Mosque of al-Khayf. Then after sunrise he goes to Arafat and stays there. When the sun declines, he comes to the mosque of Namirah and prays Zuhr and Asr with the great Imam or his deputy after he delivers two sermons with a sitting between them. He prays the two obligatory prayers with one adhan and two iqamahs, and he does not combine them except on two conditions: ihram and the great Imam. He does not separate the two prayers with a supererogatory prayer. If he does not catch the great Imam, he prays each at its usual time. When he prays with the Imam, he proceeds to the standing place. All of Arafat is a standing place except the bottom of 'Uranah. He performs ghusl after noon at Arafat for the standing. He stands near the Mountain of Mercy, facing the Qibla, saying takbir, tahlil, talbiyah, and supplicating, stretching out his hands like one begging for food. He strives in supplication for himself, his parents, and his brothers. He strives to have drops of tears come out of his eyes, for that is a sign of acceptance. He is persistent in supplication with strong hope of response. He does not fall short on this day, for he cannot make it up, especially if he is from outside the miqat. Standing on a mount is better, and standing on the ground is better than sitting. When the sun sets, the Imam and the people depart from Arafat at their normal pace. If he finds a gap, he speeds up without harming anyone. He avoids what the ignorant do of speeding, crowding, and harming, for that is haram. He then comes to Muzdalifah and descends near the mountain of Quzah, and he stays away from the bottom of the valley to make space for passersby. He prays Maghrib and Isha there with one adhan and one iqamah. If he prays a supererogatory between them or busies himself, he repeats the iqamah. Maghrib is not valid on the way to Muzdalifah, and he must repeat it before Fajr. It is sunnah to spend the night at Muzdalifah. When dawn breaks, the Imam leads the people in Fajr early in darkness. Then he stands with the people. All of Muzdalifah is a standing place except the bottom of Muhassir. He stands striving in his supplication, and asks Allah to fulfill his desire and request in this standing as He fulfilled for our master Muhammad (peace be upon him). When it becomes very bright, the Imam and the people depart before sunrise. He comes to Mina and stays there. Then he comes to Jamrat al-Aqaba and stabs it from the bottom of the valley with seven pebbles like pebbles of pottery. It is mustahabb to take the jamarat from Muzdalifah or from the road. It is makruh to take them from near the jamrah. It is makruh to shoot from above the Aqaba because it causes harm to people. He picks them up one by one, and does not break stones. He washes them to be sure of their purity, for a good deed is performed with them. If he shoots with an impure object, it suffices him but it is makruh. He stops talbiyah with the first pebble he throws. The manner of throwing is that he takes the pebble with the tip of his thumb and index finger in the most correct view, because it is easier and more insulting to the devil. The sunnah is to throw with the right hand. He places the pebble on the back of his thumb and uses the forefinger to help. The distance between the thrower and the landing place should be five cubits. If it falls on the back of a person or a place and sticks, he repeats it. If it falls in its normal path, it suffices. He says takbir with each pebble. Then the one performing Hajj al-Ifrad slaughters an animal if he wishes. Then he shaves or shortens, and shaving is better. It is sufficient to shave a quarter of the head. Shortening is to take from... Footnotes: (1) It is a valley beside Arafat to the left of the standing place, and the devil appeared there, and it was commanded that no one stand there. (2) Meaning like one who asks for food, his posture is like a beggar. (3) It is so called because the elephant (i.e., the army of the elephant) grew tired and exhausted there, so it is not permissible to stand there. (4) Narrated from Abu Hurairah (may Allah be pleased with him) who said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'O Allah, forgive those who shave.' They said: O Messenger of Allah, and those who shorten? He said: 'O Allah, forgive those who shave,' three times. They said: O Messenger of Allah, and those who shorten? He said: 'And those who shorten.' Reported by Bukhari in Hajj, Chapter on Shaving and Shortening (1728).
Source pages p. 694

Commentary
This passage from Imdad al-Fattah outlines the sequential rites of Hajj from the 8th of Dhul Hijjah. After sa'i, the pilgrim stays in Mecca as a muhrim, performing voluntary tawaf which is considered better than voluntary prayer for the afaqi. On the 8th, after Fajr, he proceeds to Mina, arriving after sunrise. Zuhr is recommended in Mina. Talbiyah is maintained except during tawaf. After spending the night, he performs Fajr in darkness and then proceeds to Arafat after sunrise. At Arafat, he goes to Namirah Mosque, where the Imam delivers two sermons and leads Zuhr and Asr combined, subject to two conditions: being in ihram and following the Imam (or his deputy). If unable to join the Imam, each prayer is offered at its own time. After the combined prayer, he proceeds to the standing place. The entire plain of Arafat is valid except Batn 'Uranah, where standing is prohibited. Ghusl before standing is recommended. Standing near Jabal al-Rahmah, facing the Qibla, with raised hands like a beggar, is described with emphasis on earnest supplication and tears as a sign of acceptance. After sunset, the departure (ifadah) to Muzdalifah is done calmly, but one may speed up without harming others. Crowding and harming are haram. At Muzdalifah, he descends near Jabal Quzah, avoiding the valley floor to allow passage. Maghrib and Isha are prayed together with one adhan and one iqamah; any supererogatory between them requires repeating the iqamah. Maghrib performed en route is invalid and must be repeated before Fajr. Spending the night at Muzdalifah is sunnah. After Fajr in darkness, the Imam leads the prayer, then they stand in supplication until just before sunrise (isfar). All of Muzdalifah is a valid standing place except Batn Muhassir. Then they proceed to Mina before sunrise for the stoning of Jamrat al-Aqaba, performed with seven smooth pebbles from the valley floor. It is mustahabb to collect pebbles from Muzdalifah or the road, but makruh to take them from near the jamrah. Throwing from above is makruh due to harm. Pebbles should be washed for purity; throwing with najis suffices but is makruh. Talbiyah ends with the first pebble. The method described involves thumb and index finger, right hand, with a five-cubit distance. After stoning, the ifrad pilgrim may sacrifice, then shave or shorten hair. Shaving is better, and it suffices to shave a quarter of the head. The footnote provides the hadith supporting the preference for shaving over shortening.

Key Terms
عرفة (Arafat): The plain where pilgrims stand on the 9th of Dhul Hijjah; all of it is a valid standing place except Batn 'Uranah.
مزدلفة (Muzdalifah): The area between Arafat and Mina where pilgrims spend the night after ifadah; all of it is a standing place except Batn Muhassir.
جمرة العقبة (Jamrat al-Aqaba): The large pillar representing the devil, stoned on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah with seven pebbles.
الحلق (al-halq): Shaving the head as a rite of Hajj; considered more virtuous than shortening.
التقصير (al-taqsir): Shortening the hair, sufficient to remove at least a quarter of the head's hair.
التلبية (al-talbiyah): The recitation of 'Labbayk Allahumma Labbayk...' which is maintained until the first stoning of Jamrat al-Aqaba.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When does the pilgrim stop reciting talbiyah?
A) At the beginning of tawaf
B) At the stoning of Jamrat al-Aqaba with the first pebble
C) After standing at Arafat
D) Upon entering Mina

Key Takeaway
The Hajj rites from the 8th to the 10th are sequential and include specific conditions for combining prayers, valid standing areas, and the recommendation to shave rather than shorten.

Standing at Arafat: Conditions and Rites
Describes the standing at Arafat and its conditions, including the exception of Batn 'Urnah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for valid standing (wuquf) at Arafat, identify the prohibited area (Batn 'Urnah), and list the recommended actions during the standing.

Core Idea
All of Arafat is a valid standing place except Batn 'Urnah; the standing is a pillar of Hajj.

This lesson covers the central rite of Hajj: the standing at Arafat on the 9th of Dhul Hijjah. The passage from Nur al-Idah details the conditions for a valid standing, the actions to be performed, and the proper conduct. Understanding these details ensures the pilgrim's Hajj is sound and accepted.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
The passage states that standing (wuquf) at Arafat is a central rite. Recognize that it is a pillar (rukn) of Hajj – missing it invalidates the pilgrimage.
Hanafi school: wuquf is fard (rukn).
2
Note the exception – Batn 'Urnah
The text explicitly excludes the valley of Batn 'Urnah. A pilgrim standing there has not performed the rite at Arafat.
This area is well-known; standing there is invalid.
3
List the conditions and recommended actions
The text mentions conditions: time (after zawal until sunset), location (within Arafat excluding Batn 'Urnah), and actions: ghusl, facing qiblah, supplication, etc.
Distinguish between obligatory (shurut/arkan) and recommended (sunan).
4
Understand the departure (ifada)
At sunset, the imam and pilgrims depart calmly. This marks the end of the standing and the beginning of the journey to Muzdalifah.
Haste and crowding are prohibited as they cause harm.

ويتوجه إلى الموقف، وعرفات كلها موقف إلا بطن عُرنة (وهو واد بحذاء عرفات عن يسار الموقف وقد رأى الشيطان فيه وأمر أن لا يقف فيه أحد. ط)، ويغتسل بعد الزوال في عرفات للوقوف، ويقف بقرب جبل الرحمة، مستقبلاً مكبراً مهللاً ملبياً داعياً، ماداً يديه كالمُسْتَطْعِم (أي: كالذي يطلب الطعام وهيئته كالدعي. ط). ويجتهد في الدعاء لنفسه ووالديه وإخوانه. ويجتهد على أن يخرج من عينيه قطرات من الدمع فإنه دليل القبول، ويلح في الدعاء مع قوة رجاء الإجابة، ولا يَقَصِّرُ في هذا اليوم، إذ لا يمكنه تداركه، سيما إذا كان من الآفاق، والوقوف على الراحلة أفضل، والقائم على الأرض أفضل من القاعد، فإذا غربت الشمس أفاض الإمام والناس معه على هَيْنَتِهِمْ. وإذا وجد فرجة يسرع من غير أن يؤذي أحداً، ويحترز مما يفعله الجهلة من الاشتداد في السير والازدحام والإيذاء فإنه حرام حتى يأتي مزدلفة فينزل بقرب جبل قُزَح، ويرتفع عن بطن الوادي توسعة للمارين، ويصلي بها المغرب والعشاء بأذان واحد، وإقامة واحدة ولو تطوع بينهما، أو تشاغل، أعاد الإقامة، ولم تجز المغرب في طريق المزدلفة، وعليه إعادتها ما لم يطلع الفجر ويسنُ المبيت بالمزدلفة، فإذا طلع الفجر صلى الإمام بالناس الفجر بغلس، ثم يقف والناس معه، والمزدلفة كلها موقف إلا بطن محسر (سمي به لأن الفيل [أصحاب الفيل] حسر وأعيا فيه فلا يجوز الوقوف فيه. ط) ويقف مجتهداً في دعائه، ويدعو الله أن يتم مراده وسؤله في هذا الموقف كما أتمه لسيدنا محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم
He proceeds to the standing place, and all of Arafat is a standing place except Batn 'Urnah, and he performs ghusl after zawal in Arafat for the standing, and he stands near the Mountain of Mercy, facing the qiblah, saying takbir, tahlil, talbiyah, supplicating, extending his hands like a beggar. And he strives in supplication for himself, his parents, and his brothers. And he strives to bring out drops of tears from his eyes, for it is a sign of acceptance, and he persists in supplication with strong hope of response, and he does not fall short on this day, for he cannot make it up, especially if he is from the distant horizons. And standing on a mount is better, and standing on the ground is better than sitting. When the sun sets, the imam and the people depart with them in a calm manner. And if he finds an opening, he hurries without harming anyone, and he avoids what the ignorant do of speeding, crowding, and harming, for it is haram, until he comes to Muzdalifah, and he stays near Mount Quzah, and he rises above the valley floor to give space to passersby, and he prays in it Maghrib and 'Isha with one adhan and one iqamah; even if he prays nafl between them or occupies himself, he repeats the iqamah. And Maghrib is not valid on the way to Muzdalifah, and he must repeat it if he did not see the dawn. And it is sunnah to spend the night in Muzdalifah. When dawn breaks, the imam leads the people in Fajr prayer in darkness, then he stands with the people, and all of Muzdalifah is a standing place except Batn Muhassir. And he stands striving in his supplication, and he beseeches Allah to complete his desire and request in this standing as He completed it for our master Muhammad (peace be upon him).
Source pages p. 694

Commentary
This is a ruling_statement passage from the Hanafi manual on Hajj, detailing the rites of Arafat and Muzdalifah. The passage begins by stating that all of Arafat is a valid place for the standing (wuquf) except Batn 'Urnah, a valley on the left side of the standing place; standing there is invalid. The pilgrim should perform ghusl before zawal (noon) in preparation for the standing. He should stand near the Mountain of Mercy facing the qiblah, engaging in takbir, tahlil, talbiyah, and supplication with raised hands like a beggar. Emphasis is placed on earnest supplication, tears, and persistence. Standing on a mount is recommended but standing on the ground is better. At sunset, the imam and people proceed calmly to Muzdalifah, avoiding harm. In Muzdalifah, they pray Maghrib and 'Isha with one adhan and one iqamah; any nafl between them requires repetition of iqamah. Praying Maghrib on the way is invalid and must be repeated before dawn. Spending the night in Muzdalifah is sunnah. Before Fajr, the imam prays Fajr with them in darkness, then they stand supplicating. All of Muzdalifah is a standing place except Batn Muhassir (where the elephant army failed).

Key Terms
عرفة ('Arafat): The plain near Mecca where pilgrims stand on the 9th of Dhul Hijjah; the entire area is a standing place except Batn 'Urnah.
بطن عرنة (Batn 'Urnah): A valley adjacent to Arafat on the left side of the standing place; standing there is invalid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Standing at Arafat is a pillar of Hajj; it must be performed within the valid boundaries (excluding Batn 'Urnah) from noon to sunset, with accompanying sunan acts.

Rites of Muzdalifah: Prayer, Standing, and Exclusions
Describes the rites at Muzdalifah: prayer, night stay, and standing, including the exception of Batn Muhassir.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the rites performed at Muzdalifah, including the combined prayer, the night stay, and the standing, and identify the excluded area (Batn Muhassir).

Core Idea
Muzdalifah is a place of combined prayer and standing; all of it is valid except Batn Muhassir.

After departing Arafat, pilgrims proceed to Muzdalifah for a sequence of rites: combining Maghrib and 'Isha prayers, spending the night, and standing after Fajr. This lesson from Nur al-Idah outlines the proper performance and warns against common errors.

Guided Path
1
Identify the arrival and prayer at Muzdalifah
Upon arriving, the pilgrim stays near Mount Quzah and prays Maghrib and 'Isha together with one adhan and one iqamah. If he prays nafl between them, he must repeat the iqamah.
Praying Maghrib on the way is invalid and must be repeated before dawn.
2
Understand the night stay
Spending the night (mabit) in Muzdalifah is sunnah muakkadah (emphasized sunnah).
It is not wajib but recommended.
3
Note the Fajr prayer and standing
Before dawn, the imam leads Fajr prayer in darkness, then the pilgrims stand for supplication. All of Muzdalifah is a valid standing place except Batn Muhassir.
Batn Muhassir is where the elephant army (Ashab al-Fil) perished.
4
Recognize the exception – Batn Muhassir
The text explicitly excludes Batn Muhassir from the valid standing area. Standing there is invalid.
This valley is avoided.

ويتوجه إلى الموقف، وعرفات كلها موقف إلا بطن عُرنة (وهو واد بحذاء عرفات عن يسار الموقف وقد رأى الشيطان فيه وأمر أن لا يقف فيه أحد. ط)، ويغتسل بعد الزوال في عرفات للوقوف، ويقف بقرب جبل الرحمة، مستقبلاً مكبراً مهللاً ملبياً داعياً، ماداً يديه كالمُسْتَطْعِم (أي: كالذي يطلب الطعام وهيئته كالدعي. ط). ويجتهد في الدعاء لنفسه ووالديه وإخوانه. ويجتهد على أن يخرج من عينيه قطرات من الدمع فإنه دليل القبول، ويلح في الدعاء مع قوة رجاء الإجابة، ولا يَقَصِّرُ في هذا اليوم، إذ لا يمكنه تداركه، سيما إذا كان من الآفاق، والوقوف على الراحلة أفضل، والقائم على الأرض أفضل من القاعد، فإذا غربت الشمس أفاض الإمام والناس معه على هَيْنَتِهِمْ. وإذا وجد فرجة يسرع من غير أن يؤذي أحداً، ويحترز مما يفعله الجهلة من الاشتداد في السير والازدحام والإيذاء فإنه حرام حتى يأتي مزدلفة فينزل بقرب جبل قُزَح، ويرتفع عن بطن الوادي توسعة للمارين، ويصلي بها المغرب والعشاء بأذان واحد، وإقامة واحدة ولو تطوع بينهما، أو تشاغل، أعاد الإقامة، ولم تجز المغرب في طريق المزدلفة، وعليه إعادتها ما لم يطلع الفجر ويسنُ المبيت بالمزدلفة، فإذا طلع الفجر صلى الإمام بالناس الفجر بغلس، ثم يقف والناس معه، والمزدلفة كلها موقف إلا بطن محسر (سمي به لأن الفيل [أصحاب الفيل] حسر وأعيا فيه فلا يجوز الوقوف فيه. ط) ويقف مجتهداً في دعائه، ويدعو الله أن يتم مراده وسؤله في هذا الموقف كما أتمه لسيدنا محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم
He proceeds to the standing place, and all of Arafat is a standing place except Batn 'Urnah, and he performs ghusl after zawal in Arafat for the standing, and he stands near the Mountain of Mercy, facing the qiblah, saying takbir, tahlil, talbiyah, supplicating, extending his hands like a beggar. And he strives in supplication for himself, his parents, and his brothers. And he strives to bring out drops of tears from his eyes, for it is a sign of acceptance, and he persists in supplication with strong hope of response, and he does not fall short on this day, for he cannot make it up, especially if he is from the distant horizons. And standing on a mount is better, and standing on the ground is better than sitting. When the sun sets, the imam and the people depart with them in a calm manner. And if he finds an opening, he hurries without harming anyone, and he avoids what the ignorant do of speeding, crowding, and harming, for it is haram, until he comes to Muzdalifah, and he stays near Mount Quzah, and he rises above the valley floor to give space to passersby, and he prays in it Maghrib and 'Isha with one adhan and one iqamah; even if he prays nafl between them or occupies himself, he repeats the iqamah. And Maghrib is not valid on the way to Muzdalifah, and he must repeat it if he did not see the dawn. And it is sunnah to spend the night in Muzdalifah. When dawn breaks, the imam leads the people in Fajr prayer in darkness, then he stands with the people, and all of Muzdalifah is a standing place except Batn Muhassir. And he stands striving in his supplication, and he beseeches Allah to complete his desire and request in this standing as He completed it for our master Muhammad (peace be upon him).
Source pages p. 694

Commentary
This is a ruling_statement passage from the Hanafi manual on Hajj, detailing the rites of Arafat and Muzdalifah. The passage begins by stating that all of Arafat is a valid place for the standing (wuquf) except Batn 'Urnah, a valley on the left side of the standing place; standing there is invalid. The pilgrim should perform ghusl before zawal (noon) in preparation for the standing. He should stand near the Mountain of Mercy facing the qiblah, engaging in takbir, tahlil, talbiyah, and supplication with raised hands like a beggar. Emphasis is placed on earnest supplication, tears, and persistence. Standing on a mount is recommended but standing on the ground is better. At sunset, the imam and people proceed calmly to Muzdalifah, avoiding harm. In Muzdalifah, they pray Maghrib and 'Isha with one adhan and one iqamah; any nafl between them requires repetition of iqamah. Praying Maghrib on the way is invalid and must be repeated before dawn. Spending the night in Muzdalifah is sunnah. Before Fajr, the imam prays Fajr with them in darkness, then they stand supplicating. All of Muzdalifah is a standing place except Batn Muhassir (where the elephant army failed).

Key Terms
مزدلفة (Muzdalifah): A place between Arafat and Mina where pilgrims spend the night and stand after Fajr; all of it is a standing place except Batn Muhassir.
بطن محسر (Batn Muhassir): A valley where the elephant army failed; standing there is invalid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the sunnah regarding staying in Muzdalifah?
A) Wajib
B) Sunnah
C) Haram
D) Makruh

Key Takeaway
Muzdalifah combines prayer and standing; the key sunnah acts include combining Maghrib and 'Isha, spending the night, and standing after Fajr, while avoiding Batn Muhassir.

Hajj — Pilgrimage

Ramy al-Jamrat al-Aqaba: Rules and Details
Describes the rites after Muzdalifah: ramy of Jamrat al-Aqaba and details of pebbles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the correct method of throwing Jamrat al-Aqaba and state the conditions that validate or require repetition of the throw.

Core Idea
The first rami at Mina initiates partial release from ihram; proper pebble selection and method ensure validity.

After departing Muzdalifah at dawn, the pilgrim proceeds to Mina to perform the first essential rite: throwing Jamrat al-Aqaba. This lesson details the rules for pebbles, the recommended throwing technique, and the circumstances under which a throw must be repeated. Understanding these details protects the pilgrim from inadvertent invalidity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the time and location
This rami is performed on the morning of the 10th of Dhul Hijjah, just after dawn, at the bottom of the valley near Jamrat al-Aqaba.
The imam leads the departure from Muzdalifah before sunrise.
2
Describe the required pebbles
Seven pebbles, like pottery pebbles, preferably taken from Muzdalifah or the road. They should be washed, picked individually, and not broken.
Taking from near the jamrah is disliked; throwing with impurity suffices but is disliked.
3
Explain the recommended throwing method
Hold the pebble with thumb and forefinger (the most correct view), throw with the right hand, and say takbir with each pebble. Distance from the landing spot: five cubits.
This is the sunnah method; thumb and forefinger are more insulting to Shaytan.
4
Understand the ruling on pebble landing
If the pebble lands on a person or surface and sticks, the throw must be repeated. If it falls on its side without sticking, it suffices.
This applies to all jamrahs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإذا أسفر جداً أفاض الإمام والناس قبل طلوع الشمس، فيأتي إلى مِنَى وينزل بها، ثم يأتي جمرة العقبة فيرميها من بطن الوادي بسبع حصيات مثل حصى الخزف ويستحب أخذ الجمار من المزدلفة أو من الطريق. ويكره من الذي عند الجمرة. ويكره الرمي من أعلى العقبة لإيذائه الناس، ويلتقطها التقاطاً، ولا یکسر حجراً حِمَارَاً، ويغسلها ليتيقن طهارتها فإنها يقام بها قربة، ولـو رمـى بنجسة أجزأه وكره، ويقطع التلبية مع أول حصاة يرميها. وكيفية الرمي أن يأخذ الحصاة بطرف إبهامه وسبابته في الأصح، لأنه أيسر وأكثر إهانة للشيطان. والمسنون الرمي باليد اليمنى، ويضع الحصاة على ظهر إبهامه، ويستعين بالمُسَبَّحَةِ، ويكون بين الرامي وموضع السقوط خمسة أذرع. ولو وقعت على ظهر رجل أو محل وثبتت أعادها، وإن سقطت على سننها ذلك أجزأه ، وكبر بكل حصاة، ثم يذبح المفرد بالحج إن أحبه، ثم يحلق أو يقصر والحلق أفضل)، ويكفي فيه ربع الرأس، والتقصير أن يأخذ من رؤوس شعره مقدار الأنملة، وقد حلَّ له كل شيء إلا النساء، ثم يأتي مكة من يومه ذلك، أو من الغد، أو بعده، فيطوف بالبيت طواف الزيارة سبعة أشواط، وحلت له النساء، وأفضل هذه الأيـام أولها، وإن أخره عنها لزمه شاة لتأخير الواجب، ثم يعود إلى مِنَى فيقيم بها. فإذا زالت الشمس مـن اليوم الثاني من أيام النحر رمي الجمار الثلاث، يبدأ بالجمرة التي تلي مسجد الخيف، فيرميها بسبع حصیات ماشياً، يكبر بكل حصاة، ثم يقف عندها داعياً بما أحب، وحامداً لله تعالى، مصلياً عـلـى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ، ويرفع يديه في الدعاء، ويستغفر لوالديه وإخوانه المؤمنين، ثم يرمي الثانية التي تليها مثل ذلك ويقف عندها داعياً، ثم يرمي جمرة العقبة راكباً ولا يقف عندها، فإذا كان اليوم الثالث من أيام النحر رمي الجمار الثلاث بعد الزوال كذلك. وإذا أراد أن يتعجل نَفَرَ إلى مكة قبل غروب الشمس، وإن أقام إلى الغروب كره، وليس عليه شيء، وإن طلع الفجر وهو يمنى في الرابع لـزمـه الرمي، وجاز قبل الزوال، والأفضل بعده، وكره قبل طلوع الشمس، وكل رمي بعده رمي ترميه ماشياً لتدعو بعده، وإلا راكباً لتذهب عَقِبَهُ بلا دعاء، وكره المبيت بغير مِنَى ليالي الرمي، ثم إذا رحل إلى مكة نزل بالمُحَصَّبِ ساعة، ثم يدخل مكة، ويطوف بالبيت سبعة أشواط بلا رمل، وسعى إن قدمهما، وهذا طواف الوداع، ويسمى أيضاً طواف الصدر، وهذا واجب إلا على أهـل مكـة ومـن أقام بـها، ويصلي بعده ركعتين، ثم يأتي زمزم فيشرب من مائها، ويستخرج الماء منها بنفسه إن قدر، ويستقبل البيت، ويتضلع منه ، ويتنفس فيه مراراً، ويرفع بصره كل مرة ينظر إلى البيت، ويصب على جسده إن تيسر، وإلا يمسح به وجهه ورأسه، وينوي بشربه ماشاء. وكان ابن عباس – رضي الله عنهما – إذا شربه يقول: « اللهم إني أسألك علماً نافعاً، ورزقاً واسعاً، وشفاء من كل داء » (أخرجه الحاكم في المستدرك (٦٤٦/١)، وعبد الرزاق في مصنفه (١١٣/٥)) . وقال صلى الله عليه وسلم : «ماءُ زمزم لما شرب له (أخرجه ابن ماجه في المناسك، باب: الشرب من زمزم (٣٠٦٢) ، وأحمد في مسنده (٣٥٧/٣))». ويستحب بعد شربه أن يأتي باب الكعبة ويقبل العتبة، ثم يأتي إلى الملتزم، وهو ما بين الحجر الأسود والباب فيضع صدره ووجهه عليه، ويتشبث بأستار الكعبة ساعة، يتضرع الله تعالى بالدعاء بما أحب من أمور الدارين، ويقول: اللهم إن هذا بيتك الذي جعلته مباركاً إلى وهدى للعالمين. اللهم كما هديتني له فتقبل مني، ولا تجعل هذا آخر العهد مـن بيتك، وارزقـنـي الـعــود إليه حتى ترضى عني برحمتك يا أرحم الراحمين. والملتزم من الأماكن التي يستجاب فيها الدعاء بمكة (روي عن ابن عباس رضي الله عنهما مرفوعاً)
When it becomes very bright, the imam and the people depart before sunrise, then he comes to Mina and stays there, then he comes to Jamrat al-Aqaba and throws it from the bottom of the valley with seven pebbles like pebbles of pottery. It is recommended to take the pebbles from Muzdalifah or from the road. It is disliked to take them from near the jamrah. It is disliked to throw from above al-Aqaba due to harming people. He picks them up one by one, and does not break a stone. He washes them to be sure of their purity, for the act is performed as worship. If he throws with impurity, it suffices but is disliked. He stops the talbiyah with the first pebble he throws. The method of throwing is to take the pebble with the tip of the thumb and forefinger in the most correct view, because it is easier and more insulting to the devil. The sunnah is to throw with the right hand, placing the pebble on the back of the thumb, and using the index finger. The distance between the thrower and the landing spot is five cubits. If it lands on a man's back or a place and sticks, he repeats it. If it falls on its side without sticking, it suffices. He says takbir with each pebble. Then the pilgrim performing ifrad sacrifices if he wishes, then shaves or shortens, and shaving is better, and it suffices to shave a quarter of the head. Shortening is to take from the ends of his hair the length of a fingertip. Then everything becomes lawful for him except women. Then he comes to Mecca on that day or the next or after, and performs tawaf al-ziyarah of the House seven circuits, and women become lawful for him. The best of these days is the first. If he delays it beyond them, a sheep becomes obligatory for delaying the wajib. Then he returns to Mina and stays there. When the sun declines on the second day of the days of sacrifice, he throws the three jamrahs, starting with the jamrah nearest to the Masjid al-Khayf, throwing seven pebbles walking, saying takbir with each pebble, then stands supplicating as he wishes, praising Allah and sending blessings on the Prophet, raising his hands in supplication, and asking forgiveness for his parents and believing brothers. Then he throws the second one similarly and stands supplicating. Then he throws Jamrat al-Aqaba riding and does not stand there. On the third day of the days of sacrifice, he throws the three jamrahs after zawal similarly. If he wants to hasten, he departs to Mecca before sunset; if he stays until sunset, it is disliked, and nothing is upon him. If dawn breaks while he is in Mina on the fourth day, throwing becomes obligatory, and it is permissible before zawal, and better after, and disliked before sunrise. Every throwing after that, he should throw walking so that he supplicates after it, otherwise riding so that his trace goes without supplication. It is disliked to spend the nights of throwing elsewhere than Mina. Then when he departs to Mecca, he stops at al-Muhassab for a while, then enters Mecca and performs tawaf of the House seven circuits without raml, and sa'y if he came early with them. This is tawaf al-wada', also called tawaf al-sadr. This is wajib except for the people of Mecca and those who reside there. He prays two rak'ahs after it. Then he comes to Zamzam and drinks from its water, and draws water himself if able, faces the House, drinks to satiety, breathes many times, raises his gaze each time to the House, pours water on his body if possible, otherwise wipes his face and head, and intends with his drinking whatever he wishes. Ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with them) when he drank it said: 'O Allah, I ask You for beneficial knowledge, abundant provision, and healing from every disease.' And the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'The water of Zamzam is for whatever it is drunk for.' After drinking, it is recommended that he come to the door of the Ka'bah and kiss the threshold, then come to al-Multazam, which is between the Black Stone and the door, and place his chest and face on it, and cling to the curtains of the Ka'bah for a while, supplicating to Allah for whatever he wishes of the affairs of this world and the Hereafter, and say: 'O Allah, this is Your House which You have made blessed and a guidance for the worlds. O Allah, as You guided me to it, accept it from me, and do not make this the last of my visits to Your House, and grant me return to it until You are pleased with me, by Your mercy, O Most Merciful of the merciful.' Al-Multazam is among the places where supplication is answered in Mecca.
Source pages p. 694

Commentary
This ruling_statement passage covers the sequence of Hajj rites after departing Muzdalifah. At Mina, the pilgrim first throws Jamrat al-Aqaba from the valley floor with seven pebbles, preferably taken from Muzdalifah. He picks them individually, does not break them, and washes them. Throwing with impurity suffices but is disliked. Talbiyah ends with the first pebble. The method: using thumb and forefinger with right hand. If pebble lands on something and sticks, it must be repeated; otherwise it suffices. After ramy, the pilgrim sacrifices (if ifrad), then shaves or trims. Shaving is better and requires at least a quarter of the head. After this, everything becomes halal except women. Then he performs tawaf al-ziyarah in Mecca, which makes women halal. Delaying this tawaf beyond the days of sacrifice requires a penalty sacrifice. Then he returns to Mina for the days of tashreeq: on the 2nd day (after the 10th), he throws all three jamrahs after zawal, in order: the first (nearest Masjid al-Khayf) walking with supplication, the second similarly, then Jamrat al-Aqaba riding without stopping. On the 3rd day, he does the same. If hastening, he may leave Mina before sunset on the 13th; staying until sunset is disliked. If he remains until dawn of the 14th, throwing becomes obligatory. After completing Mina rites, he goes to Mecca, stops briefly at al-Muhassab, then performs tawaf al-wada' (seven circuits without raml, and sa'y if not done before). This tawaf is wajib except for residents of Mecca. After tawaf, he prays two rak'ahs and then goes to Zamzam, drinks to satiety, and may intend any good. He then goes to the door of Ka'bah, kisses the threshold, and clings to al-Multazam supplicating for worldly and Hereafter benefits.

Key Terms
جمرة العقبة (Jamrat al-Aqaba): The largest of the three stone pillars at Mina, thrown on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah and on subsequent days.
التلبية (Talbiyah): The chant 'Labbayk Allahumma labbayk...' recited during ihram; it stops with the first pebble of Jamrat al-Aqaba.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if a pebble lands on a man's back and stays there?
A) The throw is invalid and must be repeated.
B) The throw is valid and nothing is required.
C) The throw is makruh but suffices.
D) A penalty (dam) becomes obligatory.

Key Takeaway
The first ramy at Mina must be performed with seven clean pebbles thrown one by one; a stick requires a repeat.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
beginner
6 min
Sacrifice and Shaving: Tahallul Awwal
Describes the rites after ramy: optional sacrifice, shaving or trimming, and the first tahallul.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the rulings of sacrifice, shaving, and the state of partial tahallul after ramy.

Core Idea
After ramy, sacrifice and shaving release the pilgrim from most ihram prohibitions, but marital relations remain forbidden until tawaf.

The pilgrim's next actions after throwing Jamrat al-Aqaba are to sacrifice (if ifrad) and then to shave or trim his hair. This lesson clarifies the options for sacrifice, the minimum requirements for shaving/trimming, and the resulting tahallul (partial release). Understanding these steps ensures the pilgrim correctly transitions out of ihram.

Guided Path
1
Understand the sacrifice ruling
For the ifrad pilgrim, sacrifice is optional ('if he wishes'). For qiran and tamattu', it is obligatory in hajj.
This lesson focuses on the ifrad pilgrim as per the text.
2
Shave or trim the hair
Shaving (halaq) is better than trimming (taqsir). Shaving at least a quarter of the head suffices. Taqsir means to cut the hair to the length of a fingertip.
Shaving is recommended for men; women only trim.
3
Apply the partial tahallul
After shaving/trimming, everything becomes lawful except sexual relations with one's spouse. This is the first tahallul.
Marital relations become permissible only after tawaf al-ziyarah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

الذي عند الجمرة. ويكره الرمي من أعلى العقبة لإيذائه الناس، ويلتقطها التقاطاً، ولا یکسر حجراً حِمَارَاً، ويغسلها ليتيقن طهارتها فإنها يقام بها قربة، ولـو رمـى بنجسة أجزأه وكره، ويقطع التلبية مع أول والتقصير أن يأخذ من رؤوس شعره مقدار الأنملة، وقد حلَّ له كل شيء إلا النساء، ثم يأتي مكة من يومه ذلك، أو من الغد، أو بعده، فيطوف بالبيت طواف الزيارة سبعة أشواط، وحلت له النساء، وأفضل هذه الأيـام أولها، وإن أخره عنها لزمه شاة لتأخير الواجب، ثم يعود إلى مِنَى فيقيم بها. فإذا زالت الشمس مـن اليوم الثاني من أيام النحر رمي الجمار الثلاث، يبدأ بالجمرة التي تلي مسجد الخيف، فيرميها بسبع حصیات ماشياً، يكبر بكل حصاة، ثم يقف عندها داعياً بما أحب، وحامداً لله تعالى، مصلياً عـلـى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ، ويرفع يديه في الدعاء، ويستغفر لوالديه وإخوانه المؤمنين، ثم يرمي الثانية التي تليها مثل ذلك ويقف عندها داعياً، ثم يرمي جمرة العقبة راكباً ولا يقف عندها، فإذا كان اليوم الثالث من أيام النحر رمي الجمار الثلاث بعد الزوال كذلك. وإذا أراد أن يتعجل نَفَرَ إلى مكة قبل غروب الشمس، وإن أقام إلى الغروب كره، وليس عليه شيء، وإن طلع الفجر وهو يمنى في الرابع لـزمـه الرمي، وجاز قبل الزوال، والأفضل بعده، وكره قبل طلوع الشمس، وكل رمي بعده رمي ترميه ماشياً لتدعو بعده، وإلا راكباً لتذهب عَقِبَهُ بلا دعاء، وكره المبيت بغير مِنَى ليالي الرمي، ثم إذا رحل إلى مكة نزل بالمُحَصَّبِ ساعة، ثم يدخل مكة، ويطوف بالبيت سبعة أشواط بلا رمل، وسعى إن قدمهما، وهذا طواف الوداع، ويسمى أيضاً طواف الصدر، وهذا واجب إلا على أهـل مكـة ومـن أقام بـها، ويصلي بعده ركعتين، ثم يأتي زمزم فيشرب من مائها، ويستخرج الماء منها بنفسه إن قدر، ويستقبل البيت، ويتضلع منه ، ويتنفس فيه مراراً، ويرفع بصره كل مرة ينظر إلى البيت، ويصب على جسده إن تيسر، وإلا يمسح به وجهه ورأسه، وينوي بشربه ماشاء. وكان ابن عباس – رضي الله عنهما – إذا شربه يقول: « اللهم إني أسألك علماً نافعاً، ورزقاً واسعاً، وشفاء من كل داء » (أخرجه الحاكم في المستدرك (٦٤٦/١)، وعبد الرزاق في مصنفه (١١٣/٥)) . وقال صلى الله عليه وسلم : «ماءُ زمزم لما شرب له (أخرجه ابن ماجه في المناسك، باب: الشرب من زمزم (٣٠٦٢) ، وأحمد في مسنده (٣٥٧/٣))». ويستحب بعد شربه أن يأتي باب الكعبة ويقبل العتبة، ثم يأتي إلى الملتزم، وهو ما بين الحجر الأسود والباب فيضع صدره ووجهه عليه، ويتشبث بأستار الكعبة ساعة، يتضرع الله تعالى بالدعاء بما أحب من أمور الدارين، ويقول: اللهم إن هذا بيتك الذي جعلته مباركاً إلى وهدى للعالمين. اللهم كما هديتني له فتقبل مني، ولا تجعل هذا آخر العهد مـن بيتك، وارزقـنـي الـعــود إليه حتى ترضى عني برحمتك يا أرحم الراحمين. والملتزم من الأماكن التي يستجاب فيها الدعاء بمكة (روي عن ابن عباس رضي الله عنهما مرفوعاً)
When it becomes very bright, the imam and the people depart before sunrise, then he comes to Mina and stays there, then he comes to Jamrat al-Aqaba and throws it from the bottom of the valley with seven pebbles like pebbles of pottery. It is recommended to take the pebbles from Muzdalifah or from the road. It is disliked to take them from near the jamrah. It is disliked to throw from above al-Aqaba due to harming people. He picks them up one by one, and does not break a stone. He washes them to be sure of their purity, for the act is performed as worship. If he throws with impurity, it suffices but is disliked. He stops the talbiyah with the first pebble he throws. The method of throwing is to take the pebble with the tip of the thumb and forefinger in the most correct view, because it is easier and more insulting to the devil. The sunnah is to throw with the right hand, placing the pebble on the back of the thumb, and using the index finger. The distance between the thrower and the landing spot is five cubits. If it lands on a man's back or a place and sticks, he repeats it. If it falls on its side without sticking, it suffices. He says takbir with each pebble. Then the pilgrim performing ifrad sacrifices if he wishes, then shaves or shortens, and shaving is better, and it suffices to shave a quarter of the head. Shortening is to take from the ends of his hair the length of a fingertip. Then everything becomes lawful for him except women. Then he comes to Mecca on that day or the next or after, and performs tawaf al-ziyarah of the House seven circuits, and women become lawful for him. The best of these days is the first. If he delays it beyond them, a sheep becomes obligatory for delaying the wajib. Then he returns to Mina and stays there. When the sun declines on the second day of the days of sacrifice, he throws the three jamrahs, starting with the jamrah nearest to the Masjid al-Khayf, throwing seven pebbles walking, saying takbir with each pebble, then stands supplicating as he wishes, praising Allah and sending blessings on the Prophet, raising his hands in supplication, and asking forgiveness for his parents and believing brothers. Then he throws the second one similarly and stands supplicating. Then he throws Jamrat al-Aqaba riding and does not stand there. On the third day of the days of sacrifice, he throws the three jamrahs after zawal similarly. If he wants to hasten, he departs to Mecca before sunset; if he stays until sunset, it is disliked, and nothing is upon him. If dawn breaks while he is in Mina on the fourth day, throwing becomes obligatory, and it is permissible before zawal, and better after, and disliked before sunrise. Every throwing after that, he should throw walking so that he supplicates after it, otherwise riding so that his trace goes without supplication. It is disliked to spend the nights of throwing elsewhere than Mina. Then when he departs to Mecca, he stops at al-Muhassab for a while, then enters Mecca and performs tawaf of the House seven circuits without raml, and sa'y if he came early with them. This is tawaf al-wada', also called tawaf al-sadr. This is wajib except for the people of Mecca and those who reside there. He prays two rak'ahs after it. Then he comes to Zamzam and drinks from its water, and draws water himself if able, faces the House, drinks to satiety, breathes many times, raises his gaze each time to the House, pours water on his body if possible, otherwise wipes his face and head, and intends with his drinking whatever he wishes. Ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with them) when he drank it said: 'O Allah, I ask You for beneficial knowledge, abundant provision, and healing from every disease.' And the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'The water of Zamzam is for whatever it is drunk for.' After drinking, it is recommended that he come to the door of the Ka'bah and kiss the threshold, then come to al-Multazam, which is between the Black Stone and the door, and place his chest and face on it, and cling to the curtains of the Ka'bah for a while, supplicating to Allah for whatever he wishes of the affairs of this world and the Hereafter, and say: 'O Allah, this is Your House which You have made blessed and a guidance for the worlds. O Allah, as You guided me to it, accept it from me, and do not make this the last of my visits to Your House, and grant me return to it until You are pleased with me, by Your mercy, O Most Merciful of the merciful.' Al-Multazam is among the places where supplication is answered in Mecca.
Source pages p. 694

Commentary
This ruling_statement passage covers the sequence of Hajj rites after departing Muzdalifah. At Mina, the pilgrim first throws Jamrat al-Aqaba from the valley floor with seven pebbles, preferably taken from Muzdalifah. He picks them individually, does not break them, and washes them. Throwing with impurity suffices but is disliked. Talbiyah ends with the first pebble. The method: using thumb and forefinger with right hand. If pebble lands on something and sticks, it must be repeated; otherwise it suffices. After ramy, the pilgrim sacrifices (if ifrad), then shaves or trims. Shaving is better and requires at least a quarter of the head. After this, everything becomes halal except women. Then he performs tawaf al-ziyarah in Mecca, which makes women halal. Delaying this tawaf beyond the days of sacrifice requires a penalty sacrifice. Then he returns to Mina for the days of tashreeq: on the 2nd day (after the 10th), he throws all three jamrahs after zawal, in order: the first (nearest Masjid al-Khayf) walking with supplication, the second similarly, then Jamrat al-Aqaba riding without stopping. On the 3rd day, he does the same. If hastening, he may leave Mina before sunset on the 13th; staying until sunset is disliked. If he remains until dawn of the 14th, throwing becomes obligatory. After completing Mina rites, he goes to Mecca, stops briefly at al-Muhassab, then performs tawaf al-wada' (seven circuits without raml, and sa'y if not done before). This tawaf is wajib except for residents of Mecca. After tawaf, he prays two rak'ahs and then goes to Zamzam, drinks to satiety, and may intend any good. He then goes to the door of Ka'bah, kisses the threshold, and clings to al-Multazam supplicating for worldly and Hereafter benefits.

Key Terms
تحلل (Tahallul): The release from ihram restrictions; the first tahallul (after shaving) lifts most prohibitions except women.
الحلق (Halaq): Shaving of the head; it is a wajib act for men after ramy, and shaving at least a quarter of the head suffices.
التقصير (Taqsir): Trimming the hair to the length of a fingertip; it suffices for men who do not shave.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
After shaving, what remains forbidden for the pilgrim?
A) Wearing sewn clothes
B) Using perfume
C) Marital relations
D) Trimming nails

Key Takeaway
Sacrifice is optional for ifrad; shaving or trimming a quarter of the head fulfills the first tahallul, but women remain forbidden until tawaf.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
beginner
6 min
Tawaf al-Ziyarah and Return to Mina
Describes tawaf al-ziyarah, its timing, effect on tahallul, and penalty for delay.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the rulings of tawaf al-ziyarah, including its timing, effect on tahallul, and the penalty for delay.

Core Idea
Tawaf al-Ziyarah completes the second tahallul, making women halal; delaying it beyond the days of sacrifice incurs a penalty.

After the first tahallul, the pilgrim proceeds to Mecca to perform tawaf al-ziyarah (the obligatory tawaf). This act removes the final restriction (women) and can be performed on the 10th, 11th, or 12th of Dhul Hijjah. Delaying it beyond the days of sacrifice requires a sacrifice. This lesson covers the timing and effect of this essential rite.

Guided Path
1
Identify the time for tawaf al-ziyarah
After ramy, sacrifice, and shaving, the pilgrim goes to Mecca on the same day (10th) or the next day (11th or 12th). The best is the first day.
The pilgrim can delay up to the 12th; after that, a penalty applies.
2
Perform the tawaf
Circumambulate the Ka'bah seven times. This is tawaf al-ziyarah.
This tawaf is wajib (obligatory) in Hanafi fiqh.
3
Apply the second tahallul
After completing tawaf, marital relations become permissible. This is the second and complete tahallul.
No further restrictions remain; the pilgrim is completely out of ihram.

Source Text

فإذا أسفر جداً أفاض الإمام والناس قبل طلوع الشمس، فيأتي إلى مِنَى وينزل بها، ثم يأتي جمرة العقبة فيرميها من بطن الوادي بسبع حصيات مثل حصى الخزف ويستحب أخذ الجمار من المزدلفة أو من الطريق. ويكره من الذي عند الجمرة. ويكره الرمي من أعلى العقبة لإيذائه الناس، ويلتقطها التقاطاً، ولا یکسر حجراً حِمَارَاً، ويغسلها ليتيقن طهارتها فإنها يقام بها قربة، ولـو رمـى بنجسة أجزأه وكره، ويقطع التلبية مع أول حصاة يرميها. وكيفية الرمي أن يأخذ الحصاة بطرف إبهامه وسبابته في الأصح، لأنه أيسر وأكثر إهانة للشيطان. والمسنون الرمي باليد اليمنى، ويضع الحصاة على ظهر إبهامه، ويستعين بالمُسَبَّحَةِ، ويكون بين الرامي وموضع السقوط خمسة أذرع. ولو وقعت على ظهر رجل أو محل وثبتت أعادها، وإن سقطت على سننها ذلك أجزأه ، وكبر بكل حصاة، ثم يذبح المفرد بالحج إن أحبه، ثم يحلق أو يقصر والحلق أفضل)، ويكفي فيه ربع الرأس، Commentary
This ruling_statement passage covers the sequence of Hajj rites after departing Muzdalifah. Key Terms
طواف الزيارة (Tawaf al-Ziyarah): The obligatory tawaf performed on the 10th, 11th, or 12th of Dhul Hijjah, after which women become halal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the best day to perform tawaf al-ziyarah according to the text?
A) The 10th of Dhul Hijjah
B) The 11th of Dhul Hijjah
C) The 12th of Dhul Hijjah
D) The 13th of Dhul Hijjah

Key Takeaway
Tawaf al-ziyarah removes the final ihram restriction; delay until after the 12th requires a sacrifice.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
intermediate
10 min
The Days of Tashreeq: Rami of the Three Jamrahs
Describes the ramy of the three jamrahs on the days of tashreeq, including order, method, and hastening rules.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the procedure for throwing the three jamrahs on the days of tashreeq and state the options for hastening.

Core Idea
On the 11th and 12th (and optionally 13th) after zawal, the pilgrim throws all three jamrahs in order, walking for the first two and riding for the third.

After performing tawaf al-ziyarah and returning to Mina, the pilgrim spends the days of tashreeq (11th, 12th, and optionally 13th) engaged in ramy of the three jamrahs. This lesson details the order, method (walking vs riding), supplications, and the rules for hastening or staying. Mastering this ensures the pilgrim correctly fulfills this wajib obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the days and timing
The ramy of all three jamrahs occurs after zawal (noon) on the 11th and 12th of Dhul Hijjah. On the 13th, it is only if the pilgrim delays departure beyond sunset on the 12th.
The first jamrah is the one nearest to Masjid al-Khayf.
2
Perform the ramy in order
Start with the jamrah nearest Masjid al-Khayf (the small jamrah), then the middle jamrah, then Jamrat al-Aqaba. Throw seven pebbles at each, saying takbir.
The first two are thrown walking; Jamrat al-Aqaba is thrown riding.
3
Include supplication after first two
After throwing the first and second jamrah, the pilgrim stands, faces the qibla, and supplicates. No supplication after Jamrat al-Aqaba.
The text outlines the recommended posture and words.
4
Understand the hastening rule
If the pilgrim wishes to hasten (ta'ajjul), he may leave Mina before sunset on the 12th. If he stays until sunset, it is disliked but no penalty. If dawn breaks on the 13th while he is in Mina, ramy on the 13th becomes obligatory.
The preferred time for ramy on the 13th is after zawal, but it is permissible earlier.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإذا أسفر جداً أفاض الإمام والناس قبل طلوع الشمس، فيأتي إلى مِنَى وينزل بها، ثم يأتي جمرة العقبة فيرميها من بطن الوادي بسبع حصيات مثل حصى الخزف ويستحب أخذ الجمار من المزدلفة أو من الطريق. ويكره من الذي عند الجمرة. ويكره الرمي من أعلى العقبة لإيذائه الناس، ويلتقطها التقاطاً، ولا یکسر حجراً حِمَارَاً، ويغسلها ليتيقن طهارتها فإنها يقام بها قربة، ولـو رمـى بنجسة أجزأه وكره، ويقطع التلبية مع أول حصاة يرميها. وكيفية الرمي أن يأخذ الحصاة بطرف إبهامه وسبابته في الأصح، لأنه أيسر وأكثر إهانة للشيطان. والمسنون الرمي باليد اليمنى، ويضع الحصاة على ظهر إبهامه، ويستعين بالمُسَبَّحَةِ، ويكون بين الرامي وموضع السقوط خمسة أذرع. ولو وقعت على ظهر رجل أو محل وثبتت أعادها، وإن سقطت على سننها ذلك أجزأه ، وكبر بكل حصاة، ثم يذبح المفرد بالحج إن أحبه، ثم يحلق أو يقصر والحلق أفضل)، ويكفي فيه ربع الرأس، والتقصير أن يأخذ من رؤوس شعره مقدار الأنملة، وقد حلَّ له كل شيء إلا النساء، ثم يأتي مكة من يومه ذلك، أو من الغد، أو بعده، فيطوف بالبيت طواف الزيارة سبعة أشواط، وحلت له النساء، وأفضل هذه الأيـام أولها، وإن أخره عنها لزمه شاة لتأخير الواجب، ثم يعود إلى مِنَى فيقيم بها. فإذا زالت الشمس مـن اليوم الثاني من أيام النحر رمي الجمار الثلاث، يبدأ بالجمرة التي تلي مسجد الخيف، فيرميها بسبع حصیات ماشياً، يكبر بكل حصاة، ثم يقف عندها داعياً بما أحب، وحامداً لله تعالى، مصلياً عـلـى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ، ويرفع يديه في الدعاء، ويستغفر لوالديه وإخوانه المؤمنين، ثم يرمي الثانية التي تليها مثل ذلك ويقف عندها داعياً، ثم يرمي جمرة العقبة راكباً ولا يقف عندها، فإذا كان اليوم الثالث من أيام النحر رمي الجمار الثلاث بعد الزوال كذلك. وإذا أراد أن يتعجل نَفَرَ إلى مكة قبل غروب الشمس، وإن أقام إلى الغروب كره، وليس عليه شيء، وإن طلع الفجر وهو يمنى في الرابع لـزمـه الرمي، وجاز قبل الزوال، والأفضل بعده، وكره قبل طلوع الشمس، وكل رمي بعده رمي ترميه ماشياً لتدعو بعده، وإلا راكباً لتذهب عَقِبَهُ بلا دعاء، وكره المبيت بغير مِنَى ليالي الرمي، ثم إذا رحل إلى مكة نزل بالمُحَصَّبِ ساعة، ثم يدخل مكة، ويطوف بالبيت سبعة أشواط بلا رمل، وسعى إن قدمهما، وهذا طواف الوداع، ويسمى أيضاً طواف الصدر، وهذا واجب إلا على أهـل مكـة ومـن أقام بـها، ويصلي بعده ركعتين، ثم يأتي زمزم فيشرب من مائها، ويستخرج الماء منها بنفسه إن قدر، ويستقبل البيت، ويتضلع منه ، ويتنفس فيه مراراً، ويرفع بصره كل مرة ينظر إلى البيت، ويصب على جسده إن تيسر، وإلا يمسح به وجهه ورأسه، وينوي بشربه ماشاء. وكان ابن عباس – رضي الله عنهما – إذا شربه يقول: « اللهم إني أسألك علماً نافعاً، ورزقاً واسعاً، وشفاء من كل داء » (أخرجه الحاكم في المستدرك (٦٤٦/١)، وعبد الرزاق في مصنفه (١١٣/٥)) . وقال صلى الله عليه وسلم : «ماءُ زمزم لما شرب له (أخرجه ابن ماجه في المناسك، باب: الشرب من زمزم (٣٠٦٢) ، وأحمد في مسنده (٣٥٧/٣))». ويستحب بعد شربه أن يأتي باب الكعبة ويقبل العتبة، ثم يأتي إلى الملتزم، وهو ما بين الحجر الأسود والباب فيضع صدره ووجهه عليه، ويتشبث بأستار الكعبة ساعة، يتضرع الله تعالى بالدعاء بما أحب من أمور الدارين، ويقول: اللهم إن هذا بيتك الذي جعلته مباركاً إلى وهدى للعالمين. اللهم كما هديتني له فتقبل مني، ولا تجعل هذا آخر العهد مـن بيتك، وارزقـنـي الـعــود إليه حتى ترضى عني برحمتك يا أرحم الراحمين. والملتزم من الأماكن التي يستجاب فيها الدعاء بمكة (روي عن ابن عباس رضي الله عنهما مرفوعاً)
When it becomes very bright, the imam and the people depart before sunrise, then he comes to Mina and stays there, then he comes to Jamrat al-Aqaba and throws it from the bottom of the valley with seven pebbles like pebbles of pottery. It is recommended to take the pebbles from Muzdalifah or from the road. It is disliked to take them from near the jamrah. It is disliked to throw from above al-Aqaba due to harming people. He picks them up one by one, and does not break a stone. He washes them to be sure of their purity, for the act is performed as worship. If he throws with impurity, it suffices but is disliked. He stops the talbiyah with the first pebble he throws. The method of throwing is to take the pebble with the tip of the thumb and forefinger in the most correct view, because it is easier and more insulting to the devil. The sunnah is to throw with the right hand, placing the pebble on the back of the thumb, and using the index finger. The distance between the thrower and the landing spot is five cubits. If it lands on a man's back or a place and sticks, he repeats it. If it falls on its side without sticking, it suffices. He says takbir with each pebble. Then the pilgrim performing ifrad sacrifices if he wishes, then shaves or shortens, and shaving is better, and it suffices to shave a quarter of the head. Shortening is to take from the ends of his hair the length of a fingertip. Then everything becomes lawful for him except women. Then he comes to Mecca on that day or the next or after, and performs tawaf al-ziyarah of the House seven circuits, and women become lawful for him. The best of these days is the first. If he delays it beyond them, a sheep becomes obligatory for delaying the wajib. Then he returns to Mina and stays there. When the sun declines on the second day of the days of sacrifice, he throws the three jamrahs, starting with the jamrah nearest to the Masjid al-Khayf, throwing seven pebbles walking, saying takbir with each pebble, then stands supplicating as he wishes, praising Allah and sending blessings on the Prophet, raising his hands in supplication, and asking forgiveness for his parents and believing brothers. Then he throws the second one similarly and stands supplicating. Then he throws Jamrat al-Aqaba riding and does not stand there. On the third day of the days of sacrifice, he throws the three jamrahs after zawal similarly. If he wants to hasten, he departs to Mecca before sunset; if he stays until sunset, it is disliked, and nothing is upon him. If dawn breaks while he is in Mina on the fourth day, throwing becomes obligatory, and it is permissible before zawal, and better after, and disliked before sunrise. Every throwing after that, he should throw walking so that he supplicates after it, otherwise riding so that his trace goes without supplication. It is disliked to spend the nights of throwing elsewhere than Mina. Then when he departs to Mecca, he stops at al-Muhassab for a while, then enters Mecca and performs tawaf of the House seven circuits without raml, and sa'y if he came early with them. This is tawaf al-wada', also called tawaf al-sadr. This is wajib except for the people of Mecca and those who reside there. He prays two rak'ahs after it. Then he comes to Zamzam and drinks from its water, and draws water himself if able, faces the House, drinks to satiety, breathes many times, raises his gaze each time to the House, pours water on his body if possible, otherwise wipes his face and head, and intends with his drinking whatever he wishes. Ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with them) when he drank it said: 'O Allah, I ask You for beneficial knowledge, abundant provision, and healing from every disease.' And the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'The water of Zamzam is for whatever it is drunk for.' After drinking, it is recommended that he come to the door of the Ka'bah and kiss the threshold, then come to al-Multazam, which is between the Black Stone and the door, and place his chest and face on it, and cling to the curtains of the Ka'bah for a while, supplicating to Allah for whatever he wishes of the affairs of this world and the Hereafter, and say: 'O Allah, this is Your House which You have made blessed and a guidance for the worlds. O Allah, as You guided me to it, accept it from me, and do not make this the last of my visits to Your House, and grant me return to it until You are pleased with me, by Your mercy, O Most Merciful of the merciful.' Al-Multazam is among the places where supplication is answered in Mecca.
Source pages p. 694

Commentary
This ruling_statement passage covers the sequence of Hajj rites after departing Muzdalifah. At Mina, the pilgrim first throws Jamrat al-Aqaba from the valley floor with seven pebbles, preferably taken from Muzdalifah. He picks them individually, does not break them, and washes them. Throwing with impurity suffices but is disliked. Talbiyah ends with the first pebble. The method: using thumb and forefinger with right hand. If pebble lands on something and sticks, it must be repeated; otherwise it suffices. After ramy, the pilgrim sacrifices (if ifrad), then shaves or trims. Shaving is better and requires at least a quarter of the head. After this, everything becomes halal except women. Then he performs tawaf al-ziyarah in Mecca, which makes women halal. Delaying this tawaf beyond the days of sacrifice requires a penalty sacrifice. Then he returns to Mina for the days of tashreeq: on the 2nd day (after the 10th), he throws all three jamrahs after zawal, in order: the first (nearest Masjid al-Khayf) walking with supplication, the second similarly, then Jamrat al-Aqaba riding without stopping. On the 3rd day, he does the same. If hastening, he may leave Mina before sunset on the 13th; staying until sunset is disliked. If he remains until dawn of the 14th, throwing becomes obligatory. After completing Mina rites, he goes to Mecca, stops briefly at al-Muhassab, then performs tawaf al-wada' (seven circuits without raml, and sa'y if not done before). This tawaf is wajib except for residents of Mecca. After tawaf, he prays two rak'ahs and then goes to Zamzam, drinks to satiety, and may intend any good. He then goes to the door of Ka'bah, kisses the threshold, and clings to al-Multazam supplicating for worldly and Hereafter benefits.

Key Terms
جمرة العقبة (Jamrat al-Aqaba): The largest jamrah, thrown riding on the days of tashreeq, and no supplication after it.
أيام التشريق (Ayam al-Tashreeq): The 11th, 12th, and 13th of Dhul Hijjah; days of ramy, takbir, and sacrifice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
On which jamrah does the pilgrim stand to supplicate after throwing?
A) Only the first jamrah
B) The first and second jamrah
C) The third jamrah (Jamrat al-Aqaba)
D) All three jamrahs

Key Takeaway
On tashreeq days, throw first two jamrahs walking with du'a, and the third riding without du'a; hastening avoids the 13th day.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
beginner
