Tawaf al-Wada' and Farewell Rites
Describes tawaf al-wada', its ruling, exemptions, and recommended acts at Zamzam and al-Multazam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the rulings of tawaf al-wada', its exemptions, and the recommended sunan at Zamzam and al-Multazam.

Core Idea
Tawaf al-Wada' is wajib for non-Meccans; followed by blessed practices at Zamzam and supplication at al-Multazam.

As the pilgrim prepares to leave Mecca, the final obligatory rite is tawaf al-wada' (farewell tawaf). This lesson covers its ruling (wajib), who is exempt, and the beautiful sunan that follow: drinking Zamzam with intention, kissing the Ka'bah threshold, and clinging to al-Multazam for supplication. These acts complete the Hajj experience with devotion and hope for acceptance.

Guided Path
1
Understand the obligation of tawaf al-wada'
Tawaf al-wada' is wajib for every pilgrim who is not a resident of Mecca. It consists of seven circuits without raml, followed by sa'y if not already performed, and two rak'ahs.
This tawaf is also called tawaf al-sadr.
2
Perform the sunan at Zamzam
After tawaf, go to Zamzam, drink to satiety while facing the Ka'bah, and make intention for any good (e.g., beneficial knowledge, healing). Pour water on the body if possible.
The hadith 'Zamzam water is for whatever it is drunk for' is cited.
3
Proceed to the Ka'bah door and al-Multazam
Kiss the threshold, then go to al-Multazam (between Black Stone and door). Place chest and face on it, cling to the curtains, and supplicate for worldly and religious needs.
This is a place of answered supplication.

When it becomes very bright, the imam and the people depart before sunrise, then he comes to Mina and stays there, then he comes to Jamrat al-Aqaba and throws it from the bottom of the valley with seven pebbles like pebbles of pottery. It is recommended to take the pebbles from Muzdalifah or from the road. It is disliked to take them from near the jamrah. It is disliked to throw from above al-Aqaba due to harming people. He picks them up one by one, and does not break a stone. He washes them to be sure of their purity, for the act is performed as worship. If he throws with impurity, it suffices but is disliked. He stops the talbiyah with the first pebble he throws. The method of throwing is to take the pebble with the tip of the thumb and forefinger in the most correct view, because it is easier and more insulting to the devil. The sunnah is to throw with the right hand, placing the pebble on the back of the thumb, and using the index finger. The distance between the thrower and the landing spot is five cubits. If it lands on a man's back or a place and sticks, he repeats it. If it falls on its side without sticking, it suffices. He says takbir with each pebble. Then the pilgrim performing ifrad sacrifices if he wishes, then shaves or shortens, and shaving is better, and it suffices to shave a quarter of the head. Shortening is to take from the ends of his hair the length of a fingertip. Then everything becomes lawful for him except women. Then he comes to Mecca on that day or the next or after, and performs tawaf al-ziyarah of the House seven circuits, and women become lawful for him. The best of these days is the first. If he delays it beyond them, a sheep becomes obligatory for delaying the wajib. Then he returns to Mina and stays there. When the sun declines on the second day of the days of sacrifice, he throws the three jamrahs, starting with the jamrah nearest to the Masjid al-Khayf, throwing seven pebbles walking, saying takbir with each pebble, then stands supplicating as he wishes, praising Allah and sending blessings on the Prophet, raising his hands in supplication, and asking forgiveness for his parents and believing brothers. Then he throws the second one similarly and stands supplicating. Then he throws Jamrat al-Aqaba riding and does not stand there. On the third day of the days of sacrifice, he throws the three jamrahs after zawal similarly. If he wants to hasten, he departs to Mecca before sunset; if he stays until sunset, it is disliked, and nothing is upon him. If dawn breaks while he is in Mina on the fourth day, throwing becomes obligatory, and it is permissible before zawal, and better after, and disliked before sunrise. Every throwing after that, he should throw walking so that he supplicates after it, otherwise riding so that his trace goes without supplication. It is disliked to spend the nights of throwing elsewhere than Mina. Then when he departs to Mecca, he stops at al-Muhassab for a while, then enters Mecca and performs tawaf of the House seven circuits without raml, and sa'y if he came early with them. This is tawaf al-wada', also called tawaf al-sadr. This is wajib except for the people of Mecca and those who reside there. He prays two rak'ahs after it. Then he comes to Zamzam and drinks from its water, and draws water himself if able, faces the House, drinks to satiety, breathes many times, raises his gaze each time to the House, pours water on his body if possible, otherwise wipes his face and head, and intends with his drinking whatever he wishes. Ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with them) when he drank it said: 'O Allah, I ask You for beneficial knowledge, abundant provision, and healing from every disease.' And the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'The water of Zamzam is for whatever it is drunk for.' After drinking, it is recommended that he come to the door of the Ka'bah and kiss the threshold, then come to al-Multazam, which is between the Black Stone and the door, and place his chest and face on it, and cling to the curtains of the Ka'bah for a while, supplicating to Allah for whatever he wishes of the affairs of this world and the Hereafter, and say: 'O Allah, this is Your House which You have made blessed and a guidance for the worlds. O Allah, as You guided me to it, accept it from me, and do not make this the last of my visits to Your House, and grant me return to it until You are pleased with me, by Your mercy, O Most Merciful of the merciful.' Al-Multazam is among the places where supplication is answered in Mecca.
Source pages p. 694

Commentary
This ruling_statement passage covers the sequence of Hajj rites after departing Muzdalifah. At Mina, the pilgrim first throws Jamrat al-Aqaba from the valley floor with seven pebbles, preferably taken from Muzdalifah. He picks them individually, does not break them, and washes them. Throwing with impurity suffices but is disliked. Talbiyah ends with the first pebble. The method: using thumb and forefinger with right hand. If pebble lands on something and sticks, it must be repeated; otherwise it suffices. After ramy, the pilgrim sacrifices (if ifrad), then shaves or trims. Shaving is better and requires at least a quarter of the head. After this, everything becomes halal except women. Then he performs tawaf al-ziyarah in Mecca, which makes women halal. Delaying this tawaf beyond the days of sacrifice requires a penalty sacrifice. Then he returns to Mina for the days of tashreeq: on the 2nd day (after the 10th), he throws all three jamrahs after zawal, in order: the first (nearest Masjid al-Khayf) walking with supplication, the second similarly, then Jamrat al-Aqaba riding without stopping. On the 3rd day, he does the same. If hastening, he may leave Mina before sunset on the 13th; staying until sunset is disliked. If he remains until dawn of the 14th, throwing becomes obligatory. After completing Mina rites, he goes to Mecca, stops briefly at al-Muhassab, then performs tawaf al-wada' (seven circuits without raml, and sa'y if not done before). This tawaf is wajib except for residents of Mecca. After tawaf, he prays two rak'ahs and then goes to Zamzam, drinks to satiety, and may intend any good. He then goes to the door of Ka'bah, kisses the threshold, and clings to al-Multazam supplicating for worldly and Hereafter benefits.

Key Terms
طواف الوداع (Tawaf al-Wada'): The farewell tawaf performed before leaving Mecca, wajib except for residents.
الملتزم (al-Multazam): The area between the Black Stone and the Ka'bah door; a place where supplication is answered.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling for a non-Meccan pilgrim who omits tawaf al-wada'?
A) His Hajj is invalid.
B) He must repeat the Hajj.
C) He must sacrifice a sheep.
D) It is excused; no penalty.

Key Takeaway
Tawaf al-Wada' is wajib for non-Meccans; omitting it requires a sacrifice; the ensuing sunan enrich the farewell.

Recommended Acts and Etiquette of Entering the Kaaba
Lists recommended du'a locations and etiquette of entering Kaaba

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the fifteen recommended places for du'a and explain the etiquette of entering the Kaaba, distinguishing sunnah from innovation.

Core Idea
Fifteen sacred places for du'a; entering the Kaaba is a sunnah with specific etiquette; avoid baseless innovations.

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah lists auspicious locations for supplication during Hajj and details the recommended conduct for entering the Kaaba. It also warns against common innovations like the green slab and the nail. Understanding these recommendations enhances your pilgrimage with proper adab and protects you from bid'ah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the fifteen du'a locations
The passage lists fifteen places where supplication is recommended: during tawaf, at Multazam, under the water-spout, inside the House, at Zamzam, behind Maqam, on Safa, on Marwa, in sa'y, at Arafat, at Mina, and at the Jamarat (stoning over four days). Also upon seeing the House.
These are transmitted from Hasan al-Basri by Kamal ibn al-Humam.
2
Understand the etiquette of entering the Kaaba
Entering the Kaaba is recommended if it causes no harm. One should pray in the Prophet's designated spot: stand with the door behind, about three cubits from the front wall. Then pray, place cheek on the wall, seek forgiveness, go to corners, and glorify Allah.
The green slab between the columns is not the Prophet's prayer place.
3
Distinguish sunnah from innovation
The text refutes two innovations: (1) the green slab is not the Prophet's prayer place, (2) the so-called 'al-urwa al-wuthqa' on the wall and the 'navel of the world' nail are baseless. Uncovering oneself on that nail is an act of folly.
4
Note the farewell tawaf procedure
When leaving for home, one should perform farewell tawaf, then walk backwards facing the Kaaba, weeping, until exiting the mosque. Exit through the gate of Bani Shaybah from the lower hill.
This shows the deep attachment to the sacred house.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المشرفة، وهي خمسة عشر موضعاً، نقلها الكمال بن الهمام عن رسالة الحسن البصري - رحمه الله - بقوله: في الطواف، وعند الملتزم، وتحت الميزاب، وفي البيت، وعند زمزم، وخلف المقام، وعلى الصفا، وعلى المروة، وفي السعي، وفي عرفات، وفي منى، وعند الجمرات انتهى. والجمرات ترمى في أربعة أيام: يوم النحر وثلاثة بعده كما تقدم، وذكرنا استجابته أيضاً عند رؤية البيت المكرم. ويستحب دخول البيت الشريف المبارك إن لم يؤذ أحداً، وينبغي أن يقصد مصلى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فيه، وهو قبل وجهه، وقد جعل الباب قبل ظهره، حتى يكون بينه وبين الجدار الذي قبل وجهه قرب ثلاثة أذرع، ثم يصلي، فإذا صلى إلى الجدار يضع خده عليه، ويستغفر الله ويحمده، ثم يأتي الأركان، فيحمده ويهلل ويسبح ويكبر، ويسأل الله تعالى ما شاء، ويلزم الأدب ما استطاع بظاهره وباطنه. وليست البلاطة الخضراء التي بين العمودين مصلى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم، وما تقوله العامة من أن العروة الوثقى وهو موضع عال في جدار البيت بدعة باطلة لا أصل لها، والمسمار الذي في وسط البيت يسمونه سرة الدنيا، يكشف أحدهم عورته وسرته، ويضعها عليه، فعل من لا عقل له فضلاً عن علم... كما قاله الكمال. وإذا أراد العود إلى أهله ينبغي أن ينصرف بعد طوافه للوداع، وهو يمشي إلى ورائه ووجهه إلى البيت باكياً أو متباكياً متحسراً على فراق البيت حتى يخرج من المسجد، ويخرج من مكة من باب بني شيبة من الثنية السفلى. والمرأة في جميع أفعال الحج كالرجل، غير أنها لا تكشف رأسها، وتسدل على وجهها شيئاً تحته عيدان كالقبة تمنع مسه بالغطاء، ولا ترفع صوتها بالتلبية، ولا ترمل ولا تهرول في السعي بين الميلين الأخضرين، بل تمشي على هيئتها في جميع السعي بين الصفا والمروة، ولا تحلق وتقصر، وتلبس المخيط، ولا تزاحم الرجال في استلام الحجر. وهذا تمام حج المفرد، وهو دون المتمتع في الفضل، والقران أفضل من التمتع.
The honored places: they are fifteen locations, transmitted by Kamal ibn al-Humam from the treatise of Hasan al-Basri - may Allah have mercy on him - his statement: at the tawaf, and at the Multazam, and under the water-spout, and inside the House, and at Zamzam, and behind the Maqam, and on Safa, and on Marwa, and during the sa'y, and at Arafat, and at Mina, and at the Jamarat. End. And the Jamarat are stoned over four days: the Day of Sacrifice and three after as previously mentioned. And we mentioned its recommendation also at the sight of the honored House. And it is recommended to enter the blessed noble House if one does not harm anyone. And one should aim for the prayer place of the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, inside it, which is in front of his face, having made the door behind his back, so that there is about three cubits between him and the wall in front of his face, then he prays. When he prays towards the wall, he places his cheek on it, seeks forgiveness from Allah and praises Him. Then he goes to the corners, praises Him, says la ilaha illa Allah, glorifies Him, magnifies Him, and asks Allah Almighty for whatever he wishes, and adheres to proper conduct as much as he can outwardly and inwardly. And the green slab between the two columns is not the prayer place of the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace. And what the common people say that al-urwa al-wuthqa is a high place on the wall of the House is an innovation, false, with no basis. And the nail in the middle of the House they call the navel of the world, one of them uncovers his genitals and navel and places it on it, the act of one with no intellect, let alone knowledge... as Kamal said. And when he intends to return to his family, he should depart after his farewell tawaf, walking backwards with his face towards the House, weeping or pretending to weep, regretful at parting from the House, until he leaves the mosque, and he leaves Mecca from the gate of Bani Shaybah from the lower hill. And the woman is like the man in all actions of Hajj, except that she does not uncover her head, and she lets down over her face something with sticks under it like a dome to prevent its touch by the covering, and she does not raise her voice in talbiyah, and she does not do raml nor hurry in the sa'y between the two green markers, but walks at her normal pace throughout the sa'y between Safa and Marwah, and she does not shave but shortens, and she wears sewn garments, and she does not crowd men in kissing the Black Stone. And this completes the Hajj of ifrad, which is inferior in merit to tamattu', and qiran is better than tamattu'.
Source pages p. 696

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement covering several recommended acts and specific rulings in Hajj. It begins by listing fifteen recommended places for supplication during the pilgrimage, transmitted by Kamal ibn al-Humam from Hasan al-Basri, including during tawaf, at the Multazam, under the water-spout, inside the Kaaba, at Zamzam, etc. Stoning the Jamarat is over four days. Entering the Kaaba is recommended if it causes no harm. The author details the etiquette of entering: pray in the Prophet's designated spot, with the door behind, about three cubits from the front wall, then pray, place cheek on wall, seek forgiveness, go to corners, glorify Allah. Then he refutes two innovations: the green slab between columns is not the Prophet's prayer place, and the claim about 'al-urwa al-wuthqa' on the wall is baseless. Similarly, uncovering one's navel on the nail called 'navel of the world' is an act of folly. Next, the farewell tawaf: one should leave walking backwards facing the Kaaba, weeping, and exit through the lower gate of Bani Shaybah. Finally, women's rulings: they are like men in all Hajj acts except: they do not uncover their heads, they cover their faces with a dome-like veil that doesn't touch the face, they do not raise their voice in talbiyah, they do not do raml or hurrying in sa'y, they walk normally, they shorten hair instead of shaving, they wear sewn clothes, and they do not crowd men at the Black Stone. The passage concludes that ifrad Hajj is less meritorious than tamattu', and qiran is best. All these are relied-upon Hanafi positions.

Key Terms
الملتزم (al-multazam): The area between the Black Stone and the door of the Kaaba where supplication is recommended.
الميزاب (al-mizab): The water-spout of the Kaaba, located on the roof. Supplicating under it is recommended.
طواف الوداع (tawaf al-wada'): Farewell tawaf performed when leaving Mecca.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Women's Rulings in Hajj: Key Differences
Lists women-specific rulings in Hajj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the five specific rulings where women differ from men in Hajj according to the Hanafi school, and apply them to practical scenarios.

Core Idea
Women perform Hajj like men except in covering, voice, raml, hair removal, and sewn clothes.

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah clarifies that women are generally like men in all Hajj actions, but with specific exceptions to maintain modesty and avoid fitnah. Understanding these differences is crucial for female pilgrims and their companions to ensure correctness of rites.

Guided Path
1
State the general principle
The text begins: 'And the woman is like the man in all actions of Hajj.' This establishes equality in the basic rites.
2
List the exceptions for women
The exceptions are: (1) She does not uncover her head, (2) she covers her face with a veil that does not touch the skin (like a dome), (3) she does not raise her voice in talbiyah, (4) she does not do raml (brisk walking) in tawaf, (5) she does not hurry (harwalah) in sa'y between the green markers, (6) she does not shave her head but shortens (taqsir), (7) she wears sewn garments (makhit), (8) she does not crowd men at the Black Stone.
The first two are about covering; others about actions.
3
Understand the reasons
These exceptions preserve modesty and prevent fitnah. Raising voice, raml, and shaving are for men; women should remain concealed and dignified.
4
Apply to a scenario
Ask: Can a woman raise her voice in talbiyah? No. Can she wear a sewn shirt? Yes. Can she join men at the Black Stone? No, she should avoid crowding.
These are clear from the text.
5
Compare the merits of Hajj types
The passage concludes that ifrad (Hajj alone) is inferior to tamattu' (Hajj with umrah), and qiran (combined Hajj and umrah) is best.
This is a separate ruling but attached here.

Key Terms
الترمل (al-raml): Walking with rapid short steps and swaying shoulders in the first three rounds of tawaf.
الهرولة (al-harwalah): Jogging or hurrying between the two green markers in sa'y.
التلبية (al-talbiyah): The phrase 'Labbayka Allahumma labbayk...' recited during Hajj.
المخيط (al-makhit): Sewn garments such as shirts, trousers, etc. Not permitted for men in ihram, but permitted for women.
التقصير (al-taqsir): Shortening the hair by cutting a small portion, typically the length of a fingertip.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Women follow the same Hajj rites as men with specific exceptions for modesty; they should avoid raml, loud talbiyah, and shaving, and may wear sewn clothes.

Completion of Hajj al-Ifrad: Farewell Tawaf and Women's Rulings
Describes farewell tawaf and women's specific Hajj rulings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rulings and etiquette of the farewell tawaf and list the exceptions for women in Hajj al-Ifrad.

Core Idea
Farewell tawaf is a wajib act with unique etiquette; women follow men's Hajj rules except in specified matters of modesty.

This passage completes the description of Hajj al-Ifrad by detailing the etiquette of the farewell tawaf and the special concessions for women. While women generally perform all rites like men, the Hanafi school has established several exceptions to preserve modesty and avoid harm.

Guided Path
1
Identify the farewell tawaf and its etiquette
The pilgrim should perform tawaf al-wada' before leaving Mecca, walking backwards facing the Kaaba, weeping, and exiting from Bab Bani Shaybah.
This is wajib for non-Meccan pilgrims.
2
State the general principle for women
The text says 'The woman is like the man in all actions of Hajj' – a clear statement of equality in rites.
3
List the exceptions for women
Identify each exception: covering head and face (with a veil that does not touch), lowering voice in talbiyah, no ramal or hurrying in sa'i, no shaving (only shortening), wearing sewn garments, and not crowding men at the Black Stone.
These exceptions are based on modesty and avoiding fitna.
4
Apply the rulings to a scenario
Consider a female pilgrim performing sa'i: she must walk normally between the green milestones, not run like men.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كما قاله « الكمال». وإذا أراد العود إلى أهله ينبغي أن ينصرف بعد طوافه للوداع، وهو يمشي إلى ورائه ووجهه إلى البيت باكياً، أو متباكياً، متحسّراً على فراق البيت حتى يخرج من المسجد، ويخرج من مكة من باب بني شَيْبَةَ من الثَّنِيَّةِ السُّفلى، والمرأة في جميع أفعال الحــج كالرجل، غـيـر أنها لا تكشف رأسها، وتسدل على وجهها شيئاً تحته عيدان كالقبة تمنع مسـه بالغطاء، ولا ترفع صوتها بالتلبية، ولا ترمل ولا تُهرول في السعي بين الميلين الأخضرين، بل تمشي على هيئتها في جميع السعي بين الصفا والمروة، ولا تحلق ، وتقصر، وتلبس المخيط، ولا تزاحم الرجال في استلام الحجر، وهذا تمام حج المفرد، وهو دون المتمتع في الفضل، والقران أفضل من التمتع.
As al-Kamal said. And when he wants to return to his family, he should depart after performing the farewell tawaf, walking backwards with his face towards the House, weeping or pretending to weep, regretful at leaving the House until he exits the mosque, and he leaves Mecca from the Bab Bani Shaybah from the lower Thaniyyah. The woman is like the man in all actions of Hajj, except that she does not uncover her head, and she lets down over her face something underneath which there are sticks like a dome to prevent it from touching the covering, and she does not raise her voice in talbiyah, and she does not ramal (quick pace with short steps) nor hurry in the sa'i between the two green milestones, but she walks in her normal manner throughout the sa'i between Safa and Marwah, and she does not shave but shortens, and she wears sewn garments, and she does not crowd men in kissing the Black Stone. This is the completion of Hajj al-Ifrad, and it is inferior in merit to Tamattu', and Qiran is better than Tamattu'.
Source pages p. 697

Commentary
This passage completes the description of Hajj al-Ifrad by detailing the farewell tawaf (tawaf al-wada') and the etiquette of leaving Mecca. The pilgrim is to walk backwards facing the Kaaba, showing grief. Women perform all actions like men with specific exceptions: they cover their heads, use a veil with sticks to avoid contact, do not raise voices in talbiyah, do not ramal or hurry in sa'i, do not shave but only shorten, may wear sewn garments (since they are not in ihram for the head covering?), and avoid crowding men at the Black Stone. The author notes that Ifrad is less meritorious than Tamattu', and Qiran is better than Tamattu'.

Key Terms
طواف الوداع (tawaf al-wada'): The farewell circumambulation performed by a pilgrim before leaving Mecca, walking backwards facing the Kaaba.
الرمل (ramal): Quick walking with short steps while moving the shoulders, performed by men in the first three rounds of tawaf al-qudum and in sa'i.
المخيط (makhit): Sewn garments (such as a chemise or trousers), which a woman in ihram may wear because her ihram is for covering, unlike men who must wear unsewn garments.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Hajj al-Ifrad, what is the ruling regarding a woman's performance of sa'i between Safa and Marwah?
A) She runs between the green milestones like men.
B) She walks normally throughout the sa'i.
C) She is exempt from sa'i entirely.
D) She performs sa'i only after shaving her head.

Key Takeaway
In Hajj, women follow the same rites as men except for specific exceptions related to covering, voice, pace, haircut, clothing, and interaction.

Hajj al-Qiran: Definition, Procedure, and Obligation of Sacrifice
Definition, procedure, conditions, and proof of Qiran

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define Hajj al-Qiran, describe its procedure, and state when the blood sacrifice becomes wajib and what invalidates it.

Core Idea
The qarin combines Umrah and Hajj in one ihram and must sacrifice; exiting ihram early requires two dam.

In this lesson, we examine Hajj al-Qiran, a form of Hajj where the pilgrim intends Umrah and Hajj simultaneously from a single ihram. The passage from Imdad al-Fattah explains the precise procedure, the obligatory sacrifice (dam), and key conditions that ensure its validity. Understanding these rulings safeguards your Hajj from common errors.

Guided Path
1
Understand the definition of Qiran
Identify the intention phrase and the combination of Umrah and Hajj in one ihram. Note that the pilgrim says a specific supplication after the two rak'ahs of ihram.
2
Outline the procedure of Qiran
Follow the sequence: upon entering Mecca, perform Umrah first (tawaf with ramal, sa'i), then tawaf al-qudum for Hajj, then complete Hajj rites. Umrah is sunnah in this context.
3
Identify the obligation of sacrifice (dam)
After throwing Jamrat al-Aqabah on the Day of Sacrifice, a sheep or one-seventh of a camel becomes wajib. If unable, fasting three days before the Day of Sacrifice and seven after Hajj is a substitute.
The proof is Quran 2:196, applied to Qiran by analogy (qiyas) with Tamattu'.
4
Examine the conditions for validity
Two conditions are highlighted: (1) the Umrah tawaf must be mostly within the Hajj months, and (2) the qarin must not exit ihram after Umrah. Doing so violates both ihrams and requires two dam.
5
Recognize the consequence of violation
If a qarin performs tahlil (haircut) after Umrah, he commits a jinaayah against both ihrams and must sacrifice two animals. His Hajj remains valid but with added compensation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل القران هو أن يجمع بين إحرام الحج والعمرة، فيقول بعد صلاة ركعتي الإحرام: « اللهم إني أريد العمرة والحج فيسرهما لي وتقبلهما مني، ثم يلبي فإذا دخـــل مكـة بـدأ بـطــواف العـمـرة سبعة أشواط، يَرْمُلُ في الثلاثة الأول فقط، ثم يصلي ركعتي الطواف، ثم يخرج إلى الصفا، ويقـوم عليه داعياً مكبراً مهللاً ملبياً، مصلياً على النبي ، ثم يهبط نحو المروة، ويسعى بين الميلين، فيتم سبعة أشواط، وهذه أفعال العمرة، والعمرة سُنَّة، ثم يطوف طواف القدوم للحج، ثـم يتـم أفـعـال الحج كما تقدم، فإذا رمى يوم النحر جمرة العقبة، وجب عليه ذبح شاة، أو سبع بدنة (۳)، فإذا لم يجد () (نَصِيَامُ ثَلَثَةِ أَيَّامي [البقرة : ١٩٦] (٥) قبل مجيء يوم النحر من أشهر الحج، وسبعة أيـام بـعـد الفراغ من الحج ولو بمكة بعد مضي أيام التشريق، ولو فرقها جاز. (۱) ومن شرائط صحة القران أن يطوف للعمرة كله أو أكثره من أشهر الحج، ولا يتحلل القارن بعـد عمـرتـه فلـو طاف وقصر كان جناية على إحرام الحج وإحرام العمرة، فيجب عليه دَمَان لأن تحلل القارن مـن الـعـمـرة إنمـا هو يوم النحر. فتح باب العناية (٦٧٨/١). (۲) ص (٦٩١). (۳) لقوله تعالى: ﴿ فَمَنْ تَمَتَّعَ بِالْعُمْرَةِ إِلَى الْحَجِّ فَمَا اسْتَيْسَرَ مِنَ الْهَدْي ) [البقرة: ١٩٦]. (٤) أي: المال وهو بأن لا يكون في ملكه عن كفافه قدر ما يشتري به الدم ولا هو في ملكه. (٥) آخرها يوم عرفة، فإن فاتت الثلاثة تعين الدم. ط. (٦) لقوله تعالى: ﴿ وَسَبْعَةٍ إِذَا رَجَعْتُمْ ﴾ [البقرة: ١٩٦] أي: من منى إلى مكة.
Section on Qiran: Qiran is to combine ihram for Hajj and Umrah. He says after praying two rak'ahs of ihram: 'O Allah, I intend Umrah and Hajj, so make them easy for me and accept them from me.' Then he recites talbiyah. When he enters Mecca, he begins with the tawaf of Umrah, seven circuits, performing ramal only in the first three, then prays two rak'ahs of tawaf, then goes to Safa and stands upon it supplicating, saying Allahu Akbar, la ilaha illa Allah, talbiyah, and sending blessings on the Prophet, then descends towards Marwah and performs sa'i between the two green milestones, completing seven circuits. These are the actions of Umrah, and Umrah is sunnah. Then he performs the tawaf of arrival (tawaf al-qudum) for Hajj, then completes the actions of Hajj as previously described. When he throws at Jamrat al-Aqabah on the Day of Sacrifice, it becomes obligatory upon him to slaughter a sheep or one-seventh of a camel. If he does not find [the means], then fasting three days [before the Day of Sacrifice] during the months of Hajj, and seven days after completing Hajj, even if in Mecca after the days of Tashriq, and if he separates them it is permissible. (One of the conditions for the validity of Qiran is that he performs the tawaf of Umrah entirely or most of it during the months of Hajj, and the Qarin does not become free of ihram after his Umrah. So if he performs tawaf and shortens [his hair], that would be an offense against the ihram of Hajj and the ihram of Umrah, and two blood sacrifices become obligatory upon him, because the Qarin's release from Umrah is only on the Day of Sacrifice.)
Source pages p. 698

Commentary
This passage defines Hajj al-Qiran as combining Umrah and Hajj with a single ihram. The pilgrim (qarin) intends both simultaneously and performs the actions of Umrah first upon entering Mecca: tawaf (with ramal in first three rounds), two rak'ahs, sa'i, then tawaf al-qudum for Hajj, then continues with Hajj rites. Umrah is considered sunnah (not fard) in this context. On the Day of Sacrifice, the qarin must slaughter a sheep or share a camel; if unable, he fasts three days before the Day of Sacrifice during the months of Hajj, and seven days after returning (from Mina to Mecca). A footnote clarifies conditions: the Umrah tawaf must be mostly or fully within the Hajj months, and the qarin cannot perform a partial tahlil (getting out of ihram) after Umrah; doing so would violate both ihrams and require two dam (blood sacrifices). The proof for the sacrifice is from Quran 2:196, and the fasting alternative is also from the same verse.

Key Terms
القران (al-qiran): Combining Umrah and Hajj with one ihram, intending both simultaneously.
دم (dam): A blood sacrifice (a sheep or one-seventh of a camel) obligatory on the qarin as a requirement of qiran.
هدي (hady): An animal sacrificed during Hajj, here specifically for the qarin.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on a qarin who performs tawaf and shortens his hair after Umrah, intending to exit ihram?
A) He is free from ihram and must only give a dam.
B) He has committed a violation requiring two blood sacrifices.
C) His Hajj becomes invalid and he must repeat it.
D) No penalty because Umrah is completed.

Key Takeaway
A qarin remains in ihram until the Day of Sacrifice; premature exit requires two dam, but Hajj remains valid.

Definition and Ruling of Qiran
Defines Qiran, its procedure, and ruling on sacrifice

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define Qiran, describe its procedure, state the ruling on the sacrifice (dam), and apply the conditions for its validity.

Core Idea
Qiran combines Hajj and Umrah in one ihram; a wajib sacrifice is required, and the pilgrim remains in ihram until the Day of Sacrifice.

This lesson unpacks the definition, procedure, and legal consequences of performing Hajj in the Qiran form. You will learn exactly what a Qarin must do, when the sacrifice becomes obligatory, and what happens if the conditions are violated. The source text we study is from Imdad al-Fattah Sharh Nur al-Idah, a standard Hanafi fiqh manual.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Definition of Qiran
Locate the opening sentence that defines Qiran as combining the ihram of Hajj and Umrah. Note that a single intention (niyyah) suffices.
The definition is explicit: 'al-qiran huwa an yajma'a bayna ihram al-hajj wa al-umrah.'
2
Trace the Procedure
Follow the sequence of actions: after two rak'ahs of ihram, the pilgrim makes niyyah, recites talbiyah, enters Mecca, performs tawaf and sa'y for Umrah (with raml in first three circuits), then performs tawaf al-qudum for Hajj, and completes the Hajj rituals.
The passage lists the actions in order; the word 'thumma' indicates sequence.
3
Recognize the Sacrifice Obligation
Note that after throwing the Jamrat al-Aqabah on the Day of Sacrifice, slaughtering a sheep or seventh of a camel becomes wajib. If the pilgrim cannot afford it, fasting is substituted: three days before Eid and seven days after returning.
The dalil is Quran 2:196, applied by qiyas from tamattu' to qiran.
4
Understand the Condition for Validity
The passage states that for Qiran to be valid, all or most of the Umrah tawaf must be performed within the months of Hajj (Shawwal, Dhul-Qa'dah first ten days of Dhul-Hijjah).
This condition ensures the combination is within the permissible time frame.
5
Note the Consequence of Violation
If the Qarin performs tawaf and shortens his hair before the Day of Sacrifice, he violates both ihrams and must offer two separate sacrifices (daman).
The Qarin does not become halal after Umrah; his tahlil is only on the Day of Sacrifice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل القران هو أن يجمع بين إحرام الحج والعمرة، فيقول بعد صلاة ركعتي الإحرام: « اللهم إني أريد العمرة والحج فيسرهما لي وتقبلهما مني، ثم يلبي فإذا دخـــل مكـة بـدأ بـطــواف العـمـرة سبعة أشواط، يَرْمُلُ في الثلاثة الأول فقط، ثم يصلي ركعتي الطواف، ثم يخرج إلى الصفا، ويقـوم عليه داعياً مكبراً مهللاً ملبياً، مصلياً على النبي ، ثم يهبط نحو المروة، ويسعى بين الميلين، فيتم سبعة أشواط، وهذه أفعال العمرة، والعمرة سُنَّة، ثم يطوف طواف القدوم للحج، ثـم يتـم أفـعـال الحج كما تقدم، فإذا رمى يوم النحر جمرة العقبة، وجب عليه ذبح شاة، أو سبع بدنة (۳)، فإذا لم يجد (٤) (نَصِيَامُ ثَلَثَةِ أَيَّامَي [البقرة : ١٩٦] (٥) قبل مجيء يوم النحر من أشهر الحج، وسبعة أيـام بـعـد الفراغ من الحج ولو بمكة بعد مضي أيام التشريق، ولو فرقها جاز. (۱) ومن شرائط صحة القران أن يطوف للعمرة كله أو أكثره من أشهر الحج، ولا يتحلل القارن بعـد عمـرتـه فلـو طاف وقصر كان جناية على إحرام الحج وإحرام العمرة، فيجب عليه دَمَان لأن تحلل القارن مـن الـعـمـرة إنمـا هو يوم النحر. فتح باب العناية (٦٧٨/١). (۲) ص (٦٩١). (۳) لقوله تعالى: ﴿ فَمَنْ تَمَتَّعَ بِالْعُمْرَةِ إِلَى الْحَجِّ فَمَا اسْتَيْسَرَ مِنَ الْهَدْي ) [البقرة: ١٩٦]. (٤) أي: المال وهو بأن لا يكون في ملكه عن كفافه قدر ما يشتري به الدم ولا هو في ملكه. (٥) آخرها يوم عرفة، فإن فاتت الثلاثة تعين الدم. ط. (٦) لقوله تعالى: ﴿ وَسَبْعَةٍ إِذَا رَجَعْتُمْ ﴾ [البقرة: ١٩٦] أي: من منى إلى مكة.
Chapter of Qiran: Qiran is to combine the ihram of Hajj and Umrah. He says after performing the two rak'ahs of ihram: 'O Allah, I intend Umrah and Hajj, so make them easy for me and accept them from me.' Then he recites the talbiyah. When he enters Mecca, he begins the tawaf of Umrah with seven circuits, doing raml only in the first three, then prays two rak'ahs of tawaf, then goes to Safa, stands upon it supplicating, saying takbir, tahlil, and talbiyah, sending blessings on the Prophet, then descends towards Marwa, and runs between the two green markers, completing seven circuits. These are the actions of Umrah, and Umrah is Sunnah. Then he performs the tawaf of arrival for Hajj, then completes the actions of Hajj as previously mentioned. When he throws at the Jamrat al-Aqabah on the Day of Sacrifice, it becomes obligatory for him to slaughter a sheep or one seventh of a camel. If he cannot find (the means), then (he must) fast three days before the Day of Sacrifice during the months of Hajj, and seven days after completing Hajj, even if in Mecca after the days of Tashriq pass. If he performs them separately, it is permissible. (1) Among the conditions of validity of Qiran is that he performs all or most of the tawaf of Umrah within the months of Hajj, and the Qarin does not become halal after his Umrah. So if he performs tawaf and shortens (his hair), it is an offense against the ihram of Hajj and the ihram of Umrah, so two sacrifices (blood) are obligatory upon him because the tahlil of the Qarin from Umrah is only on the Day of Sacrifice. Fath Bab al-Inayah (1/678). (2) See p. 691. (3) Due to His statement: "And whoever performs Umrah and Hajj consecutively, then what is easy from the sacrificial animal" [Al-Baqarah: 196]. (4) Meaning: wealth, that is, he does not possess sufficient surplus wealth to buy the blood (animal), nor is it in his possession. (5) The last of it is the Day of Arafah; if the three days are missed, then blood becomes obligatory. (6) Due to His statement: "And seven when you return" [Al-Baqarah: 196], meaning from Mina to Mecca.
Source pages p. 698

Commentary
This passage defines the Qiran (Combined) method of Hajj. The author states that Qiran means combining the ihram of both Hajj and Umrah with a single intention. The procedure begins with the niyyah after two rak'ahs of ihram, followed by talbiyah. Upon reaching Mecca, the pilgrim first performs the tawaf of Umrah with raml (brisk walking) in the first three circuits, then the two rak'ahs of tawaf, then goes to Safa and Marwa for sa'y (seven circuits). After completing these actions of Umrah (which is Sunnah according to the Hanafi school), he performs the tawaf al-qudum (tawaf of arrival) for Hajj and then continues with the rest of the Hajj rituals. On the Day of Sacrifice, after throwing the Jamrat al-Aqabah, a sacrifice (a sheep or a seventh of a camel) becomes wajib (obligatory). If the pilgrim cannot afford the sacrifice, then fasting is required: three days before Eid (during the months of Hajj, with the last day being Arafah) and seven days after returning from Mina. The author notes a condition for the validity of Qiran: most of the Umrah tawaf must be performed within the months of Hajj (Shawwal, Dhul-Qa'dah, and the first ten days of Dhul-Hijjah). Additionally, the Qarin does not become halal from his ihram after completing Umrah; he remains in ihram until the Day of Sacrifice. If he mistakenly performs tawaf and cuts his hair, he has violated both ihrams and must offer two separate sacrifices (dam).

Key Terms
القران (al-qiran): Combining the ihram of Hajj and Umrah with a single intention
الرمل (ar-raml): Brisk walking with shoulder movements, performed in the first three circuits of tawaf
الدم (ad-dam): Sacrifice of a sheep or seventh of a camel as compensation or penalty

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, if a Qarin (performer of Qiran) performs tawaf for Umrah and then shortens his hair before the Day of Sacrifice, what is required?
A) Nothing, as he has completed Umrah and is halal.
B) One sacrifice (dam) for violating the ihram of Umrah.
C) Two sacrifices (daman) for violating both ihrams of Hajj and Umrah.
D) He must repeat the entire Hajj.

Key Takeaway
Qiran combines Hajj and Umrah with one ihram; a wajib sacrifice is due on the Day of Sacrifice, and the pilgrim remains in ihram until that day, with two sacrifices required for any premature tahlil.

Definition and Procedure of Tamattu'
Defines Tamattu' with procedure and two cases

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define Tamattu', describe its complete procedure, and state the ruling on sacrifice for a Mutamatti' who brings hady versus one who does not.

Core Idea
Tamattu' requires a sacrifice; bringing hady keeps you in ihram until Hajj ends.

Tamattu' is one of the three ways to perform Hajj in the Hanafi school. This lesson defines it clearly and explains the two scenarios: with and without a sacrificial animal. Understanding this distinction is crucial for fulfilling the obligations correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition of Tamattu'
Tamattu' is performing Umrah first during the months of Hajj, then performing Hajj in the same year, with separate ihrams. The pilgrim begins by assuming ihram for Umrah from the miqat.
The intention is only for Umrah at the start.
2
Follow the procedure from Umrah to halal status
After ihram, recite talbiyah until tawaf, perform tawaf with raml, two rak'ahs, sa'y, then shave or shorten hair. If no hady is brought, everything becomes halal.
The talbiyah is stopped at the beginning of tawaf, not when seeing the Kaaba.
3
Distinguish between the two cases: with and without hady
If hady is brought, the pilgrim does not become halal after Umrah; he remains in ihram until Hajj. On the Day of Tarwiyah, he assumes ihram for Hajj from the Haram.
The type with hady is considered more virtuous.
4
Determine the ruling on sacrifice
After throwing Jamrat al-Aqabah on the Day of Sacrifice, slaughtering a sheep or seventh of a camel becomes wajib. If unable, fast three days before Eid and seven after returning. If the fast is missed on the Day of Sacrifice, only slaughter suffices.
The sacrifice is wajib, not a sunnah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل التمتع: هو أن يحرم بالعمرة من الميقات، فيقول بعد صلاة ركعتي الإحرام: « اللهم إني أريد العمرة فيسرها لي وتقبلها مني، ثم يلبي حتى يدخل مكة، فيطوف لها، ويقطع التلبية بأول طوافه)، ويَرْمُلُ فيه، ثم يصلي ركعتي الطواف، ثم يسعى بين الصفا والمروة بعد الوقوف على الصفا كما تقدم " سبعة أشواط، ثم يحلق رأسه، أو يقصر إذا لم يسق الهدي، وحل له كل شيء من الجماع وغيره، ويستمر حلالاً، وإن ساق الهدي لا يتحلل من عمرته، فإذا جاء يوم التروية يُحرم بالحج من الحرم، ويخرج إلى مني، فإذا رمى جمرة العقبة يوم النحر لزمه ذبح شاة أو سبع بدنة، فإن لم يجد صام ثلاثة أيام قبل مجيء يوم النحر، وسبعة إذا رجع كالقارن، فإن لم يصم يوم النحر، تعين عليه ذبح شاة؛ ولا يجزئه صوم ولا صدقة. (۱) باستلام الحجر الأسود، لا عند مشاهدته للبيت لما روى ابن عباس رضي الله عنهما : أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم كان يمسك من التلبية في العمرة إذا استلم الحجر. أخرجه الترمذي في الحج، باب ما جاء متى تقطع التلبية في العمرة (۹۱۹). (٢) ص (٦٩٢). (۳) أي: إلا بعد الفراغ من الحج ط. حتى ينحر هديه فيستمر محرماً حتى يحرم بالحج يوم التروية، فإذا حلق يـوم النحر حل من الإحرامين، لأنه محلل فيتحلل به عنهما، وذبح دم التمتع. وهذا الوجه الثاني من التمتع، وهـو أفضل من الأول الذي لم يسق هديه لفعله . ش بتصرف. (٤) شكراً لما أنعم الله تعالى عليه حيث وفق لأداء النسكين. ط.
Chapter of Tamattu': Tamattu' is to assume ihram for Umrah from the miqat, saying after performing the two rak'ahs of ihram: 'O Allah, I intend Umrah, so make it easy for me and accept it from me.' Then he recites the talbiyah until he enters Mecca. He performs tawaf for it, and stops the talbiyah at the beginning of his tawaf, and he does raml in it. Then he prays two rak'ahs of tawaf, then runs between Safa and Marwa after standing on Safa as previously mentioned, seven circuits. Then he shaves his head or shortens (his hair) if he has not brought the sacrificial animal, and everything becomes permissible for him including intercourse and other things, and he remains in a state of being halal. But if he brought the sacrificial animal, he does not become halal from his Umrah. When the Day of Tarwiyah comes, he assumes ihram for Hajj from the Haram, and goes out to Mina. If he throws the Jamrat al-Aqabah on the Day of Sacrifice, a sheep or one seventh of a camel becomes binding on him. If he does not find (the means), he fasts three days before the Day of Sacrifice, and seven when he returns, like the Qarin. If he does not fast on the Day of Sacrifice, slaughtering a sheep becomes mandated on him, and neither fasting nor charity suffices. (1) By touching the Black Stone, not when he sees the House, due to what Ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with them both) narrated: that the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to stop the talbiyah in Umrah when he touched the Stone. Tirmidhi recorded it in Hajj, chapter on when to stop talbiyah in Umrah (919). (2) See p. 692. (3) Meaning: except after completing Hajj, until he slaughters his hady, so he remains in ihram until he assumes ihram for Hajj on Day of Tarwiyah. When he shaves on Day of Sacrifice, he becomes halal from both ihrams, because he is a Muhallil (one for whom it is permissible), so he becomes halal by it from both, and he slaughters the dam of Tamattu'. This is the second type of Tamattu', and it is better than the first where he did not bring hady, because of his action. (4) In gratitude for what Allah has bestowed upon him, by granting him to perform both rites.
Source pages p. 699

Commentary
This passage defines the Tamattu' (Enjoyment) method of Hajj. The pilgrim first performs Umrah from the miqat, intending only Umrah. After the two rak'ahs of ihram, he recites talbiyah until he starts tawaf upon entering Mecca. He performs tawaf with raml, then two rak'ahs, then sa'y between Safa and Marwa. He then shaves or shortens his hair, becoming halal, unless he has brought a sacrificial animal (hady). If he brought hady, he remains in ihram until the Day of Sacrifice. On the Day of Tarwiyah (8th Dhul-Hijjah), he assumes ihram for Hajj from Haram (Mecca) and goes to Mina. After throwing Jamrat al-Aqabah on Eid day, slaughter of a sheep or seventh of a camel becomes wajib. If unable, he fasts three days before Eid (during the months of Hajj) and seven days after returning, similar to the Qarin. If he fails to fast on the Day of Sacrifice, he must slaughter; no other expiation suffices. The footnote explains that the talbiyah is stopped upon touching the Black Stone, not upon seeing the Kaaba, based on a hadith. Also, there are two forms of Tamattu': one without hady (he becomes halal after Umrah) and one with hady (he remains in ihram until Hajj). The latter is considered better because the Prophet acted upon it.

Key Terms
التمتع (at-tamattu'): Performing Umrah first during the months of Hajj, then performing Hajj in the same year, with separate ihrams
الهدي (al-hady): A sacrificial animal brought by the pilgrim for Tamattu' or Qiran, which prevents one from becoming halal after Umrah
التلبية (at-talbiyah): The pilgrim's proclamation 'Labbayk...' starting from ihram until certain points in the rituals

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, if a Mutamatti' (performer of Tamattu') brings a sacrificial animal (hady), when does he become halal?
A) Immediately after completing Umrah.
B) On the Day of Tarwiyah.
C) On the Day of Sacrifice after shaving.
D) He never becomes halal.

Key Takeaway
Tamattu' requires a wajib sacrifice; bringing hady keeps the pilgrim in ihram until the Day of Sacrifice, whereas without hady, he becomes halal after Umrah.

Ruling and Procedure of 'Umrah
Ruling statement on 'Umrah with procedure and exceptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on 'Umrah (sunnah mu'akkadah) and explain its procedure including the difference in ihram location for those in Mecca versus afaqi.

Core Idea
'Umrah is a commended pilgrimage valid year-round except on four days; ihram for a Meccan must be from outside the Haram.

This lesson clarifies the Hanafi position on 'Umrah—its legal status, valid times, and the steps to perform it. The source passage distinguishes between those already in Mecca and those coming from outside, and it sets the stage for understanding a key procedural difference with Hajj.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on 'Umrah
Locate the first sentence: 'العمرة: سنة' and the footnote which clarifies it is sunnah mu'akkadah. Note that some scholars consider it wajib.
The Hanafi mufta bihi is sunnah mu'akkadah.
2
Note the disliked days
The text lists four days when 'Umrah is makruh: the day of 'Arafah, the day of Nahr, and the days of Tashreeq. Understand that these are days associated with Hajj.
This ruling applies to 'Umrah, not Hajj.
3
Explain the procedure for a Meccan
For someone in Mecca, ihram for 'Umrah must be from al-Hil (outside the Haram), unlike Hajj where ihram is from inside the Haram. This is based on the Prophet's instruction to Aisha.
Tan'im is the common place for Meccans to enter ihram for 'Umrah.
4
Explain the procedure for an afaqi
A person coming from outside Mecca enters ihram for 'Umrah from the miqat, the same as for Hajj. Then they perform tawaf, sa'y, and shave or trim to exit ihram.
The miqat depends on the direction of arrival.
5
Identify the components of 'Umrah
From the footnote: ihram is a condition, most of tawaf is a rukn, and other elements (sa'y, halq) are wajib. Understand the difference between condition, pillar, and obligation.
This distinction affects validity and compensation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل العمرة: سنة، وتصح في جميع السَنَةِ، وتكره يوم عرفة ، ويوم النحر، وأيام التشريق. وكيفيتها: أن يحرم لها من بمكة من الحل، بخلاف إحرامه للحج فإنه من الحرم. وأما الآفــاقـي الـذي لم يدخل مكة، فيحرم إذا قصدها من الميقات، ثم يطوف ويسعى لها، ثم يحلق، وقــد حــل منـهـا كمـا بيناه (۲) بحمد الله. [تنبيه] وأفضل الأيام يوم عرفة إذا وافق يوم الجمعة، وهو أفضل من سبعين حجة في غير جمعة، رواه صاحب معراج الدراية بقوله: وقد صح عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أنه قال: « أفضل الأيــام يوم عرفة إذا وافق جمعة، وهو أفضلُ من سبعين حجةٍ ) (۳) ذكره في تجريد الصحاح بعلامة الموطأ، وكذا قاله الزيلعي شارح الكنز. والمجاورة بمكة مكروهة عند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى، لـعــدم القيام بحقوق البيت والحرم ، ونفى الكراهة صاحباه رحمهما الله تعالى.
(1) أي: مؤكدة على المذهب وصحح في الجوهرة وجوبها وهي إحرام وطواف وحلق أو تقصير فالإحرام شرط ومعظم الطواف ركن وغيرهما واجب هو المختار ويفعل فيها كفعل الحاج ط.
(2) ص (٦٩٠).
(3) ذكره ابن حجر في فتح الباري (۲۷۱/۸)، وقال: ذكره رزين في جامعه مرفوعاً. وذكر الحديث ثـم قـال: فهو حديث لا أعرف حاله لأنه لم يذكر صحابية ولا من أخرجه بل أدرجه في حديث الموطأ الذي ذكره مرسلاً عن طلحة بن كريز.
(4) قال الغزالي رحمه | ه الله في إحياء علوم الدين (۳۲۳/۱): كره الخائفون المحتاطون من العلماء المقام بمكة لمعان ثلاثة...
Chapter of 'Umrah: It is sunnah, and it is valid throughout the entire year, and it is disliked on the day of 'Arafah, the day of Nahr, and the days of Tashreeq. Its method: one enters ihram for it from Mecca from the Hal (outside the Haram), unlike his ihram for Hajj which is from the Haram. As for the one coming from distant horizons who has not entered Mecca, he enters ihram when intending it from the miqat, then performs tawaf and sa'y for it, then shaves, and he is released from it as we explained (2) by the praise of Allah. [Notification] The best of days is the day of 'Arafah if it coincides with Friday, and it is better than seventy Hajj not on Friday, as narrated by the author of Mi'raj al-Dirayah with his words: 'It has been confirmed from the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, that he said: The best of days is the day of 'Arafah if it coincides with Friday, and it is better than seventy Hajj.' Mentioned in Tajrid al-Sihah with the symbol of al-Muwatta', and likewise said by al-Zayla'i, the commentator of al-Kanz. And residing in Mecca is disliked according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, due to the failure to fulfill the rights of the House and the Haram, and his two companions negated the dislike.
Source pages p. 700

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement that defines 'Umrah and its rulings. The author states that 'Umrah is sunnah mu'akkadah (according to the relied-upon view, though some scholars like al-Jawharah consider it wajib). It is valid throughout the year but makruh on four days: the day of 'Arafah, the day of Nahr (10th Dhul Hijjah), and the three days of Tashreeq (11th-13th). The procedure is similar to Hajj but with some differences: for someone already in Mecca, the ihram for 'Umrah must be from outside the Haram (al-Hil), while ihram for Hajj is from inside. For an afaqi (one coming from outside), ihram for 'Umrah is from the miqat. After tawaf, sa'y, and shaving, one exits ihram. The text then notes that the best day of the year is 'Arafah when it falls on Friday, citing a hadith (though the chain is disputed). Finally, there is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa considers residing permanently in Mecca makruh due to the difficulty of fulfilling the sanctuary's rights, but the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) do not consider it disliked. The footnotes explain that the ruling of 'Umrah is sunnah mu'akkadah (or wajib according to some), and detail the components: ihram is a condition, most of tawaf is a rukn, and other elements are wajib. The hadith about the virtue of Friday 'Arafah is cited but its authenticity is questioned by Ibn Hajar.

Key Terms
العمرة (al-'umrah): A pilgrimage to the Ka'bah performed at any time of the year, consisting of ihram, tawaf, sa'y, and shaving or trimming.
الحل (al-hill): The area outside the Haram. For 'Umrah, the person in Mecca must go to the Hill to enter ihram.
السنة المؤكدة (al-sunnah al-mu'akkadah): A recommended act that the Prophet consistently performed and encouraged; omitting it is disliked but not sinful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, on which days is it disliked (makruh) to perform 'Umrah?
A) Fridays and Mondays
B) The day of 'Arafah, the day of Nahr, and the days of Tashreeq
C) The first ten days of Dhul Hijjah
D) Only the day of Nahr

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school treats 'Umrah as a highly recommended sunnah with a specific procedure that differs from Hajj in the location of ihram for those already in Mecca.

The Dispute on Residing in Mecca (Mujawarah)
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the ruling of residing in Mecca

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify Abu Hanifa's position that residing permanently in Mecca (mujawarah) is makruh, contrast it with the Sahibayn's negation of dislike, and explain the reasoning and practical consequence.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa considers permanent residence in Mecca disliked due to the high standard of rights of the Haram; his companions disagree based on the inherent virtue of the place.

While the virtues of Mecca are immense, the Hanafi school has an internal debate about whether it is recommended to live there permanently. This lesson unpacks the reasoning of Imam Abu Hanifa and his two chief disciples on this issue, helping you understand how different legal considerations can lead to divergent rulings even within the same school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
The issue is whether it is makruh (disliked) to reside permanently in Mecca (al-mujawarah) for the purpose of worship.
This is about long-term residency, not just a visit.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa says it is makruh. His reasoning is that people fail to fulfill the rights of the House and the Haram, and that sins are multiplied there.
The source mentions: 'لعدم القيام بحقوق البيت والحرم'.
3
State the Sahibayn's position
The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) negate the dislike. They argue that residing in Mecca is inherently good and allows one to perform numerous acts of worship; the fear of punishment does not make it disliked.
They focus on the positive aspect of being in the sacred precincts.
4
Analyze the evidence
The text does not provide detailed proofs. Abu Hanifa's view is based on caution and reports that sins are multiplied in Mecca. The Sahibayn rely on the general recommendation of worship in the Haram.
A more detailed analysis might involve hadith about the multiplication of good and bad deeds in Mecca.
5
Determine the practical consequence
If one follows Abu Hanifa, one should be extra vigilant to fulfill the rights of the Haram if residing there, and perhaps avoid permanent residence if he cannot maintain proper conduct. If one follows the Sahibayn, there is no dislike, but one should still be mindful.
The mufta bihi is not explicitly given; the author presents both views.

Key Terms
المجاورة (al-mujawarah): Residing permanently or for a long period in Mecca for the sake of worship.
الكراهة (al-karahah): Dislike; a legal classification between mubah and haram. Acts that are makruh are discouraged but not sinful if done without justification.
حقوق البيت والحرم (huquq al-bayt wa al-haram): The rights and obligations due to the Ka'bah and the Sacred Precincts, including reverence, cleanliness, and increased worship.

Key Takeaway

Ruling and Procedure of Umrah
Ruling and procedure for Umrah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Umrah, identify the disliked times, and describe the procedure for both a Makki and an Afaqi.

Core Idea
Umrah is a confirmed sunnah, valid all year except on four specific days; its procedure differs for residents and outsiders.

This part of the chapter clarifies the legal status of Umrah in the Hanafi school: it is a sunnah mu'akkadah, not obligatory. It also specifies the four days on which performing Umrah is disliked (makruh tanzihan) and outlines the correct procedure for assuming ihram, distinguishing between a person already in Makkah and one coming from outside. Understanding these basics ensures one performs Umrah with proper discipline.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on Umrah
Look for the explicit statement that Umrah is 'sunnah' and note the footnote indicating it is mu'akkadah. Recognize that the relied-upon Hanafi position is sunnah, not wajib.
Some early texts consider it wajib, but the majority and later fatwa uphold sunnah.
2
List the disliked days
Find the four days: the day of Arafah (9 Dhul Hijjah), the day of Nahr (10 Dhul Hijjah), and the three days of Tashriq (11-13 Dhul Hijjah). Understand that Umrah is valid but disliked on these days.
Dislike is tanzihan, meaning it is better to avoid but not sinful.
3
Distinguish ihram locations
For a person in Makkah, ihram for Umrah is taken from the hill (outside the Haram), while for Hajj it is taken from inside the Haram. For an Afaqi coming from outside, ihram is taken at the miqat before entering Makkah.
This distinction is unique to Umrah; for Hajj, the Makki also stays within the Haram.
4
Break down the components
The text states: ihram is a condition (shart), most of tawaf is a pillar (rukn), and the rest (sa'i, halq/taqsir) are wajib. Understand the Hanafi categorization of these acts.
The chosen view is that ihram is shart, tawaf is rukn, others are wajib.
5
Summarize the procedure
Combine: assume ihram from the proper place, then perform tawaf, sa'i, then shave or trim hair. This completes the Umrah and one exits ihram.
The same actions as in Hajj but without standing at Arafah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل العمرة: سنة(1)، وتصح في جميع السَنَةِ، وتكره يوم عرفة ، ويوم النحر، وأيام التشريق. وكيفيتها: أن يحرم لها من بمكة من الحل، بخلاف إحرامه للحج فإنه من الحرم. وأما الآفــاقـي الـذي لم يدخل مكة، فيحرم إذا قصدها من الميقات، ثم يطوف ويسعى لها، ثم يحلق، وقــد حــل منـهـا كمـا بيناه (۲) بحمد الله. [تنبيه] وأفضل الأيام يوم عرفة إذا وافق يوم الجمعة، وهو أفضل من سبعين حجة في غير جمعة، رواه صاحب معراج الدراية بقوله: وقد صح عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أنه قال: « أفضل الأيــام يوم عرفة إذا وافق جمعة، وهو أفضلُ من سبعين حجةٍ ) (۳) ذكره في تجريد الصحاح بعلامة الموطأ، وكذا قاله الزيلعي شارح الكنز. والمجاورة بمكة مكروهة عند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى، لـعــدم القيام بحقوق البيت والحرم ، ونفى الكراهة صاحباه رحمهما الله تعالى.
(۱) أي: مؤكدة على المذهب وصحح في الجوهرة وجوبها وهي إحرام وطواف وحلق أو تقصير فالإحرام شرط ومعظم الطواف ركن وغيرهما واجب هو المختار ويفعل فيها كفعل الحاج ط.
(۲) ص (٦٩٠).
(۳) ذكره ابن حجر في فتح الباري (۲۷۱/۸)، وقال: ذكره رزين في جامعه مرفوعاً. وذكر الحديث ثـم قـال: فهو حديث لا أعرف حاله لأنه لم يذكر صحابية ولا من أخرجه بل أدرجه في حديث الموطأ الذي ذكره مرسلاً عن طلحة بن كريز.
(٤) قال الغزالي رحمه | ه الله في إحياء علوم الدين (۳۲۳/۱): كره الخائفون المحتاطون من العلماء المقام بمكة لمعان ثلاثة الأول: خوف التبرم والأنس بالبيت فإن ذلك ربما يؤثر في تسكين حرقة القلب في الإحترام. الثاني: تهييج الشوق بالمفارقة لتنبعث داعية العود، فإن الله تعالى جعل البيت مثابة للناس وأمناً أي: يثوبون ويعودون إليه مرة أخرى ولا يقضمون منه وطراً. الثالث: الخوف من ركوب الخطايا والذنوب بها، فإن ذلك مخطر، وبالحري أن يورث مقت الله عز وجل لشرف الموضع. ويقال: إن السيئات تضاعف بها كما تضاعف الحسنات. وعن ابن عباس رضي الله عنهما: ذنباً (بركية) وهي منزل بين مكة والطائف، أحب إلي من أن أذنب ذنباً واحداً بمكة. ولهذا كره الإمام المجاورة بمكة.
Chapter of Umrah: It is sunnah (1), and it is valid throughout the entire year, and it is disliked on the day of Arafah, the day of Nahr, and the days of Tashriq. Its procedure: that one assumes ihram for it from Makkah from the hill, contrary to his ihram for Hajj which is from the Haram. As for the Afaqi (one coming from outside) who has not entered Makkah, he assumes ihram when he intends it from the miqat, then he performs tawaf and sa'i for it, then shaves, and he has exited from it as we explained (2) by the praise of Allah. [Note] And the best of days is the day of Arafah if it coincides with Friday, and it is better than seventy Hajjs on a non-Friday, as related by the author of Mi'raj al-Diraya with his statement: It has been authentically reported from the Messenger of Allah (SAW) that he said: 'The best of days is the day of Arafah when it coincides with Friday, and it is better than seventy Hajjs' (3). It was mentioned in Tajrid al-Sihah with the mark of al-Muwatta, and similarly stated by al-Zayla'i, commentator of al-Kanz. Residing in Makkah is disliked according to Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him), due to the lack of fulfilling the rights of the House and the Sanctuary, and his two companions (may Allah have mercy on them) denied the dislike. (1) i.e., confirmed sunnah according to the madhhab, and in al-Jawharah its obligation was declared sahih. It consists of ihram, tawaf, and shaving or trimming. So ihram is a condition, most of tawaf is a pillar, and the rest are wajib; that is the chosen view. One performs in it the same as the pilgrim. (2) Page 690. (3) Ibn Hajar mentioned it in Fath al-Bari (8/271) and said: Razin mentioned it in his Jami' as marfu'. He mentioned the hadith then said: It is a hadith whose status I do not know because he did not mention the Companion nor who narrated it; rather he inserted it into the hadith of al-Muwatta which he mentioned as mursal from Talha ibn Kuraiz. (4) Al-Ghazali said in Ihya' 'Ulum al-Din (1/323): The cautious God-fearing scholars disliked residing in Makkah for three reasons: first, fear of boredom and familiarity with the House, for that might affect calming the heart's burning in veneration. Second, stirring up longing through separation so that the desire to return is ignited, for Allah made the House a place of return (mathaba) and security, i.e., they return to it again and again and do not satisfy their desire from it. Third, fear of committing sins and transgressions there, for that is dangerous, and it is likely to bring about Allah's anger due to the honor of the place. It is said that evil deeds are multiplied there just as good deeds are multiplied. Ibn Abbas (RA) said: A sin at Barkiyya (a station between Makkah and Ta'if) is more beloved to me than committing a single sin in Makkah. Hence the Imam disliked residing in Makkah.
Source pages p. 700

Commentary
This passage from the Chapter of Umrah presents several rulings. First, Umrah is a confirmed sunnah (sunnah mu'akkadah), although some scholars like the author of al-Jawharah stated it is obligatory. The Hanafi relied-upon position is that it is sunnah mu'akkadah. Second, it is valid throughout the year but disliked (makruh tanzihan) on four specific days: the day of Arafah (9th Dhul Hijjah), the day of Nahr (10th Dhul Hijjah), and the three days of Tashriq (11th, 12th, 13th). Third, the procedure: someone in Makkah (a non-Makki resident) must go out to the hill (outside the Haram) to assume ihram for Umrah, unlike for Hajj where one assumes ihram inside the Haram. An Afaqi (one coming from outside the miqat) assumes ihram at the miqat when intending Makkah, then performs tawaf, sa'i, and shaves (or trims) to exit ihram. Fourth, a note mentions the best day is Arafah if it coincides with Friday, citing a hadith that such a day is better than seventy Hajjs on other days, though some question the hadith's chain. Fifth, regarding residing in Makkah (mujawarah), Abu Hanifa considers it makruh due to inability to fulfill the rights of the House, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) deny the karahah. The passage thus provides a comprehensive overview of key Umrah rulings.

Key Terms
عمرة (umrah): The lesser pilgrimage; consists of ihram, tawaf, sa'i, and halq or taqsir.
سنة (sunnah): A confirmed recommended act (sunnah mu'akkadah), not obligatory but constantly practiced by the Prophet.
حل (hill): The area outside the Haram (sanctuary) of Makkah; one must go to the hill to assume ihram for Umrah if resident in Makkah.
مواقيت (mawaqit): Appointed places for ihram for Hajj and Umrah; for Afaqi coming from outside, the miqat is the boundary.
طواف (tawaf): Circumambulation of the Kaaba; most of it (four circuits) is a pillar (rukn) in Hanafi.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
On which days is Umrah disliked according to this passage?
A) The day of Arafah, day of Nahr, and days of Tashriq
B) Only the day of Arafah
C) The last ten days of Ramadan
D) Fridays

Key Takeaway
Umrah is a confirmed sunnah, valid all year except on four specific days, and its ihram location depends on whether you are a Makki or an Afaqi.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
intermediate
10 min
Virtue of Arafah on Friday and the Ruling on Residing in Makkah
Virtue narration and legal dispute on staying in Makkah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the hadith on the virtue of Arafah coinciding with Friday and explain the Hanafi dispute on residing in Makkah (mujawarah).

Core Idea
Arafah on Friday is the best day, better than seventy Hajjs, but the hadith is weak; residing in Makkah is not disliked according to the relied-upon Hanafi position.

The author adds a note on the virtue of the day of Arafah when it falls on Friday, citing a hadith that calls it better than seventy Hajjs. However, scholars note the hadith's chain is questionable. The passage then turns to an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa disliked prolonged residence in Makkah due to spiritual risks, while the Sahibayn saw no harm. Later fatwa follows the Sahibayn. This lesson unpacks both the virtue claim and the legal discussion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the reported virtue
Read the hadith: 'The best of days is the day of Arafah when it coincides with Friday, and it is better than seventy Hajjs on a non-Friday.' Note the source references.
The hadith is cited from Mi'raj al-Diraya and Fath al-Bari, but its chain is mursal and unknown.
2
Evaluate the authenticity
Ibn Hajar al-Asqalani in Fath al-Bari comments that the hadith is mursal, with unknown narrator. Thus its evidentiary value for legal rulings is weak, though it can be used for virtue (fada'il).
Hanafi usul accepts ahad hadith for non-obligatory matters; here it is used for virtue, not obligation.
3
State Abu Hanifa's position on residing in Makkah
Abu Hanifa considered it makruh (disliked) because of fear of failing to fulfill the rights of the House and the possibility of sins being multiplied in the sacred precinct.
The text quotes Ibn Abbas: a sin in Barkiyya is lighter than one in Makkah.
4
State the Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani denied the karahah. They saw no prohibition and allowed prolonged stay.
Their view is considered the mufta bihi in later Hanafi fatwa.
5
Determine the practical difference
The thamarah al-khilaf is whether a person incurs dislike by living in Makkah for an extended period. The mufta bihi removes the dislike.
The mufti should issue the fatwa according to the Sahibayn unless there is a reason to prefer the cautionary view.

Classification of Hajj Violations and Their Expiations
Classifies violations and their expiations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify Hajj violations into four categories based on required expiation and identify the expiation for specific acts.

Core Idea
Hajj violations require graded expiations: dam, sadaqah, less than sadaqah, or market value.

This passage from Nur al-Idah lays out a comprehensive classification of violations (jinaayat) that a muhrim may commit during Hajj or Umrah. Rather than a single penalty, the Shari'ah prescribes a graded system based on the severity of the infraction. Understanding this taxonomy is essential for fulfilling the obligations of Hajj correctly.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish the two broad categories
Violations are either against the state of ihram (e.g., wearing sewn clothes) or against the sanctity of the Haram (e.g., hunting). The second type applies even to non-muhrim.
The category affects the expiation type.
2
Identify the four expiation levels
The passage lists four levels: dam (a sheep), sadaqah (half a sa' of wheat), less than sadaqah (charity as one wishes), and qeemah (market value of game).
Each level corresponds to a set of violations.
3
Match specific acts to their expiation level
From the detailed list, assign acts like perfuming a limb, shaving head, wearing sewn clothes, etc., to the appropriate expiation.
Pay attention to details like 'less than a limb' vs. 'whole limb'.
4
Apply rules for multiple violations and excuses
If multiple violations occur, expiations may combine (e.g., nails adding up to a dam). Acts done due to excuse allow a choice between dam, sadaqah, or fasting.
The text provides specific examples like tawaf while in hadath or janabah.

باب الجنايات: هي على قسمين: جناية على الإحرام، وجناية على الحرم. والثانية: لا تختص بالمحرم وجناية المحرم على أقسام منها ما يوجب دماً(1). ومنها ما يوجب صدقة، هي نصف صاع من بر. ومنها : ما يوجب دون ذلك. ومنها ما يوجب القيمة، وهي جزاء الصيد، ويتعدد الجزاء بتعدد القاتلين المحرمين، فالتي توجب دماً هي: ما لو طيب محرم بالغ عضواً، أو خضـب رأســه بحـنـاء، أو ادهن بزيت ونحوه، أو لبس مخيطاً، أو ستر رأسه يوماً كاملاً، أو حلق ربع رأسه، أو محجمه(2)، أو أحد إبطيه، أو عانته أو رقبته، أو قص أظفار يديه ورجليه بمجلس أو يداً، أو رجلاً، أو ترك واجباً مما تقدم بيانه(3)، وفي أخذ شاريه حكومة(4)، والتي توجب الصدقة بنصف صاع من بر، أو قيمته، هي: ما لو طيب أقل من عضو، أو لبس مخيطاً، أو غطّى رأسه أقل من يوم، أو حلق أقل من ربع رأسه، أو قص ظفراً، وكذا لكل ظفر نصف صاع ، إلا أن يبلغ المجموع دماً(5) فينقص ما شاء منـه كخمسة (6) متفرقة، أو طاف للقدوم، أو للصدر ،محدثاً، وتجب شاة ولو طاف جنباً، أو ترك شوطاً من طواف الصدر، وكذا لكل شوط من أقله، أو حصاة من إحدى الجمار، وكذا لكل حصاة فيما لم يبلغ رمـي يوم إلا أن يبلغ دماً فينقص ما شاء، أو حلق رأس غيره، أو قص أظفاره، وإن تطيب، أو لبس، أو حلـق بعذر تخير بين الذبح، أو التصدق بثلاثة أصوع على ستة مساكين، أو صيام ثلاثة أيام. والتي توجب أقل من نصف صاع، فهي ما لو قتل قملة، أو جرادة، فيتصدق بما شاء والتي توجب القيمة، فهي: ما لو قتل صيداً فيقومه عدلان في مقتله، أو قريب منه، فإن بلغت هدياً فله الخيار إن شاء اشتراه وذبحه، أو اشترى طعاماً وتصدق به لكل فقير نصف صاع أو صام عن طعام كل مسكين يوماً، وإن فضل أقل من نصف صاع تصدق به، أو صام يوماً. وتجب قيمة ما نقص بنتف ريشه الذي لا يـطـيـر بـه وشـعـره، وقطع عضو لا يمنعه الامتناع به وتجب القيمة بقطع بعض قوائمه، ونتف ريشه، وكسر بيضه.

Chapter of Violations: They are of two types: violation against the ihram, and violation against the Haram. The second is not specific to the muhrim. Violations of the muhrim are of several kinds: among them what necessitates a dam (1). Among them what necessitates sadaqah, which is half a sa' of wheat. Among them what necessitates less than that. Among them what necessitates the value, which is the compensation for hunting. And the compensation is multiplied by the multiplicity of the killers who are muhrim. So what necessitates a dam are: if a muhrim adult perfumes a limb, or dyes his head with henna, or oils himself with oil and the like, or wears sewn clothing, or covers his head for a complete day, or shaves a quarter of his head, or shaves the place of cupping (2), or one of his armpits, or his pubic area or his neck, or cuts the nails of his hands and feet in one sitting, or one hand, or one foot, or omits a wajib from what has been previously explained (3), and for taking his mustache there is a hukuma (4). And what necessitates the sadaqah of half a sa' of wheat, or its value, are: if he perfumes less than a limb, or wears sewn clothing, or covers his head less than a day, or shaves less than a quarter of his head, or cuts one nail, and likewise for each nail half a sa', unless the total reaches a dam (5), then he may deduct whatever he wishes from it, like five (6) separate nails, or if he performs tawaf al-qudum or tawaf al-sadr while in a state of minor impurity (hadath). And a sheep is wajib if he performs tawaf while in a state of major impurity (janabah), or omits a single circuit (shout) of tawaf al-sadr, and likewise for each circuit from the minimum, or one pebble from one of the jamarat, and likewise for each pebble in what does not reach the throwing of a day, unless it reaches a dam, then he may deduct whatever he wishes. Or if he shaves someone else's head, or cuts his nails, and if he perfumes, wears, or shaves due to an excuse, he has a choice between slaughtering, or giving charity with three sa' to six poor people, or fasting three days. And what necessitates less than half a sa' is: if he kills a louse or a locust, then he gives charity as he wishes. And what necessitates the value is: if he kills game, then two just men evaluate it at the place of its killing or near it. If it reaches a hady, he has the option: if he wishes, he buys it and slaughters it, or buys food and gives charity with half a sa' per poor person, or fasts one day for the food of each poor person. And if there remains less than half a sa', he gives charity with it or fasts one day. And the value is wajib for the deficiency caused by plucking feathers with which it cannot fly and its hair, and cutting a limb that does not prevent its escape by means of it, and the value is wajib for cutting some of its legs, plucking its feathers, and breaking its eggs. (1) And sometimes two dams may be obligatory, like the violation of a qarin. And 'dam' when used absolutely means a sheep. (2) i.e., shaves the place of cupping. (3) Page 691. (4) i.e., it is considered how much this taken (mustache) is from a quarter of the beard, so he must give food accordingly, so that if it is, for example, like a quarter of a quarter, he is liable for the value of a quarter of a sheep. Al-Hidayah (1/162). (5) i.e., the total of sadaqat equals the value of a sheep. (6) of the nails.

Commentary
This is a comprehensive classification of violations (jinaayat) that a muhrim (one in ihram) may commit during Hajj or Umrah, along with their required expiations. The passage first divides violations into two broad categories: those against the state of ihram and those against the sanctity of the Haram (both areas and animals/plants). It then details the subcategories of violations by the muhrim based on the expiation required: (1) those requiring a dam (a sheep), (2) those requiring sadaqah (half a sa' of wheat), (3) those requiring less than that, and (4) those requiring payment of the market value (for hunting). For each category, specific examples are given: for dam, it includes perfuming a limb, dyeing hair, wearing sewn clothes, covering the head for a full day, shaving a quarter of the head, etc. For sadaqah, it includes small infractions like perfuming less than a limb, wearing sewn clothes briefly, or cutting a single nail. The passage also addresses combined violations and multiple acts. For hunting, the evaluation is done by two just men at the place of killing. The expiation for killing game is either to buy and slaughter a similar animal, give food to the poor, or fast. The passage ends with specific cases like plucking feathers or breaking eggs. This passage is crucial for understanding the graduated penalty system in Hajj.

Key Terms
جناية (jinaayah): A violation or transgression committed during ihram, either against the ihram (e.g., wearing sewn clothes) or against the Haram (e.g., hunting).
دم (dam): The expiation of slaughtering a sheep (shah) for certain violations; in this text, it is a specific category of penalty.
صدقة (sadaqah): Here it means a specific expiation of half a sa' of wheat (or its value) to be given in charity.
قيمة (qeemah): The market value of the game or its part, to be given as expiation or compensation.
جزاء الصيد (jaza' al-sayd): Compensation for killing game while in ihram, analogous to the value of the animal or the equivalent hady.

Key Takeaway
Hajj violations have a graded penalty system: dam, sadaqah, less than sadaqah, or qeemah, based on severity.
