Categories of Offenses (Jinayat) in Hajj
Chapter opening defining two types of jinayat and four expiation categories.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between offenses against ihram and offenses against the Haram, and list the four expiation categories with their triggering offenses.

Core Idea
Hajj offenses split into two types: against ihram or Haram; expiations range from a full blood sacrifice to simple charity.

This passage opens the chapter on jinayat (offenses) during Hajj. It immediately establishes a crucial taxonomic distinction: violations related to the state of ihram and violations related to the sacred precincts themselves. Understanding this division is essential because the second category applies to all persons, not just those in ihram. The passage also previews the scale of expiation that will be detailed later.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two main types of jinayat
Read the first two lines. The passage states 'jinaayah on ihraam and jinaayah on the Haram.' These are the two broad categories.
2
Note the scope of the second type
The text says 'the second is not specific to the Muhrim.' This means violations of the Haram apply to both Muhrim and non-Muhrim.
This is a key difference from offenses against ihram.
3
Enumerate the four expiation categories
List: dam (blood sacrifice), sadaqah (half sa' of wheat), less than that, and qimah (compensation for hunting).
These are the general categories; specific rulings assign each offense to one of these.
4
Understand the multiplication rule for hunting
The passage states 'the penalty multiplies with the number of killers who are Muhrims.' If multiple Muhrims kill the same game, each owes a separate penalty.
This is unique to hunting offenses (qimah).
5
Recognize the structural role of this passage
This is a framework. Subsequent lessons will fill in details for each expiation category and which offenses trigger them.
Do not expect complete rulings here; this is a roadmap.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الجنايات: هي على قسمين: جناية على الإحرام، وجناية على الحرم. والثانية: لا تختص بالمحرم. وجناية المحرم على أقسام: منها ما يوجب دماً، ومنها ما يوجب صدقة، هي نصف صاع من بر، ومنها ما يوجب دون ذلك، ومنها ما يوجب القيمة، وهي جزاء الصيد، ويتعدد الجزاء بتعدد القاتلين المحرمين.
Chapter of Offenses: They are of two types: an offense against ihram, and an offense against the Haram. The second is not specific to the Muhrim. The offenses of the Muhrim are of categories: some necessitate a blood sacrifice (dam), some necessitate charity, which is half a sa' of wheat, some necessitate less than that, and some necessitate compensation (qimah), which is the penalty for hunting, and the penalty multiplies with the number of killers who are Muhrims.

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on jinayat (offenses) during Hajj. The author first divides jinayat into two broad categories: those that violate the state of ihram and those that violate the sanctity of the Haram (the sacred precincts). The second category, violations of the Haram, applies to both Muhrim and non-Muhrim alike. The author then lists the four types of expiations required for various offenses: dam (a blood sacrifice, typically a sheep), sadaqah (charity of half a sa' of wheat), less than half a sa' (for minor offenses), and qimah (market value compensation) specifically for hunting. He notes that if multiple Muhrims kill the same game, each owes a separate penalty. This sets the framework for the detailed rulings that follow in the chapter. No proofs are cited here; it is a statement of the legal categories.

Key Terms
جناية (jināyah): An offense or violation that incurs a legal penalty, specifically during Hajj.
دم (dam): A blood sacrifice, usually a sheep, required as expiation for certain Hajj violations.
صدقة (ṣadaqah): Charity given as expiation, here specifically half a sa' of wheat.
قيمة (qīmah): Compensation equal to the market value of the item, used for hunting penalties.

Offenses Requiring Dam and Sadaqah in Hajj
Listing specific offenses with corresponding expiations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the specific offenses during Hajj that require dam and those that require sadaqah, and identify the ruling for actions performed with an excuse.

Core Idea
Dam for major violations, sadaqah for minor; but accumulation can upgrade minor to major.

This passage enumerates the expiations required for various violations of ihram during Hajj. It distinguishes between two levels: dam (a sheep) for more substantial offenses, and sadaqah (half a sa' of wheat) for lesser ones. Additionally, it provides a ruling for those who act under duress, granting a choice among three alternatives. Understanding these categories is essential for any pilgrim.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary categories
The passage divides expiations into dam (blood) and sadaqah (charity). Locate the two main sections beginning with 'those that necessitate a dam' and 'those that necessitate sadaqah'.
2
List dam-causing offenses
Scan the first list: perfuming a whole limb, dyeing head with henna, oiling hair, wearing stitched clothing (for a full day is implied), covering head a full day, shaving a quarter or more of the head or specific areas (cupping spot, armpit, pubic area, neck), trimming all nails in one sitting, omitting an obligatory act, and trimming the mustache (hukuumah). Also included later: performing tawaf while junub, omitting a circuit of farewell tawaf, and missing a pebble from jamarat if the total equals a dam.
Wearing stitched clothing without time qualifier is understood to apply to a full day; see the sadaqah list for less than a day.
3
List sadaqah-causing offenses
The second list includes: perfuming less than a limb, wearing stitched clothing (for less than a day), covering head less than a day, shaving less than a quarter of the head, trimming a single nail (half sa' per nail, cumulative), performing arrival or farewell tawaf while in minor impurity (hadath), omitting a single circuit of these tawafs, or missing a pebble from jamarat (each pebble half sa' unless total reaches a dam).
Note: some offenses appear in both lists but with different extents or contexts.
4
Understand accumulation and deduction
When multiple minor offenses (like trimming several nails) reach the value of a dam, the pilgrim may deduct as he wishes from the total. For example, trimming five nails separately equals two and a half sa', which is less than a dam, so half sa' each; but if the total reaches a dam, he can offer one dam instead.
The text states 'إلا أن يبلغ المجموع دماً فينقص ما شاء منه'.
5
Apply the excuse ruling
If a pilgrim applies perfume, wears stitched clothing, or shaves due to a valid excuse (e.g., illness, extreme heat), he has a threefold choice: slaughter a sheep, give three sa' of food to six poor persons, or fast three days. This is an alternative to the fixed expiations.
This choice is specific to actions done under duress, not voluntary violations.

فالتي توجب دماً هي: ما لو طيب محرم بالغ عضواً، أو خضب رأسه بحناء، أو ادهن بزيت ونحوه، أو لبس مخيطاً، أو ستر رأسه يوماً كاملاً، أو حلق ربع رأسه، أو محجمه، أو أحد إبطيه، أو عانته أو رقبته، أو قص أظفار يديه ورجليه بمجلس أو يداً، أو رجلاً، أو ترك واجباً مما تقدم بيانه، وفي أخذ شاريه حكومة. والتي توجب الصدقة بنصف صاع من بر، أو قيمته، هي: ما لو طيب أقل من عضو، أو لبس مخيطاً، أو غطى رأسه أقل من يوم، أو حلق أقل من ربع رأسه، أو قص ظفراً، وكذا لكل ظفر نصف صاع، إلا أن يبلغ المجموع دماً فينقص ما شاء منه كخمسة متفرقة، أو طاف للقدوم أو للصدر محدثاً، وتجب شاة ولو طاف جنباً، أو ترك شوطاً من طواف الصدر، وكذا لكل شوط من أقله، أو حصاة من إحدى الجمار، وكذا لكل حصاة فيما لم يبلغ رمي يوم إلا أن يبلغ دماً فينقص ما شاء، أو حلق رأس غيره، أو قص أظفاره، وإن تطيب أو لبس أو حلق بعذر تخير بين الذبح أو التصدق بثلاثة أصوع على ستة مساكين أو صيام ثلاثة أيام.
Those that necessitate a dam are: if a Muhrim perfumes a whole limb, or dyes his head with henna, or oils with oil or similar, or wears stitched clothing, or covers his head a full day, or shaves a quarter of his head, or his cupping spot, or one of his armpits, or his pubic area or his neck, or trims the nails of both hands and feet in one sitting, or one hand or one foot, or omits an obligatory act mentioned previously, and in taking his mustache there is a discretionary valuation. And those that necessitate sadaqah of half a sa' of wheat or its value are: if he perfumes less than a limb, or wears stitched clothing, or covers his head less than a day, or shaves less than a quarter of his head, or trims one nail, and likewise for each nail half a sa', unless the total reaches a dam, then he may deduct whatever he wishes from it, like five [nails] separate; or he performs the arrival tawaf or farewell tawaf in a state of minor impurity (hadath), and a sheep becomes obligatory if he performs tawaf while junub, or omits one circuit of the farewell tawaf, and likewise for each circuit from its minimum, or one pebble from one of the jamarat, and likewise for each pebble as long as it does not reach the throwing of one day, unless it reaches a dam then he may deduct whatever he wishes; or he shaves another's head, or trims his nails, and if he applies perfume, or wears stitched clothing, or shaves due to an excuse, he has the choice between slaughtering, or giving charity with three sa' to six poor persons, or fasting three days.
Source pages p. 701

Commentary
This passage details the first two categories of expiations: dam and sadaqah. The author lists specific actions that obligate a full dam (a sheep): applying perfume to a whole limb, dyeing the head with henna, oiling hair, wearing stitched clothing, covering the head for a full day, shaving a quarter of the head or less (cupping spot, armpit, pubic area, neck), trimming all nails of hands and feet in one session, or omitting any wajib act mentioned earlier. For smaller amounts, such as perfuming less than a limb, covering the head less than a day, shaving less than a quarter, or trimming a single nail, the expiation is half a sa' of wheat per nail. However, if the total from such minor violations equals the value of a sheep (dam), the Muhrim may deduct as he wishes. Additional acts requiring sadaqah include performing the arrival or farewell tawaf in a state of minor impurity (though if in major impurity, a sheep is obligatory), omitting a circuit of farewell tawaf, or missing a pebble at the jamarat. If the omission reaches the value of a sheep, deduction applies. For shaving another's head or trimming their nails, the ruling is similar. When there is an excuse for using perfume, wearing stitched clothing, or shaving, the Muhrim has a choice: slaughter a sheep, give three sa' of food to six poor persons, or fast three days. This detailed enumeration helps the student identify specific violations and their corresponding expiations.

Key Terms
حكومة (ḥukūmah): A discretionary valuation by an expert to determine the compensation for an action like trimming the mustache.
مخيط (makhīṭ): Stitched clothing; wearing it is prohibited during ihram and requires expiation.
جنب (junub): State of major ritual impurity requiring ghusl; performing tawaf in this state incurs a sheep (dam).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Half a sa' of wheat
B) A blood sacrifice (dam)
C) Fasting three days
D) Nothing

Key Takeaway
Hajj violations have graded expiations: dam for major, sadaqah for minor, and a choice when excused.

Offenses Requiring Less Than Half Sa' and Compensation for Hunting
Explaining minor offenses requiring minimal charity and detailed rules for hunting compensation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three categories of hunting expiations (less than half sa', qimah, partial damages) and state the conditions for each.

Core Idea
Hunting penalties in ihram vary: from voluntary charity for a louse to full qimah for game; fasting only when value reaches a hady.

Having covered major expiations requiring a full dam (sacrifice) or more, this passage completes the scale by addressing minor offenses that require less than half a sa' of charity and the detailed rules for qimah (market value) for killing game or damaging it. Understanding these graduated penalties ensures that the pilgrim fulfills his obligation correctly and does not fall into invalid forms of expiation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two main categories
The passage opens by distinguishing offenses that require tasharruf (discretionary charity, less than half sa') from those requiring qimah (determined valuation). The former applies to killing a louse or locust; the latter to killing game.
2
Understand the valuation process
For game, the offender must have two just Muslim men (adlan) assess the animal's market value at the place of killing or nearby. This establishes the baseline for expiation.
3
Explore the three options when value reaches a hady
If the valuation equals the price of a sacrificial animal (hady), the pilgrim may choose: (a) buy and slaughter that animal, (b) purchase food and give half a sa' to each poor person, or (c) fast one day for each half sa' of food. Any fractional remainder is similarly expiated.
Fasting is only valid when the value reaches hady; it is not a general option.
4
Note special cases and restrictions
The passage lists partial damages (plucking feathers, cutting limbs, breaking eggs) that incur qimah. It also covers exceptions: killing a predatory animal (sabu') does not exceed one sheep, and if it attacks, nothing is due. Importantly, a non-Muhrim who kills game in the Haram cannot substitute fasting; only qimah applies. Cutting naturally growing vegetation in the Haram also requires qimah, except for Idhkhir and truffles.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والتي توجب أقل من نصف صاع، فهي ما لو قتل قملة، أو جرادة، فيتصدق بما شاء. والتي توجب القيمة، فهي: ما لو قتل صيداً فيقومه عدلان في مقتله، أو قريب منه، فإن بلغت هدياً فله الخيار إن شاء اشتراه وذبحه، أو اشترى طعاماً وتصدق به لكل فقير نصف صاع أو صام عن طعام كل مسكين يوماً، وإن فضل أقل من نصف صاع تصدق به، أو صام يوماً. وتجب قيمة ما نقص بنتف ريشه الذي لا يطير به وشعره، وقطع عضو لا يمنعه الامتناع به وتجب القيمة بقطع بعض قوائمه، ونتف ريشه، وكسر بيضه. (1) وقد يجب بها دمان كجناية القارن. ولا يجاوز عن شاة بقتل السبع، وإن صال لا شيء بقتله، ولا يجزئ الصوم بقتل الحلال صيد الحرم، ولا بقطع حشيش الحرم، وشجره النابت بنفسه، وليس مما ينبته الناس بل القيمة. وحرم رعي حشيش الحرم وقطعه إلا الإذخر والكمأة.
And those that necessitate less than half a sa' are: if he kills a louse or a locust, then he gives charity as he wishes. And those that necessitate compensation (qimah) are: if he kills game, then two just men evaluate it at the place of killing or near it. If it reaches the value of a Hady (sacrificial animal), then he has the choice: if he wishes, he buys it and slaughters it, or he buys food and gives it in charity to each poor person half a sa', or he fasts for the food of each poor person a day. And if there remains less than half a sa', he gives it in charity or fasts a day. And compensation is obligatory for the deficiency caused by plucking feathers with which it cannot fly, or its hair, or cutting a limb that does not prevent its ability to escape, and compensation is obligatory for cutting some of its legs, plucking its feathers, and breaking its eggs. (1) And sometimes two dams may be obligatory, like the offense of a Qarin. And one does not exceed a sheep for killing a predatory animal, and if it attacks, nothing is due for killing it. And fasting is not acceptable for a non-Muhrim killing game of the Haram, nor for cutting the grass of the Haram or its trees that grow naturally, not what people plant; rather compensation is due. And it is prohibited to graze the grass of the Haram and to cut it except Idhkhir and truffles (Kam'ah).
Source pages p. 701

Commentary
This lesson covers the remaining two categories of expiation: less than half a sa' and qimah (market value). For killing a louse or locust, the Muhrim may give any amount of charity. For killing game, the penalty is the market value determined by two just men at the location. If the value equals that of a sacrificial animal (hady), the offender has three options: buy and slaughter it, buy food and give half a sa' per poor person, or fast one day per half sa' of food. Any remaining fraction is similarly expiated. The passage also details compensation for partial damage to game: plucking feathers essential for flight, cutting hair, or severing a limb that doesn't prevent escape all require compensation. Breaking eggs also requires compensation. A footnote notes that sometimes two dams are due, as for a Qarin (one performing Hajj and Umrah together). For killing a predatory animal (like a wolf or tiger), the penalty does not exceed one sheep, and if the animal attacks, no penalty is owed. Importantly, fasting is not accepted as expiation for a non-Muhrim who kills game in the Haram; only qimah is valid. Cutting naturally growing grass or trees of the Haram also requires qimah, and grazing is prohibited except for Idhkhir (a fragrant grass) and truffles. This passage illustrates the nuanced approach to expiations based on the nature of the violation.

Key Terms
صيد (ṣayd): Wild game animals or birds that are permissible to eat when hunted outside ihram.
عدلان (ʿadlān): Two just, upright Muslim men who determine the market value of the game at the place of killing.
هدي (hady): A sacrificial animal (typically a sheep, goat, or cow) brought to the Haram for slaughter.
قارن (qārin): A pilgrim performing Hajj and Umrah together in one state of ihram, incurring additional obligations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the expiation for killing a louse by a Muhrim?
A) Half a sa' of wheat
B) A blood sacrifice (dam)
C) Any amount of charity he wishes
D) Compensation (qimah)

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prescribes a graduated system of expiation for hunting violations, with cash value (qimah) as the baseline, and fasting only allowed when the value reaches the price of a sacrificial animal.

Animals Whose Killing Requires No Expiation
Listing animals exempt from expiation for a Muhrim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the animals a Muhrim may kill without penalty and state the general principle that only game (sayd) requires expiation.

Core Idea
A Muhrim may kill harmful and non-game animals without penalty; only game requires expiation.

This short passage enumerates specific animals that a person in the state of Ihram may kill without incurring any expiation. The list includes common pests and harmful creatures, and the general rule is that any animal not considered 'game' (sayd) falls under this exemption. Understanding this list helps pilgrims avoid unnecessary worry during Hajj and Umrah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The passage begins with 'ولا شيء بقتل' meaning 'nothing is owed for killing.' This establishes that killing these animals incurs no expiation (fidyah or dam).
The ruling applies only to a Muhrim (pilgrim in ihram).
2
List the specific animals
Read through the list: crow, kite, scorpion, mouse, snake, ferocious dog, mosquito, ant, flea, tick, and turtle. Note that these are either harmful or not considered edible wild game.
Some animals like crow and kite are birds but are excluded due to their harmfulness.
3
Extract the general principle
The passage ends with 'وما ليس بصيد' meaning 'and anything that is not game.' This is the key principle: any animal that does not fall under the legal definition of 'sayd' (edible wild animals) can be killed without penalty.
Sayd in Hanafi fiqh refers to edible wild animals that are permissible to hunt outside ihram.
4
Apply the principle to new cases
Using the 'not game' principle, determine whether other animals would be exempt. For example, a cockroach or a wasp would be exempt because they are not sayd, whereas a gazelle or rabbit would require expiation.
The list is illustrative; the principle extends to all non-game creatures.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل: ولا شيء بقتل غراب، وحدأة، وعقرب، وفأرة، وحية، وكلب عقور، وبعوض، ونمل، وبرغوث، وقراد وسلحفاة، وما ليس بصيد.
Section: And nothing [is owed] for killing a crow, a kite, a scorpion, a mouse, a snake, a ferocious dog, mosquitoes, ants, fleas, ticks, and a turtle, and anything that is not game.
Source pages p. 702

Commentary
This short section (fasl) specifies a list of animals that a Muhrim may kill without incurring any expiation. The list includes common pests and harmful creatures: crow, kite (a bird of prey), scorpion, mouse, snake, ferocious dog, mosquito, ant, flea, tick, and turtle. The general principle is that any animal that is not considered 'sayd' (game) in the legal sense can be killed without penalty. Sayd is typically defined as edible wild animals that are permissible to hunt when not in ihram. Harmful animals, even if they are birds or creatures that might otherwise be hunted, are excluded from penalty because of their harmfulness. This ruling provides relief for pilgrims who may encounter such creatures during their journey.

Key Terms
فصل (faṣl): A section or chapter division within the book, here separating specific rulings.
ما ليس بصيد (mā laysa biṣayd): Anything that is not considered legally game, i.e., not an edible wild animal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) A deer
B) A crow
C) A rabbit
D) A dove

Key Takeaway
Only game animals (sayd) require expiation when killed by a Muhrim; harmful and non-game animals are exempt.

Penalties for Killing Predators and Cutting Plants in the Haram
States penalties for killing predators and cutting plants while in ihram.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings for killing predatory animals and cutting plants while in ihram, and identify the exceptions for attacking predators and for idhkhir and truffles.

Core Idea
Killing a predator that attacks incurs no penalty; cutting Haram grass requires value; idhkhir and truffles are exempt.

When in ihram, certain actions that are normally permissible become restricted. This passage from Nur al-Idah details the penalties for killing predatory animals and cutting plants in the Haram. Understanding these rulings is essential for anyone performing Hajj or Umrah, as they involve compensations that must be fulfilled.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
For each act mentioned—killing a predator, killing an attacking predator, killing game, cutting grass—determine the required penalty (sheep, nothing, sacrifice, or value).
The passage explicitly states each ruling.
2
Note the exceptions
Killing a predator that attacks incurs no penalty. Cutting idhkhir and truffles is permitted.
These exceptions are based on hadith and Hanafi rulings.
3
Understand the compensation
Fasting does not suffice for killing game of the Haram or for cutting plants; only sacrifice or payment of market value is accepted.
This is a key distinction from other expiations.
4
Apply the rulings to scenarios
Use the rulings to answer questions about hypothetical situations in the Haram while in ihram.
Practice makes these memorization anchors stick.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يجاوز عن شاة بقتل السبع، وإن صال لا شيء بقتله، ولا يجزئ الصوم بقتل الحلال صيد الحرم، ولا بقطع حشيش الحرم، وشجره النابت بنفسه، وليس مما ينبته الناس بل القيمة. وحرم رعي حشيش الحرم وقطعه إلا الإذخر والكمأة.
And it is not exceeded from a sheep for killing a predator, and if it attacks, nothing [is due] for killing it, and fasting does not suffice for killing the permissible [game] of the Haram, nor for cutting the grass of the Haram, and its trees that grow by themselves and are not what people cultivate; rather, [the penalty is] the value. And it is prohibited to graze the grass of the Haram and cut it except al-idhkhir and truffles.
Source pages p. 702

Commentary
This passage lists rulings for a person in ihram who kills certain animals or cuts plants. The first ruling: killing a predator (such as a leopard or wolf) requires a sheep. If the predator attacks the person, then killing it incurs no penalty. Next, fasting (as a substitute for sacrifice) does not suffice for killing game of the Haram; only a sacrifice is accepted. Similarly, cutting grass or trees of the Haram requires payment of the market value, not fasting. Finally, it is prohibited to graze or cut the grass of the Haram, with an exception for two types: idhkhir (a fragrant plant) and truffles, which are permissible to cut. These exceptions are recognized in the Hanafi school based on established rulings.

Key Terms
السبع (al-sabuʿ): Predatory animals that attack, such as lions, wolves, and leopards.
الحلال (al-ḥalāl): Here it refers to the permissible game animals of the Haram that a muhrim may not hunt.
القيمة (al-qīmah): Monetary value assessed as compensation for cutting plants or trees of the Haram.
الإذخر (al-idhkhir): A fragrant plant (Andropogon schoenanthus) that is exempted from the prohibition of cutting.
الكمأة (al-kamʾah): Truffles, a type of fungus that grows underground and is exempt from cutting prohibition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a muhrim kills a wolf that attacks him, what penalty is required?
A) A sheep
B) Nothing
C) Fasting
D) A camel

Key Takeaway
The Haram has specific penalties: killing a predator requires a sheep (unless it attacks), killing game requires a sacrifice (fasting not accepted), cutting plants requires payment of value, and only idhkhir and truffles are exempt.

The Chapter on Hady: Rulings of Sacrificial Animals for Hajj
Defines hady, its minimum, permissible animals, and rules for sacrifice and treatment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the minimum animal for hady, identify the two violations requiring a camel, apply the rules for sacrificing and treating hady animals, and determine the ruling for a vow of walking hajj.

Core Idea
A sheep suffices for most hady, but a camel is obligatory for tawaf in janabah and intercourse before halq.

This lesson unpacks the rulings of hady (sacrificial animals) as presented in Nur al-Idah. You will learn the minimum acceptable animal, the exceptions requiring a camel, the timing and location of sacrifice, and how to treat the animal before and after. These rules are essential for anyone performing hajj tamattu', qiran, or expiatory sacrifices.

Guided Path
1
Identify Key Terms
Understand terms: hady (sacrificial animal for hajj), shah (sheep/goat), badanah (camel), taqlid (garlanding), jilal (saddlecloth), khitam (halter), nuqakh (cold water).
These terms are specific to sacrificial animals in hajj context.
2
Extract the General Rule and Exceptions
The general rule is that a sheep suffices for all hady. Identify the two exceptions requiring a camel: tawaf of the pillar while in janabah and intercourse after wuquf before halq.
The camel is obligatory for these two violations only.
3
Analyze Timing and Place of Sacrifice
The hady of tamattu' and qiran must be sacrificed on the day of Nahr. All hady must be sacrificed within the Haram, except a voluntary offering that becomes defective on the way.
If defective, it is sacrificed where it occurs and given entirely in charity.
4
Apply Rules for Treating the Animal
Garlanding is only for voluntary camel, tamattu', and qiran. The saddlecloth and halter are given in charity. The slaughterman's wage is not taken from the animal. No riding without necessity. Milking only if far from Haram, then milk given in charity. If near, sprinkle udder with water.
These rules preserve the sanctity of the hady.
5
Determine Ruling for Vow of Walking Hajj
If one vows to walk, it becomes binding. He must not ride until after tawaf al-ifadah. If he rides before, he must sacrifice an animal. Walking is superior to riding for those able.
This applies to a vow, not obligatory hajj itself.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل الهدي: الهدي أدناه شاة، وهو من الإبل والبقر والغنم، وما جاز في الضحايا جاز في الهدايا. والشاة تجوز في كل شيء إلا في طواف الركن جنباً، ووطء بعد الوقوف قبل الحلق، ففي كل منهما بدنة. وخصص هدي المتعة والقران بيوم النحر فقط، وخصص ذبح كل هدي بالحرم، إلا أن يكون تطوعاً وتعيَّب في الطريق، فينحر في محله، ولا يأكله بمنى، وفقير الحرم وغيره سواء. وتقلد بدنة التطوع والمتعة والقران فقط، ويتصدق بجلاله وخطامه، ولا يعطى أجر الجزار منه، ولا يركبه بلا ضرورة، ولا يحلب لبنه إلا إن بعد المحل فيتصدق به، وينضح ضرعه إن قرب المحل بالنقاخ. ولو نذر حجاً ماشياً لزمه، ولا يركب حتى يطوف للركن، فإن ركب أراق دماً. وفضل المشي على الركوب للقادر عليه، وفقنا الله تعالى بفضله، ومنَّ علينا بالعود على أحسن حال إليه، بجاه سيدنا محمد.
Chapter of Hady: The minimum of hady is a sheep, and it is from camels, cattle, and sheep/goats. And whatever is permissible for udhiyah is permissible for hady. And a sheep suffices for everything except for circumambulation of the corner while in major impurity, and intercourse after standing at Arafat before shaving, so for each of these two, a camel is required. And the hady of tamattu' and qiran is specified to the day of Nahr only, and the slaughter of every hady is specified to the Haram, unless it is a voluntary offering and it becomes defective on the way, then it is slaughtered in its place, and he does not eat from it in Mina, and the poor of the Haram and others are equal. And a camel of voluntary offering, tamattu', and qiran alone are garlanded, and the saddlecloth and halter are given in charity, and the slaughterman's wage is not given from it, nor is it ridden without necessity, nor is its milk milked unless the place is far, then it is given in charity, and its udder is sprinkled with water if slaughter is near. And if one vows to perform hajj walking, it is binding upon him, and he should not ride until he performs the tawaf of the pillar; if he rides, he pours blood (sacrifices). And walking is superior to riding for one who is able. May Allah grant us success by His grace and bestow upon us return in the best condition, by the status of our master Muhammad.
Source pages p. 702

Commentary
This chapter of the text explains the rulings of hady (sacrificial animals) in the context of hajj. It begins by stating the minimum acceptable animal: a sheep (jadh'ah or thaniyyah). The permissible animals are camels, cows, and goats/sheep—the same as those for udhiyah (Eid sacrifice). The general rule is that a sheep can be used for all expiations except two specific violations: performing tawaf of the pillar (tawaf al-ifadah) while in a state of janabah (major impurity), and engaging in sexual intercourse after standing at Arafat but before shaving the head (halq). For each of these two violations, a camel (badanah) is required. The hady for tamattu' and qiran must be sacrificed specifically on the day of Nahr (10th Dhul Hijjah). All hady must be sacrificed within the boundaries of the Haram. However, if a voluntary hady becomes defective (e.g., gets injured) on the way, it is sacrificed where it is, and the owner does not eat from it; rather, it is given entirely in charity. In such a case, the poor of the Haram and those outside are equal recipients. The practice of garlanding (taqlid) is only for the camel of a voluntary offering, tamattu', and qiran. The saddlecloth (jilal) and halter (khitam) of the animal should be given in charity. The wage of the slaughterman is not taken from the hady; it must be paid separately. The animal may not be ridden without necessity. Its milk should not be milked unless the place is far from the Haram; if milked, the milk is given in charity. If the animal is near the slaughter place, the udder is sprinkled with cold water to dry up the milk. The text then discusses a vow to perform hajj on foot: it becomes binding, and the person must not ride until after performing the obligatory tawaf (tawaf al-ifadah). If he rides before that, he must offer a sacrifice. Finally, walking is considered superior to riding for those who are physically able. The chapter ends with a supplication.

Key Terms
الهدي (al-hady): The sacrificial animal brought to the Haram as an offering for hajj or expiation.
الشاة (al-shāh): A sheep or goat, the minimum acceptable animal for most hady.
البدنة (al-badanah): A camel (or cow) required for the two specified violations: tawaf in janabah and intercourse before halq.
التقليد (al-taqlīd): Garlanding the animal with a rope or shoe to mark it as a hady.
الجلال (al-jilāl): The covering or saddlecloth placed on the camel's back.
الخطام (al-khiṭām): The halter or rein of the camel.
النقاخ (al-nuqākh): Cold, fresh water used to sprinkle the udder to reduce milk.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
For which two violations is a camel (badanah) required instead of a sheep for hady?
A) Tawaf without wudu and cutting nails
B) Tawaf of the pillar while in janabah and intercourse after wuquf before halq
C) Missing stoning and shaving early
D) Wearing sewn clothes and covering the head

Key Takeaway
A sheep is the default minimum for hady, but a camel is obligatory for tawaf in janabah and intercourse before halq; additionally, the sacrifice must be in the Haram on the specified day, and the animal must be treated with sanctity.

Etiquette of Visiting the Prophet's Grave and the Caliphs
Describes the complete etiquette of visiting the Prophet's grave and the righteous caliphs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the recommended Hanafi etiquette for visiting the Prophet's grave and the graves of the Caliphs, and explain the legal status of each step.

Core Idea
Visiting the Prophet's grave is a recommended act of devotion with specific etiquettes.

This lesson outlines the detailed etiquette (adab) for visiting the Prophet Muhammad's grave and the graves of his two companions, Abu Bakr and Umar, as practiced in the Hanafi school. The author of Imdad al-Fattah expands on the basic ruling from Nur al-Idah, providing a step-by-step guide for the visitor. Understanding these etiquettes is important for anyone performing ziyarah to Madinah, as it reflects the deep love and respect for the Prophet and his companions.

Guided Path
1
Position yourself correctly
Stand facing the Prophet's grave, with your back to the qibla. This shows respect and ensures you are facing his noble face.
The qibla direction is opposite; one turns away from it to face the grave.
2
Recite the intercession supplication
Recite the long supplication including Qur'an 4:64 and ask for the Prophet's intercession (shafa'ah). Say 'ash-shafa'ah' three times. If someone requested you to convey greetings, do so.
The verse provides the textual basis for seeking forgiveness through the Prophet.
3
Greet Abu Bakr and Umar
Move about a cubit to align with Abu Bakr's head, greet and praise him. Then move similarly to align with Umar's head and greet him. Afterwards, step back half a cubit and address both together.
These greetings acknowledge their virtues and companionship with the Prophet.
4
Return to the Prophet's head for final prayer
Go back to the spot opposite the Prophet's head and recite another supplication ending with Qur'anic verses (al-Baqarah 201, as-Saffat 180-182).
This reinforces the purpose of the visit and asks for good in this world and the Hereafter.
5
Visit other blessed sites
Proceed to the pillar of Abu Lubaba (between grave and pulpit) for voluntary prayer, then to the Rawdah for more prayer and dhikr, then to the pulpit to touch the pomegranate-shaped knob, and finally to the 'yearning pillar' (with remnant of the palm trunk).
Each site has historical significance; these acts seek blessings from the Prophet's traces.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بالحلول بين يديك، وقد جئناك من بلاد شاسعة، وأمكنة بعيدة، نقطع السهل والوعر بقصد زيارتك، لنفوز بشفاعتك، والنظر إلى مآثرك ومعاهدك، والقيام بقضاء بعض حقك، والاستشفاع بك إلى ربنا، فإن الخطايا قد قصمت ظهورنا، والأوزار قد أثقلت كواهلنا، وأنت الشافع المشفّع، الموعود بالشفاعة العظمى، والمقام المحمود والوسيلة، وقد قال الله تعالى: ﴿وَلَوْ أَنَّهُمْ إِذْ ظَلَمُوا أَنفُسَهُمْ جَاءُوكَ فَاسْتَغْفَرُوا اللهَ وَاسْتَغْفَرَ لَهُمُ الرَّسُولُ لَوَجَدُوا اللهَ تَوَّابًا رَّحِيمًا [النساء : ٦٤]، وقد جئناك ظالمين لأنفسنا، مستغفرين لذنوبنا، فاشفع لنا إلى ربك، واسأله أن يميتنـا عـلـى سُنَّتك، وأن يحشرنا في زمرتك، وأن يوردنا حوضك، وأن يسقينا بكأسك، غير خزايا ولا ندامي الشفاعة الشفاعة الشفاعة يا رسول الله، يقولها ثلاثاً ربنا اغفر لنا، ولإخواننا الذين سبقونا بالإيمان، ولا تجعل في قلوبنا غلاً للذين آمنوا، ربَّنا إنك رؤوف رحيم. وتبلغه سلام من أوصاك به فتقول: السلام عليك يا رسول الله من فلان بن فلان يتشفّع بك إلى ربك فاشفع له وللمسلمين، ثم تصلي عليه وتدعو بما شئت عند وجهه الكريم مستدبر القبلة، ثم تتحول قدر ذراع حتى تحاذي رأس الصديق أبي بكر – رضي الله تعالى عنه - وتقول: السلام عليك يا خليفة رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ، السلام عليــك يـا صاحب رسول الله، وأنيسه في الغار، ورفيقه في الأسفار، وأمينه في الأسرار، جزاك الله عنا أفضل ما جزى إماماً عن أمة نبيه، فلقد خلفته بأحسن خلف، وسلكت طريقه ومنهاجـه خـيـر مسلك، وقاتلت أهل الردة والبدع، ومهدت الإسلام، وشيدت أركانه، فكنت خير إمام، ووصلت الأرحام، ولم تزل قائماً بالحق ناصراً للدين ولأهله حتى أتاك اليقين، سل الله سبحانه لنا دوام حبك، والحشـر مــع حزبك، وقبول زيارتنا، والسلام عليك ورحمة الله وبركاته. ثم تتحول مثل ذلك حتى تحاذي رأس أمير المؤمنين عمر بن الخطاب - رضي الله تعالى . عنه - فتقول: السلام عليك يا أمير المؤمنين، السلام عليك يا مظهر الإسلام السلام عليك يا مكسر الأصنام جزاك الله عنا أفضل الجزاء لقـد نصرت الإسلام والمسلمين، وفتحت معظم البلاد بعد سيد المرسلين، وكفلت الأيتام، ووصلت الأرحام، وقوي بك الإسلام، وكنت للمسلمين إماماً مرضياً؛ وهادياً مهدياً، جمعت شملهم، وأعنت فقيرهم، وجبرت كسرهم، السَّلام عليك ورحمة الله وبركاته، ثم ترجع قدر نصف ذراع فتقول:
- ٧٠٥ -
السلام عليكما يا ضجيعي رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ورفيقيه، ووزيريه، ومشيريه، والمعاونين لـه عـلـى الـقـيـام بالدين، والقائمين بعده بمصالح المسلمين، جزاكما الله أحسن الجزاء، جئناكما نتوسل بكمـا إلى رسول الله ليشفع لنا، ويسأل الله ربنا أن يتقبل سعينا، ويحيينا على ملته، ويميتنا عليها، ويحشرنا في زمرته، ثم يدعو لنفسه ولوالديه، ولمن أوصاه بالدعاء ولجميع المسلمين. ثم يقف عند رأس النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم كالأول ويقول اللهم إنك قلت وقولك الحق وَلَوْ أَنَّهُمْ إِذْ ظَلَمُوا أَنفُسَهُمْ جَاءُوكَ فَاسْتَغْفَرُوا اللَّهَ وَاسْتَغْفَرَ لَهُمُ الرَّسُولُ لَوَجَدُوا اللهَ تَوَّابًا رَحِيمًا [النساء : ٦٤] وقد جئناك سامعين قولك طائعين أمرك، مستشفعين بنبيك إليك. اللهم ربنا اغفر لنا، ولآبائنا وأمهاتنا، وإخواننا الذين سبقونا بالإيمان، ولا تجعل في قلوبنا غلاً للذين آمنوا، ربَّنا إِنَّك رؤوف رحيم ﴿رَبَّنَا ابْنَا فِي الدُّنْيَا حَسَنَةً وَفِي الْآخِرَةِ حَسَنَةً وَقِنَا عَذَابَ النَّارِ ﴾ [البقرة: ٢٠١] سُبْحَانَ رَبِّكَ رَبِّ الْعِزَّةِ عَمَّا يَصِفُونَ وَسَلَامُ عَلَى الْمُرْسَلِينَ وَالْحَمْدُ لِلَّهِ رَبِّ الْعَالَمِينَ ﴾ [الصافات ] ويزيد ما شاء، ويدعو بما حضره، ويوفق له بفضل الله
ثم يأتي أسطوانة أبي لبابة التي ربط بها نفسه حتى تاب الله عليه وهي بين القبر والمنبر، ويصلــي مـا شاء نفلاً، ويتوب إلى الله، ويدعو بما شاء، ويأتي الروضة فيصلي ما شاء، ويدعو بما أحب، ويكـثـر مـن التسبيح، والتهليل، والثناء، والاستغفار. ثم يأتي المنبر فيضع يده على الرمانة التي كانت بـه تبـركـاً بأثر رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ، ومكان يده الشريفة إذا خطب، لينال بركته ، ويصلي عليه، ويسأل اللـه مـا شـاء، ثم يأتي الأسطوانة الحنانة، وهي التي فيها بقية الجذع، الذي حنَّ إلى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ، حـين تـركـه وخطب على المنبر، حتى نزل فاحتضنه فسكن، ويتبرك بما بقي من الآثار النبوية...
(۱) أي: رفيقيه في مدفنه.
(۲) عن ابن عباس رضي الله عنه قال: غزا رسول الله [ غزوة تبوك ] فتخلف عنه عشرة أنفس منهم أبو لبابة، ثم أن أبا لبابة ورجلين معه تفكروا وندموا وأيقنوا بالهلاك، وقالوا نحن في الظلال والطمأنينة مع النساء ورسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم والمؤمنون معه في الجهاد، والله لنوثقن أنفسنا بالسواري فلا نطلقها حتى يكون رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم هو الذي يطلقها، فربط أبو لبابة نفسه بسارية وقال: والله لا أحل نفسي منها ولا أذوق طعاماً ولا شراباً حتى يتوب الله علي أو أموت فمكث سبعة أيام لا يذوق طعاماً ولا شراباً حتى ذهب سمعه فما يكاد يسمع وكاد أن يذهب بصره، وكانت ابنته تحله إذا حضرت الصلاة أو أراد أن يذهب لحاجة ، وإذا فرغ أعادته إلى الرباط حتى خر مغشاً عليه، ثم تاب الله عليه فقيل له: قد تاب الله عليك يا أبا لبابة، فقال: والله لا أحـــل نفسي حتى يكون رسول وهو الذي يحلني، فجاء رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فحله بيده تفسير الطبري (۲۲۱/۹) بتصرف.
By entering in front of you, and we have come from distant lands and far places, traversing plains and rugged terrain with the intention of visiting you, to gain your intercession, and to look at your monuments and landmarks, and to fulfill some of your rights, and to seek intercession through you to our Lord. For indeed sins have broken our backs, and burdens have weighed down our shoulders, and you are the intercessor whose intercession is accepted, promised the great intercession, the praised station, and the means. Allah Almighty said: 'And if, when they wronged themselves, they had come to you and asked forgiveness of Allah and the Messenger had asked forgiveness for them, they would have found Allah All-Forgiving, Most Merciful' [an-Nisa 64]. And we have come wronging ourselves, seeking forgiveness for our sins, so intercede for us to your Lord, and ask Him to cause us to die upon your Sunnah, and to gather us in your company, and to bring us to your Basin, and to give us drink from your cup, not disgraced nor regretful. Intercession, intercession, intercession, O Messenger of Allah—he says it three times. Our Lord, forgive us and our brothers who preceded us in faith, and do not place in our hearts any rancor toward those who believe. Our Lord, indeed You are All-Kind, Most Merciful. And you convey the greeting of one who charged you with it, saying: Peace be upon you, O Messenger of Allah, from so-and-so son of so-and-so, seeking intercession through you to your Lord, so intercede for him and for the Muslims. Then you send salutations upon him and supplicate as you wish at his noble face, facing away from the qibla. Then you move about a cubit until you align with the head of as-Siddiq Abu Bakr—may Allah be pleased with him—and say: Peace be upon you, O Caliph of the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace. Peace be upon you, O Companion of the Messenger of Allah, his intimate in the cave, his companion in journeys, and his keeper of secrets. May Allah reward you with the best reward He has given an imam for the nation of his Prophet. Indeed, you succeeded him in the best succession, followed his path and his way in the best manner, fought the people of apostasy and innovation, strengthened Islam, and established its pillars. So you were the best imam, maintained family ties, and continued standing for truth, supporting the religion and its people until certainty came to you. Ask Allah, glorified be He, for us to continue loving you, and to be gathered with your party, and to accept our visit. Peace be upon you and the mercy of Allah and His blessings. Then you move similarly until you align with the head of the Commander of the Faithful, Umar ibn al-Khattab—may Allah be pleased with him—and say: Peace be upon you, O Commander of the Faithful, peace be upon you, O manifestor of Islam, peace be upon you, O breaker of idols. May Allah reward you with the best reward. Indeed, you supported Islam and the Muslims, conquered most of the lands after the Master of the Messengers, cared for orphans, maintained family ties, and Islam was strengthened through you. You were for the Muslims a pleasing imam and a rightly guided guide. You united them, helped their poor, and mended their brokenness. Peace be upon you and the mercy of Allah and His blessings. Then you go back about half a cubit and say: Peace be upon you both, O two companions of the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, his two friends, his two viziers, his two advisors, his two helpers in establishing the religion, and those who undertook the affairs of the Muslims after him. May Allah reward you both with the best reward. We have come to you seeking your mediation to the Messenger of Allah so that he may intercede for us and ask Allah, our Lord, to accept our efforts, to keep us alive upon his religion, to cause us to die upon it, and to gather us in his company. Then he supplicates for himself, his parents, the one who charged him with supplication, and all Muslims. Then he stands at the head of the Prophet, peace be upon him, as before and says: O Allah, You have said, and Your saying is truth: 'And if, when they wronged themselves, they had come to you and asked forgiveness of Allah and the Messenger had asked forgiveness for them, they would have found Allah All-Forgiving, Most Merciful.' [an-Nisa 64]. And we have come to You, hearing Your words, obeying Your command, seeking intercession through Your Prophet to You. O Allah, our Lord, forgive us and our fathers and mothers and our brothers who preceded us in faith, and do not place in our hearts any rancor toward those who believe. Our Lord, indeed You are All-Kind, Most Merciful. 'Our Lord, give us in this world [that which is] good and in the Hereafter [that which is] good and protect us from the punishment of the Fire' [al-Baqarah 201]. 'Exalted is your Lord, the Lord of might, above what they describe. And peace upon the messengers. And praise to Allah, Lord of the worlds' [as-Saffat 180-182]. He adds what he wishes and supplicates as occurs to him, and he is guided to it by the grace of Allah. Then he comes to the pillar of Abu Lubaba, to which he tied himself until Allah forgave him—it is between the grave and the pulpit—and prays as much supererogatory prayer as he wishes, repents to Allah, and supplicates as he wishes. He comes to the Rawdah and prays as much as he wishes and supplicates as he likes, and increases in glorification, declarations of His oneness, praise, and seeking forgiveness. Then he comes to the pulpit and places his hand on the pomegranate that was on it, seeking blessing from the trace of the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, and the place of his noble hand when he gave the sermon, to attain his blessing. He sends salutations upon him and asks Allah for whatever he wishes. Then he comes to the yearning pillar (al-ustuwanah al-hannanah), which contains the remnant of the trunk that yearned for the Prophet, peace be upon him, when he left it and gave the sermon from the pulpit, so he came down and embraced it, and it became still. He seeks blessing from what remains of the prophetic relics... (1) i.e., his two companions in his grave. (2) From Ibn Abbas, may Allah be pleased with him, who said: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ went on the expedition of Tabuk, and ten men, including Abu Lubaba, lagged behind. Then Abu Lubaba and two men with him thought, regretted, and were certain of destruction. They said: We are in the shade and comfort with women while the Messenger of Allah and the believers are with him in jihad. By Allah, we will tie ourselves to the pillars and not release ourselves until the Messenger of Allah himself releases us. So Abu Lubaba tied himself to a pillar and said: By Allah, I will not untie myself nor taste food or drink until Allah forgives me or I die. He remained seven days without tasting food or drink until his hearing was lost, he could barely hear, and his sight was almost gone. His daughter would untie him when it was time for prayer or when he needed to relieve himself, and when he finished, she would return him to the bond until he fell unconscious. Then Allah forgave him, and it was said: O Abu Lubaba, Allah has forgiven you. He said: By Allah, I will not untie myself until the Messenger of Allah unties me. So the Messenger of Allah came and untied him with his own hand. (Tafsir al-Tabari 9/221, adapted.)
Source pages p. 706

Commentary
This passage defines the recommended etiquettes (adab) for visiting the Prophet's Mosque in Madinah, specifically the ziyarah of the grave of the Prophet ﷺ and the graves of the first two caliphs, Abu Bakr and Umar (may Allah be pleased with them). The author describes a step-by-step procedure, beginning with facing the Prophet's grave and reciting a lengthy supplication that includes the verse from Surah an-Nisa (64), seeking his intercession, and asking for forgiveness. The visitor is to say 'Ash-shafa‘ah' three times and then convey greetings from anyone who requested it. After supplicating, one moves about a cubit to the right to stand opposite the head of Abu Bakr, reciting a specific greeting and praise. Then similarly to Umar. Then one steps back half a cubit to address both companions together.

After the graves, the visitor returns to the Prophet's head and recites another supplication ending with Quranic verses. Then one proceeds to the pillar of Abu Lubaba (between the grave and pulpit), where the companion Abu Lubaba tied himself until his repentance was accepted. Here one prays supererogatory prayers, repents, and supplicates. Then to the Rawdah (the area between the pulpit and the Prophet's house) for more prayer and dhikr. Then to the pulpit, placing one hand on the pomegranate-shaped knob (rummanah) where the Prophet's hand rested during sermons. Finally, to the 'yearning pillar' (ustuwanah hannanah) which contains a remnant of the palm trunk that used to weep when the Prophet stopped leaning on it. The passage ends with a historical footnote about Abu Lubaba's story.

This is a detailed example of the Hanafi recommended practice for visiting Madinah, emphasizing respect, the seeking of intercession (tawassul) through the Prophet, and blessing (tabarruk) from prophetic relics. The rulings are based on the practice of the salaf and not on explicit textual proofs, hence the argument type is 'none'. The authority weight is from later Hanafi texts (fatawa mutakhkhirin) as it expands on the basic ruling of visiting the grave, which is considered mustahabb (recommended) according to the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
زيارة (ziyarah): The act of visiting the Prophet's mosque and grave, and the graves of the righteous, as a recommended act of devotion.
الشفاعة (ash-shafa'ah): The intercession of the Prophet ﷺ on behalf of sinners; the visitor asks the Prophet to intercede for him before Allah.
ضجيع (daji'): One who lies in the grave nearby; here referring to Abu Bakr and Umar as companions of the Prophet in his burial place.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
After finishing the supplication at the Prophet's grave, where do you move to next?
A) The grave of Umar ibn al-Khattab
B) The grave of Abu Bakr al-Siddiq
C) The pulpit
D) The pillar of Abu Lubaba

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi recommendation for visiting the Prophet's grave includes specific etiquettes and supplications that reflect love and reverence, and it is a mustahabb act of devotion.
